Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Three Scenarios of Attribution in Agency Purchase
Explaining the three attribution scenarios and the consensus rule when dispute occurs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios of attribution in an agency purchase and apply the rule of payment as decisive when a dispute arises.

Core Idea
In an agency purchase, attribution to own property, principal's property, or absolute dirhams determines ownership, with payment resolving disputes and intention guiding when clear.

The Hanafi school has detailed rules for when an agent buys an unspecified item. The key is how the agent attributes the purchase: to his own money, the principal's money, or absolutely. Each scenario has its own ruling on ownership, and when there is a dispute after purchase, the payment of the price becomes the decisive factor. In this lesson, we'll work through these three scenarios and the consensus on payment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three attribution scenarios
Learn the three ways an agent can express the purchase: (1) 'I bought with my dirhams' – attribution to own property; (2) 'I bought with the principal's dirhams' – attribution to principal's property; (3) 'I bought for one hundred dirhams' – absolute dirhams, no owner specified.
The first scenario is only valid if the agent buys for himself; buying for another with own money would involve usurpation.
2
Determine the ruling for each scenario when intention is present
If the agent attributes to own property, the purchase is for himself. If he attributes to the principal's property, it is for the principal. For absolute dirhams, the agent's intention decides: if he intended for the principal, it is for the principal; if for himself, it is for himself.
The agent has dual authority in the absolute case because the principal authorized buying an unspecified slave.
3
Apply the rule of payment as decisive in disputes
When the agent and principal disagree about intention (agent says for himself, principal says for him), and no other evidence, the payment decides ownership: whoever's money was used to pay the price owns the item.
This is based on custom (urf): the one who pays is presumed to be the buyer, and to avoid usurpation.

موکل کے دراہم کا نصب کرنا لازم آتا ہے اور غصب کا حرام ہونا واضح ہے اور اگر عقد شراء اپنے مال کی طرف منسوب ہو اور شراء دوسرے کیلئے ہو یہ حرام نہیں ہوتا۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں غصب کا مرتکب ہونالازم نہیں آتا ہے۔
بہر حال مصنف ہدایہ نے حملاً لحاله على ما يحل له شرعاً سے دلیل شرع بیان کی ہے۔ اور او یفعلہ عادةً سے دلیل عرف کو بیان کیا ہے۔ دلیل شرع تو صرف پہلی صورت پر ہے اور دلیل عرف دونوں صورتوں پر ہے۔ (کفایہ ) تیسری صورت یہ ہے کہ وکیل نے عقد شراء کو د راہم مطلقہ کی طرف منسوب کیا ہے۔ مثلا یہ کہا کہ میں نے یہ غلام ایک سود را ہم کے عوض خریدا اور یہ نہیں کہا کہ اپنے ایک سود را ہم یا موکل کے ایک سو دراہم کے عوض خریدا۔ پس اس صورت میں اگر وکیل نے درا ہم مطلقہ سے مؤکل کیلئے خریدنے کی نیت کی تو یہ عقد شرا ، موکل کیلئے ہوگا اور اگر اپنے خریدنے کی نیت کی تو یہ عقد شراء خود وکیل کیلئے ہوگا۔ کیونکہ غیر یعین غلام خرید کرنے کی توکیل کی صورت میں وکیل کو دونوں اختیار ہوتے ہیں وہ اپنے لئے خرید کرنے کا بھی مجاز ہے اور مؤکل کیلئے بھی فرید کرنے کا مجاز ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا خرید کرتے وقت جس کی نیت کرے گا غلام اسی کا ہوگا۔ اور اگر دراہم مطلقہ کی صورت میں وکیل اور موکل کے درمیان اختلاف نہ گیا یعنی وکیل نے کہا کہ یہ غلام میں نے اپنے لئے خریدا ہے اور متوکل نے کہا کہ نہیں بلکہ میرے لئے خریدا ہے۔ تو س صورت میں بالاتفاق ادائیگی شمن کو فیصل قرار دیا جائے گا یعنی اگر شمن وکیل کے مال سے ادا کیا گیا ہے تو یہ خریداری وکیل کیلئے ہوگی ۔ دور وکیل غلام کا مالک ہوگا۔ اور اگر موکل کے مال سے ثمن ادا کیا گیا ہے تو یہ خریداری موکل کیلئے ہوگی اور موکل اس غلام کا مالک ہوگا۔
یونکہ یمن کا ادا کرنا اس بات پر ظاہری دلیل ہے کہ وکیل کے حال کو اس پر محمول کیا جائے۔ جو اس کیلئے شرعاً حلال ہے یا اس کو عادة جاتا ہے۔ یعنی اگر وکیل نے اپنے مال سے ثمن ادا کیا ہے تو یہ اپنے مال سے ثمن ادا کرنا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ یہ خریداری خود وکیل کیلئے ہے۔ اسلئے کہ عرفا اور عادہ ایسا نہیں کیا جاتا ہے کہ مؤکل اپنے مال سے شمن ادا کرے اور خریداری دوسرے کیلئے ہو اور گر مؤکل کے مال سے ثمن ادا کیا ہے تو یہ اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ یہ خریداری بھی مؤکل کیلئے ہے۔ اسلے کہ شرعانیہ بات حرام ہے کہ آدمی خریداری اپنے لئے کرے اور شمن دوسرے کے مال سے ادا کرے جیسا کہ پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ اس صورت میں وکیل کا غاصب ہونا لازم آئے گا اور اگر وکیل اور مؤکل اس بات پر متفق ہو گئے کہ غلام کی خریداری کرتے وقت وکیل کی کوئی نیت نہیں تھی۔ تو اس صورت میں امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد کے: رمیان اختلاف ہے۔ چنانچہ امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ یہ خریداری، عاقد یعنی وکیل کیلئے ہے کیونکہ اصل پہنی ہے کہ آدمی اپنے لئے کام کرتا ہے ہوائے اس کے کہ وہ اپنا کام کسی دوسرے کیلئے اس کے مال کی طرف نسبت کر کے یا اس کی نیت کر کے قرار دے دے۔ مگر چونکہ یہاں
رض کیا گیا ہے کہ وکیل نے اپنی اس خریداری کو دوسرے کیلئے قرار نہیں دیا ہے اسلئے یہ خریداری عاقد یعنی وکیل ہی کیلئے ہوگی ۔ اور امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ اس صورت میں بھی ادائیگی شمن کو فیصل بنایا جائے گا۔ یعنی شمن جس کے مال سے ادا ہو گا خریداری اسی کیلئے ہوگی اور وہی غلام کا مالک ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وکیل نے جو خریداری کی ہے وہ نیت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے مطلق ہے اور دونوں صورتوں کا حتمال رکھتی ہے۔ یعنی یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ خریداری موکل کیلئے ہو اور یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ خریداری خود وکیل کیلئے ہو۔ پس دونوں کا احتمال کھنے کی وجہ سے یہ خریداری موقوف رہے گی۔ یعنی نہ وکیل کیلئے ہوگی اور نہ موکل کیلئے ہوگی۔ بلکہ یہ دیکھا جائے گا کہ یمن کس کے مال سے داء کیا گیا ہوگا۔ محتمل خریداری اس کیلئے ہوگی۔ وسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب وکیل اور مؤکل نے اس بات پر اتفاق کر لیا کہ خرید کرتے وقت وکیل کی کوئی نیت نہیں تھی تو اس میں یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ وکیل نے موکل کیلئے نیت کی مگر بھول گیا ہو۔ اور جب یہ بھی احتمال ہے تو خریداری یقینی طور سے عاقد یعنی وکیل کیلئے کیسے ہو سکتی ہے اور جو ہم نے ابو یوسف کی طرف سے کہا ہے اس میں وکیل کا حال صلاح پر محمول ہے اس طور پر کہ اگر شمن موکل کے مال سے اداء کیا گیا ہو اور خریداری وکیل کیلئے ہو ۔ جیسا کہ امام محمد نے کہا ہے تو وکیل غاصب وگا اور اگر خریداری بھی مؤکل کیلئے ہو تو وکیل غاصب نہ ہو گا۔ بہر حال ادائیگی شمن کو فیصل قرار دینے کی صورت میں چونکہ وکیل کا حال ح پر محمول ہوتا ہے اسلئے خریدتے وقت نیت موجود نہ ہونے پر اتفاق کر لینے کی صورت میں ادا ئیگی شمن کو فیصل قرار دینا مناسب ہوگا۔
صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ اناج کی بیع سلم کے سلسلہ میں وکیل کرنے کی بھی یہی صورتیں میں جلو پر مذکور ہیں ۔ کیونکہ بیع سلم میں اناج بھی کی غیر معین ہوتا ہے۔ پس جب وکیل نے بیع سلم کی تو دیکھا جائے گا کہ اس نے عقد کو اپنے مال کی طرف منسوب کیا ہے یا موکل کے مال کی طرف یا مطلق دراہم کی طرف پھر مطلق دراہم کی صورت میں اس کی کچھ نیت ہے یا نہیں۔ اگر نیت ہے تو اپنے واسطے ہے یا موکل کے واسطے ہے۔ یا دونوں نے نیت میں اختلاف کیا ہے۔ اور اگر وکیل اور مؤکل کا اتفاق ہے کہ نیت نہیں تھی تو امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد کے درمیان اختلاف ہے۔
Book of Agency. For the principal, it is necessary to specify his dirhams, and usurpation is clearly prohibited. If the contract of purchase is attributed to one's own property and the purchase is for another, it is not prohibited because in that case usurpation does not necessarily occur. Nevertheless, the author of Hidayah has mentioned the shariah proof by interpreting the situation in a way that is lawful for him shariah-wise, and the custom proof by what he usually does. The shariah proof applies only to the first scenario, and the custom proof applies to both scenarios. (Kifayah) The third scenario is that the agent attributed the contract of purchase to absolute dirhams, for example, he said, 'I bought this slave for one hundred dirhams' and did not say 'for my one hundred dirhams' or 'for the principal's one hundred dirhams.' In this case, if the agent intended to buy for the principal with the absolute dirhams, the contract is for the principal; and if he intended to buy for himself, the contract is for himself. Because in the case of authorization to buy an unspecified slave, the agent has both options: he is permitted to buy for himself and for the principal. So at the time of purchase, whichever he intends, the slave belongs to that person. If there is a dispute between the agent and the principal in the case of absolute dirhams—the agent says he bought for himself and the principal says he bought for the principal—then in that case, by consensus, the payment of the price is made decisive. That is, if the price was paid from the agent's own property, the purchase is for the agent; if from the principal's property, the purchase is for the principal. Because paying the price is an apparent evidence that the agent's state is interpreted accordingly, either as lawful for him shariah-wise or as customary. If the agent paid from his own property, that indicates the purchase is for himself; customarily, a person does not pay from the principal's property for his own purchase. If the price was paid from the principal's property, that indicates the purchase is for the principal; it is shariah-wise prohibited for a person to buy for himself and pay from another's property, because that would make the agent a usurper. If the agent and principal agree that at the time of purchase the agent had no intention, then there is a disagreement between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad. Imam Muhammad said the purchase is for the agent (the contractor) because the basic principle is that a person acts for himself unless he attributes his action to another by relating it to his property or intending it for him. Since here it is established that the agent did not attribute his purchase to another, the purchase is for the contractor. Imam Abu Yusuf said that in this case also the payment is made decisive: the one from whose property the price was paid, the purchase is for him. He is the owner. Because the agent's purchase, due to absence of intention, is an absolute transaction that could be for either party. Therefore, it remains suspended until the payment determines it. Another reason: when they agree there was no intention, it is possible that the agent intended for the principal but forgot. So how can it be certain for the agent? And what we said from Abu Yusuf interprets the agent's state as one of integrity: if the payment was from the principal's property and the purchase was for the agent, the agent would be a usurper; but if for the principal, he is not a usurper. So making payment decisive is appropriate. The author of Hidayah said that the same scenarios apply in the case of agency for salam sale of grain because in salam the grain is also unspecified. So when the agent conducts a salam, it will be seen whether he attributed the contract to his own property, the principal's property, or absolute dirhams. Then in the case of absolute dirhams, whether he had some intention or not, and if intention, whether for himself or the principal, or they disputed the intention. If they agree there was no intention, then the disagreement between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad applies.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses the rules of attribution when an agent buys an unspecified item (here a slave) for a specified price. The passage first outlines three scenarios: (1) the agent attributes the purchase to his own property, which is permissible only if he buys for himself; buying for another using his own property is forbidden as it involves usurpation. (2) The agent attributes the purchase to the principal's property, which is permissible only if he buys for the principal. (3) The agent attributes the purchase to absolute dirhams (i.e., he does not specify whose money is used). In this third scenario, the decisive factor is the agent's intention at the time of purchase. If he intended for the principal, the purchase is for the principal; if for himself, it is for himself. If a dispute arises and both claim different intentions, the payment of the price (which actual money was used) is taken as decisive evidence. This is based on custom (urf) and shariah prohibition of usurpation. If both parties agree that the agent had no intention at the time, then there is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Imam Muhammad holds that the purchase is for the agent because the basic principle is that a person acts for himself. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that payment is still decisive. The passage favors Abu Yusuf's view because it preserves the agent from being a usurper and aligns with the presumption of integrity. The same rule applies to salam contracts where the commodity is unspecified.

Key Terms
دراہم مطلقہ (daraahim mutlaqah): Absolute dirhams mentioned without specification of whose property they belong to.
ثمن (thaman): The price paid for the purchased item.
موکل (muwakkil): The principal who appoints an agent.
وکیل (wakeel): The agent appointed to perform a task.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the third scenario (absolute dirhams) with a dispute about intention, what is the consensus ruling on how ownership is determined?
A) Ownership is determined by the agent's intention at the time of purchase.
B) Ownership is determined by the payment: the one who paid owns the item.
C) Ownership is determined by the principal's statement.
D) The purchase is invalid until the dispute is resolved.

Key Takeaway
In agency purchase with absolute dirhams, intention decides when known; when disputed, payment decides by consensus.

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute When Intention is Absent
Explaining the ikhtilaf between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad when intention is absent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the disagreement between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding ownership when an agent buys with absolute dirhams and both agree there was no intention, and identify the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
When intention is absent, Imam Muhammad says the agent owns; Imam Abu Yusuf says payment decides; the latter is preferred to avoid usurpation.

After establishing the three scenarios and the rule for disputes, the text addresses a special case: the agent and principal agree that at the time of purchase the agent had no specific intention. Here, the Hanafi school splits: Imam Muhammad applies the basic principle of self-attribution, while Imam Abu Yusuf argues that payment must decide. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your grasp of how Hanafi jurists balance principles (usul) against practical consequences (maqasid).

Guided Path
1
State the agreed fact: no intention at purchase
Both agent and principal agree that when the agent bought the slave with absolute dirhams, he had no intention of buying for himself or for the principal. This is different from a dispute where each claims a different intention.
This agreement removes the possibility of lying or forgetfulness as a factor.
2
Understand Imam Muhammad's position
Imam Muhammad says the purchase is for the agent because 'the basic principle is that a person acts for himself unless he attributes the act to another.' Since the agent did not attribute the purchase to the principal, it must be for himself.
This is the default rule in Hanafi usul: al-aslu idafat al-fi'l ila al-fa'il.
3
Understand Imam Abu Yusuf's position
Imam Abu Yusuf says payment decides, just like in the dispute case. The purchase is absolute (mutlaq) and could be for either. Since no intention existed, the transaction is suspended until payment determines it. Also, if payment is from the principal's money and the purchase is for the agent, the agent would be a usurper, which is avoided by making the purchase for the payer.
Abu Yusuf also argues that the agent might have intended for the principal but forgot; you cannot rule out that possibility, so the purchase cannot be definitely for the agent.
4
Identify the tarjih (preferred view)
The text (Ashraf al-Hidayah) supports Imam Abu Yusuf's view, stating that it is more appropriate (munasib) because it interprets the agent's state as one of integrity (salāh) and avoids making him a usurper.
The mufta bihi is that payment is decisive even when intention is absent.

موکل کے دراہم کا نصب کرنا لازم آتا ہے اور غصب کا حرام ہونا واضح ہے اور اگر عقد شراء اپنے مال کی طرف منسوب ہو اور شراء دوسرے کیلئے ہو یہ حرام نہیں ہوتا۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں غصب کا مرتکب ہونالازم نہیں آتا ہے۔
بہر حال مصنف ہدایہ نے حملاً لحاله على ما يحل له شرعاً سے دلیل شرع بیان کی ہے۔ اور او یفعلہ عادةً سے دلیل عرف کو بیان کیا ہے۔ دلیل شرع تو صرف پہلی صورت پر ہے اور دلیل عرف دونوں صورتوں پر ہے۔ (کفایہ ) تیسری صورت یہ ہے کہ وکیل نے عقد شراء کو د راہم مطلقہ کی طرف منسوب کیا ہے۔ مثلا یہ کہا کہ میں نے یہ غلام ایک سود را ہم کے عوض خریدا اور یہ نہیں کہا کہ اپنے ایک سود را ہم یا موکل کے ایک سو دراہم کے عوض خریدا۔ پس اس صورت میں اگر وکیل نے درا ہم مطلقہ سے مؤکل کیلئے خریدنے کی نیت کی تو یہ عقد شرا ، موکل کیلئے ہوگا اور اگر اپنے خریدنے کی نیت کی تو یہ عقد شراء خود وکیل کیلئے ہوگا۔ کیونکہ غیر یعین غلام خرید کرنے کی توکیل کی صورت میں وکیل کو دونوں اختیار ہوتے ہیں وہ اپنے لئے خرید کرنے کا بھی مجاز ہے اور مؤکل کیلئے بھی فرید کرنے کا مجاز ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا خرید کرتے وقت جس کی نیت کرے گا غلام اسی کا ہوگا۔ اور اگر دراہم مطلقہ کی صورت میں وکیل اور موکل کے درمیان اختلاف نہ گیا یعنی وکیل نے کہا کہ یہ غلام میں نے اپنے لئے خریدا ہے اور متوکل نے کہا کہ نہیں بلکہ میرے لئے خریدا ہے۔ تو س صورت میں بالاتفاق ادائیگی شمن کو فیصل قرار دیا جائے گا یعنی اگر شمن وکیل کے مال سے ادا کیا گیا ہے تو یہ خریداری وکیل کیلئے ہوگی ۔ دور وکیل غلام کا مالک ہوگا۔ اور اگر موکل کے مال سے ثمن ادا کیا گیا ہے تو یہ خریداری موکل کیلئے ہوگی اور موکل اس غلام کا مالک ہوگا۔
یونکہ یمن کا ادا کرنا اس بات پر ظاہری دلیل ہے کہ وکیل کے حال کو اس پر محمول کیا جائے۔ جو اس کیلئے شرعاً حلال ہے یا اس کو عادة جاتا ہے۔ یعنی اگر وکیل نے اپنے مال سے ثمن ادا کیا ہے تو یہ اپنے مال سے ثمن ادا کرنا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ یہ خریداری خود وکیل کیلئے ہے۔ اسلئے کہ عرفا اور عادہ ایسا نہیں کیا جاتا ہے کہ مؤکل اپنے مال سے شمن ادا کرے اور خریداری دوسرے کیلئے ہو اور گر مؤکل کے مال سے ثمن ادا کیا ہے تو یہ اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ یہ خریداری بھی مؤکل کیلئے ہے۔ اسلے کہ شرعانیہ بات حرام ہے کہ آدمی خریداری اپنے لئے کرے اور شمن دوسرے کے مال سے ادا کرے جیسا کہ پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ اس صورت میں وکیل کا غاصب ہونا لازم آئے گا اور اگر وکیل اور مؤکل اس بات پر متفق ہو گئے کہ غلام کی خریداری کرتے وقت وکیل کی کوئی نیت نہیں تھی۔ تو اس صورت میں امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد کے: رمیان اختلاف ہے۔ چنانچہ امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ یہ خریداری، عاقد یعنی وکیل کیلئے ہے کیونکہ اصل پہنی ہے کہ آدمی اپنے لئے کام کرتا ہے ہوائے اس کے کہ وہ اپنا کام کسی دوسرے کیلئے اس کے مال کی طرف نسبت کر کے یا اس کی نیت کر کے قرار دے دے۔ مگر چونکہ یہاں
رض کیا گیا ہے کہ وکیل نے اپنی اس خریداری کو دوسرے کیلئے قرار نہیں دیا ہے اسلئے یہ خریداری عاقد یعنی وکیل ہی کیلئے ہوگی ۔ اور امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ اس صورت میں بھی ادائیگی شمن کو فیصل بنایا جائے گا۔ یعنی شمن جس کے مال سے ادا ہو گا خریداری اسی کیلئے ہوگی اور وہی غلام کا مالک ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وکیل نے جو خریداری کی ہے وہ نیت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے مطلق ہے اور دونوں صورتوں کا حتمال رکھتی ہے۔ یعنی یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ خریداری موکل کیلئے ہو اور یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ خریداری خود وکیل کیلئے ہو۔ پس دونوں کا احتمال کھنے کی وجہ سے یہ خریداری موقوف رہے گی۔ یعنی نہ وکیل کیلئے ہوگی اور نہ موکل کیلئے ہوگی۔ بلکہ یہ دیکھا جائے گا کہ یمن کس کے مال سے داء کیا گیا ہوگا۔ محتمل خریداری اس کیلئے ہوگی۔ وسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب وکیل اور مؤکل نے اس بات پر اتفاق کر لیا کہ خرید کرتے وقت وکیل کی کوئی نیت نہیں تھی تو اس میں یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ وکیل نے موکل کیلئے نیت کی مگر بھول گیا ہو۔ اور جب یہ بھی احتمال ہے تو خریداری یقینی طور سے عاقد یعنی وکیل کیلئے کیسے ہو سکتی ہے اور جو ہم نے ابو یوسف کی طرف سے کہا ہے اس میں وکیل کا حال صلاح پر محمول ہے اس طور پر کہ اگر شمن موکل کے مال سے اداء کیا گیا ہو اور خریداری وکیل کیلئے ہو ۔ جیسا کہ امام محمد نے کہا ہے تو وکیل غاصب وگا اور اگر خریداری بھی مؤکل کیلئے ہو تو وکیل غاصب نہ ہو گا۔ بہر حال ادائیگی شمن کو فیصل قرار دینے کی صورت میں چونکہ وکیل کا حال ح پر محمول ہوتا ہے اسلئے خریدتے وقت نیت موجود نہ ہونے پر اتفاق کر لینے کی صورت میں ادا ئیگی شمن کو فیصل قرار دینا مناسب ہوگا۔
صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ اناج کی بیع سلم کے سلسلہ میں وکیل کرنے کی بھی یہی صورتیں میں جلو پر مذکور ہیں ۔ کیونکہ بیع سلم میں اناج بھی کی غیر معین ہوتا ہے۔ پس جب وکیل نے بیع سلم کی تو دیکھا جائے گا کہ اس نے عقد کو اپنے مال کی طرف منسوب کیا ہے یا موکل کے مال کی طرف یا مطلق دراہم کی طرف پھر مطلق دراہم کی صورت میں اس کی کچھ نیت ہے یا نہیں۔ اگر نیت ہے تو اپنے واسطے ہے یا موکل کے واسطے ہے۔ یا دونوں نے نیت میں اختلاف کیا ہے۔ اور اگر وکیل اور مؤکل کا اتفاق ہے کہ نیت نہیں تھی تو امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد کے درمیان اختلاف ہے۔
Book of Agency. For the principal, it is necessary to specify his dirhams, and usurpation is clearly prohibited. If the contract of purchase is attributed to one's own property and the purchase is for another, it is not prohibited because in that case usurpation does not necessarily occur. Nevertheless, the author of Hidayah has mentioned the shariah proof by interpreting the situation in a way that is lawful for him shariah-wise, and the custom proof by what he usually does. The shariah proof applies only to the first scenario, and the custom proof applies to both scenarios. (Kifayah) The third scenario is that the agent attributed the contract of purchase to absolute dirhams, for example, he said, 'I bought this slave for one hundred dirhams' and did not say 'for my one hundred dirhams' or 'for the principal's one hundred dirhams.' In this case, if the agent intended to buy for the principal with the absolute dirhams, the contract is for the principal; and if he intended to buy for himself, the contract is for himself. Because in the case of authorization to buy an unspecified slave, the agent has both options: he is permitted to buy for himself and for the principal. So at the time of purchase, whichever he intends, the slave belongs to that person. If there is a dispute between the agent and the principal in the case of absolute dirhams—the agent says he bought for himself and the principal says he bought for the principal—then in that case, by consensus, the payment of the price is made decisive. That is, if the price was paid from the agent's own property, the purchase is for the agent; if from the principal's property, the purchase is for the principal. Because paying the price is an apparent evidence that the agent's state is interpreted accordingly, either as lawful for him shariah-wise or as customary. If the agent paid from his own property, that indicates the purchase is for himself; customarily, a person does not pay from the principal's property for his own purchase. If the price was paid from the principal's property, that indicates the purchase is for the principal; it is shariah-wise prohibited for a person to buy for himself and pay from another's property, because that would make the agent a usurper. If the agent and principal agree that at the time of purchase the agent had no intention, then there is a disagreement between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad. Imam Muhammad said the purchase is for the agent (the contractor) because the basic principle is that a person acts for himself unless he attributes his action to another by relating it to his property or intending it for him. Since here it is established that the agent did not attribute his purchase to another, the purchase is for the contractor. Imam Abu Yusuf said that in this case also the payment is made decisive: the one from whose property the price was paid, the purchase is for him. He is the owner. Because the agent's purchase, due to absence of intention, is an absolute transaction that could be for either party. Therefore, it remains suspended until the payment determines it. Another reason: when they agree there was no intention, it is possible that the agent intended for the principal but forgot. So how can it be certain for the agent? And what we said from Abu Yusuf interprets the agent's state as one of integrity: if the payment was from the principal's property and the purchase was for the agent, the agent would be a usurper; but if for the principal, he is not a usurper. So making payment decisive is appropriate. The author of Hidayah said that the same scenarios apply in the case of agency for salam sale of grain because in salam the grain is also unspecified. So when the agent conducts a salam, it will be seen whether he attributed the contract to his own property, the principal's property, or absolute dirhams. Then in the case of absolute dirhams, whether he had some intention or not, and if intention, whether for himself or the principal, or they disputed the intention. If they agree there was no intention, then the disagreement between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad applies.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses the rules of attribution when an agent buys an unspecified item (here a slave) for a specified price. The passage first outlines three scenarios: (1) the agent attributes the purchase to his own property, which is permissible only if he buys for himself; buying for another using his own property is forbidden as it involves usurpation. (2) The agent attributes the purchase to the principal's property, which is permissible only if he buys for the principal. (3) The agent attributes the purchase to absolute dirhams (i.e., he does not specify whose money is used). In this third scenario, the decisive factor is the agent's intention at the time of purchase. If he intended for the principal, the purchase is for the principal; if for himself, it is for himself. If a dispute arises and both claim different intentions, the payment of the price (which actual money was used) is taken as decisive evidence. This is based on custom (urf) and shariah prohibition of usurpation. If both parties agree that the agent had no intention at the time, then there is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Imam Muhammad holds that the purchase is for the agent because the basic principle is that a person acts for himself. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that payment is still decisive. The passage favors Abu Yusuf's view because it preserves the agent from being a usurper and aligns with the presumption of integrity. The same rule applies to salam contracts where the commodity is unspecified.

Key Terms
اصل (asl): Basic principle that a person's actions are attributed to himself.
مطلق (mutlaq): Absolute, unspecified; used here for a purchase that does not specify for whom it is made.
موقوف (mawquf): Suspended; the transaction's effect is pending until a clarifying factor (like payment) appears.
غصب (ghasb): Usurpation; taking someone else's property without right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When agent and principal agree that the agent had no intention at purchase, what is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) ruling according to Ashraf al-Hidayah?
A) The purchase is for the agent because the basic principle applies.
B) The purchase is for the principal because he authorized the purchase.
C) Payment decides: the one who paid the price owns the item.
D) The purchase is invalid because intention is required.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school resolves the ambiguity of an intention-free purchase by making payment the decisive factor, avoiding usurpation.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
advanced
15 min
Dispute on Agent's Purchase: Whose Statement is Accepted?
Intra-Hanafi dispute with qiyas analogy and textual criticism

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whose statement is accepted when the principal and agent dispute the purchase of a slave, and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the living slave case.

Core Idea
When the price is unpaid, the principal's statement prevails if the agent cannot reperform the contract.

This lesson examines a detailed legal scenario from the Book of Agency (Kitab al-Wakalah) in al-Hidayah. An agent claims he bought a slave for his principal, but the slave died before delivery. The principal denies the purchase was for him, and the price has not been paid. The text explores whose statement is accepted—the principal's or the agent's—and extends the analysis to situations where the slave is alive, revealing an important intra-Hanafi difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two variables
The ruling depends on whether the price has been paid to the agent and whether the slave is alive or dead. List these four possible scenarios.
These are: (1) price unpaid, slave dead; (2) price unpaid, slave alive; (3) price paid, slave dead; (4) price paid, slave alive.
2
Analyze the dead slave, unpaid price case
Work through the text's reasoning: the agent claims the slave was bought for the principal but died. Because the slave is dead, the agent cannot redo the purchase contract. This makes his claim unverifiable, so the principal (the denier) is favored. Apply the qiyas with the husband claiming raj'ah after 'idda.
The analogy: a husband's claim of taking back his wife is not accepted after the 'idda because he cannot perform raj'ah anew.
3
Analyze the living slave, unpaid price case
Here the Sahibayn differ from Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn argue that because the slave is alive, the agent can rescind and buy anew for the principal, so he is not suspect and his statement is accepted. Abu Hanifa counters that even with the ability to redo, there remains a suspicion (tuhma) that the agent originally bought for himself and now seeks to pass a loss to the principal, so the principal's statement prevails.
This is the core intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. Understand each proof and the response.
4
Analyze the case where price is paid
When the price has been paid, the agent is a trustee (amin). Both the principal and the agent agree the agent received the money. The agent claims he fulfilled his duty by buying the slave for the principal (but it died). As a trustee, his statement about discharging his trust is accepted by consensus.
This also covers the living slave case: the agent's statement is accepted because he is a trustee seeking to clear himself.

قول معتبر ہے کیونکہ یہ تہمت کا مقام ہے بایں طور کہ اس کو اپنے لئے خریدا ہو پھر جب دیکھا کہ یہ گھاٹے کا معاملہ ہے تو اس کو موکل کے ذمہ ڈال دیا۔ برخلاف اس قول کے جب شمن دے دیا گیا ہو۔ کیونکہ اس میں وکیل امین ہے۔ لہذا اس کی طبیعت میں اس کا قول قبول ہوگا۔ اور یہاں وکیل کے قبضہ میں شمن نہیں ہے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر ایک شخص نے دوسرے شخص کو ایک ہزار روپیہ کے عوض ایک غلام خریدنے کا وکیل کیا ۔ وکیل نے کہا کہ میں نے وہ غلام خریدا تھا مگر میرے پاس مر گیا اور مؤکل نے کہا کہ ایسا نہیں ہے بلکہ وہ غلام تو نے اپنے واسطے خریدا تھا اور موکل نے ابھی تک وکیل کو ایک ہزار روپیہ نہیں دیا ہے تو اس صورت میں موکل کا قول معتبر ہو گا ۔ اور یہ خریداری وکیل کیلئے ہوگی نہ کہ موکل کیلئے یہی ایک روایت امام شافعی اور امام احمد کی ہے اور اگر مؤکل ، وکیل کو ایک ہزار روپیہ دے چکا ہے اور پھر یہ اختلاف ہوا ہے تو بالا تفاق وکیل کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ . ان دونوں صورتوں میں وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ پہلی صورت میں یعنی جس صورت میں مؤکل نے وکیل کوشن نہیں دیا ہے اس صورت میں وکیل نے ایسی چیز کی خبر دی ہے جس کے سبب وہ از سر نو موجود کرنا چاہے تو موجود نہیں کر سکتا ہے۔ تفصیل اس کی یہ ہے کہ وکیل کا یہ کہنا کہ میں نے آپ کے حکم کے مطابق غلام خرید لیا تھا مگر وہ غلام میرے پاس مرگیا ہے تو اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ وکیل ، موکل سے اس مردہ غلام کا شمن لینا چاہتا ہے اور موکل سے مشن لینے کا سبب عقد ہے۔ حالانکہ وکیل فی الحال اس غلام کے عقد پر قادر نہیں ہے کیونکہ جس غلام میں کلام ہے وہ غلام مردہ ہے اور مردہ غلام مکمل عقد نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا یہ وکیل اس مردہ غلام کے عقد شراء پر قادر نہیں ہے۔ اور جو شخص فی الحال کسی چیز کے موجود کرنے پر قادر نہ ہو اس چیز کے سلسلہ میں اس کا قول معتبر نہیں ہوتا۔ لہذا یہ وکیل کا قول کہ میں نے یہ غلام مؤکل کیلئے خریدا تھا اور یہ میرے پاس مرگیا ہے تو بھی معتبر نہ ہوگا۔ جیسے اگر کسی نے اپنی بیوی کو طلاق رجعی دی اور پھر یہ کہا کہ میں نے رجوع کر لیا تھا اور عورت نے کہا کہ تو نے رجوع نہیں کیا ہے تو اس صورت میں اگر عورت کی عدت باقی ہے تو شوہر کا قول معتبر ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں شوہر از سر نور جعت کرنے پر قادر ہے اور اگر عدت گزرنے کے بعد یہ اختلاف ہوا تو شوہر کا قول معتبر نہیں ہوتا ۔ کیونکہ شوہر از سر نو فی الحال رجعت کرنے پر قادر نہیں ہے، پس یہاں بھی چونکہ وکیل غلام کے مرجانے کی وجہ سے فی الحال از سر نو عقد کرنے پر قادر نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے وکیل کا قول معتبر نہ ہو گا۔ اسی دلیل کو یوں بھی کہا جا سکتا ہے کہ وکیل کا موکل سے شمن کا مطالبہ نہ کرنا اس بات کے ساتھ خاص ہے کہ وکیل نے غلام مؤکل کیلئے خریدا ہے یعنی وکیل اس کا مدعی ہے کہ میں نے یہ غلام مؤکل کیلئے خریدا ہے اور خود موکل اس کا منکر ہے اور وکیل کے پاس اپنا دعوی ثابت کرنے کیلئے بعینہ بھی موجود نہ ہونے کی صورت میں چونکہ منکر کا قول معتبر ہوتا ہے اسلئے یہاں موکل کا قول معتبر ہو گا۔
علامہ بدرالدین عینی نے اس دلیل کی عبارت پر ایک لفظی اعتراض کر کے اس کا جواب دیا ہے۔
اعتراض یہ ہے کہ عبارت میں استیناف کی ضمیر سے سبب رجوع یعنی عقد شراء مراد ہے جیسا کہ تقریر دلیل میں اس کو ملحوظ رکھا گیا ہے۔ پس جب عقد مراد ہے تو صاحب ہدا نے استیناف کی نمیر کا مرجع ظاہر کرتے ہوئے وهو الرجوع بالثمن کیوں فرمایا ہے وهو العقد کیوں نہیں فرمایا ؟

جواب ... اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ از سر نو عقد شراء کرنے سے وکیل کا مقصود، موکل سے ثمین لینا ہے نہ کہ مؤکل کیلئے عقد شراء کرنا۔ الہندا صاحب ہدایہ نے واسطہ یعنی عقد کو چھوڑ کر جو مقصود تھا اس کی صراحت فرمادی ہے۔ پس یہ سبب ( رجوع با شمن علی المؤکل ) کو ذکر کر کے سبب ( عقد شراء ) مراد لینے کی قبیل سے ہوگا۔ اور یہ جائز ہے اور دوسری صورت میں یعنی جس صورت میں مؤکل ، وکیل کو شمن ادا کر چکا ہے اس صورت میں وکیل امین ہے اور وہ یہ کہہ کر کہ میں نے آپ کیلئے غلام خریدا تھا مگر وہ میرے پاس مر گیا ہے اپنے آپ کو امانت کی ذمہ داری سے سبکدوش کرنا چاہتا ہے اور امانت کے سلسلہ میں مالک اور امین کے درمیان اگر یہ اختلاف ہو جائے کہ امین ، امانت سے عہدہ برا ہونے کا مدعی ہو اور مالک اس کا منکر ہو تو امین کا قول معتبر ہوتا ہے۔ پس یہاں بھی چونکہ مؤکل جو روپیہ کا مالک ہے یہ دعویٰ کرتا ہے کہ تو نے غلام میرے لئے نہیں خریدا ہے بلکہ اپنے لئے خریدا ہے۔ لہذا تو نے عہدہ امانت ادا نہیں کیا ہے اور وکیل جو امین ہے وہ دعوی کرتا
ہے کہ میں نے یہ غلام تیرے لئے خریدا تھا۔ لہذا میں امانت کی ذمہ داری ادا کر چکا۔ اسلئے یہاں بھی امین یعنی وکیل کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ جس وقت مؤکل اور وکیل میں اختلاف ہوا یعنی وکیل نے کہا کہ میں نے یہ غلام تیرے لئے خریدا ہے اور مؤکل نے کہا کہ نہیں بلکہ تو نے اپنے لئے خریدا ہے اسوقت اگر یہ غلام زندہ ہو اور موکل وکیل کو شمن دے چکا ہے تو وکیل کا قول معتبر ہو گا۔ کیونکہ وکیل امین ہے عہدہ امانت سے نکلنا چاہتا ہے اور پہلے گزر چکا کہ امین کا قول معتبر ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا اس صورت میں بھی وکیل کا قول معتبر ہو گا۔ اور اگر مؤکل نے وکیل کوشن نہیں دیا ہے تو صاحبین کے نزدیک اس صورت میں بھی وکیل ہی کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ مگر امام اعظم کے نزدیک مؤکل کا قول معتبر ہو گا۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں وکیل موکل کیلئے از سر نو عقد شراء کرنے پر قادر ہے کیونکہ غلام زندہ ہے اور زندہ غلام محمل شراء ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا وکیل فی الحال اس غلام کو موکل کیلئے خرید نے پر قادر ہے اور جب وکیل اس غلام کو فی الحال مؤکل کیلئے خریدنے پر قادر ہے تو وکیل اپنی اس خبر میں کہ میں نے یہ غلام مؤکل کیلئے خریدا ہے متہم نہ ہوگا۔ جب وکیل اپنی اس خبر میں متہم نہیں ہے تو اس کا قول بالیقین معتبر ہوگا۔
اعتراض لیکن اگر اس پر اعتراض کرے کہ اگر خریداری اولا وکیل کیلئے ہو جیسا کہ موکل کہتا ہے تو اس کے بعد از سرنو موکل کیلئے خریداری کیسے ہو سکتی ہے۔ جواب ... اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ وکیل اپنے بائع کے ساتھ عقد شراء کو مسخ کر دے پھر اس کو مؤکل کے لئے خرید لے اس طرح کوئی اعتراض واقع نہ ہوگا۔ حضرت امام اعظم کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وکیل کا یہ خبر دینا کہ میں نے یہ غلام موکل کیلئے خریدا ہے محل تہمت ہے اس طور پر کہ وکیل نے اس غلام کو اصلا تو اپنے لئے ہی خریدا ہو مگر جب اس میں خسارہ محسوس ہوا ہو تو اس کو مؤکل کے ذمہ ڈالنے کا ارادہ کر لیا ہو۔ پس اس تہمت کی وجہ سے وکیل کا قول معتبر نہ ہو گا۔ بلکہ مؤکل کا قول معتبر ہو گا۔ اسکے برخلاف جب مؤکل ، وکیل کوشن ادا کر چکا اور پھر وکیل اور موکل میں اختلاف ہوا تو وکیل کا قول اسلئے معتبر ہو گا کہ اس صورت میں وکیل امین ہے اور عہدہ امانت سے سبکدوش ہونے میں امین ہی کا قول معتبر ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا یہاں بھی وکیل جو امین ہے امانت سے عہدہ برا ہونے میں اس کا قول معتبر ہوگا اور اس کے ضمن اور تبعیت میں وکیل کا یہ قول بھی معتبر اور قبول ہوگا کہ غلام کی خریداری مؤکل کیلئے ہے اور جو چیز ضمناً تبعاً ثابت ہوتی ہے اس کے وصف کی طرف نظر نہیں کی
Kitab al-Wakalah. His statement is acceptable because this is a place of suspicion, in that he bought it for himself, then when he saw it was a loss-making transaction, he placed it on the principal. Contrary to the case when the price has been given, because there the agent is a trustee. Therefore, his statement will be accepted. And here the price is not in the agent's possession.
Explanation: The scenario is that if a person appointed another as an agent to buy a slave for one thousand rupees. The agent said, 'I bought that slave, but he died in my possession,' and the principal said, 'That is not so; rather, you bought that slave for yourself,' and the principal has not yet given the agent one thousand rupees, then in this case the principal's statement is accepted, and this purchase will be for the agent, not for the principal. This is also a narration of Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad. And if the principal has given the agent one thousand rupees, and then this dispute occurs, then by consensus the agent's statement is accepted. The reason for the difference between the two cases is that in the first case, i.e., where the principal has not given the price, the agent has reported a matter due to which he cannot produce it afresh. The detail is that the agent's saying, 'I bought the slave according to your command, but he died in my possession,' means that the agent wants to take the price of that dead slave from the principal, and the cause for taking the price from the principal is the contract. But the agent is not presently capable of the contract for this slave, because the slave in question is dead, and a dead slave does not form a valid contract. Therefore, this agent is not capable of the purchase contract for this dead slave. And whoever is not presently capable of producing something, his statement regarding that thing is not accepted. Hence, the agent's statement that he bought this slave for the principal and it died in his possession will not be accepted. For example, if a man gave his wife a revocable divorce and then said, 'I have taken her back,' and the woman said, 'You have not taken her back,' then if the woman's waiting period remains, the husband's statement is accepted because in that case the husband is capable of taking her back. But if the dispute occurs after the waiting period has passed, the husband's statement is not accepted, because the husband is not presently capable of taking her back. So here too, since the agent, due to the death of the slave, is not presently capable of making the contract anew, his statement will not be accepted. This argument can also be stated thus: The agent's demand for the price from the principal is specific to the fact that the agent bought the slave for the principal. That is, the agent is the claimant that he bought this slave for the principal, and the principal is the denier. And since in the case where the agent does not have the very object to prove his claim, the statement of the denier is accepted, so here the principal's statement is accepted.
Allamah Badr al-Din al-Ayni objected to a wording in this argument and gave a response. The objection is that in the phrase, the pronoun of 'istinaf' refers to the cause of return, i.e., the purchase contract, as was considered in the presentation of the argument. So when the contract is meant, why did the author of al-Hidayah, while indicating the referent of the pronoun of 'istinaf', say 'and that is the return of the price' and not say 'and that is the contract'? The answer is that the agent's purpose in making the purchase contract anew is to take the price from the principal, not to make a purchase contract for the principal. So the author of al-Hidayah, abandoning the intermediary (the contract), clarified what was intended. Thus, this will be in the category of mentioning the cause (return of price to the principal) and meaning the cause (purchase contract), and that is permissible. And in the second case, i.e., where the principal has paid the price to the agent, in that case the agent is a trustee, and by saying, 'I bought the slave for you, but he died in my possession,' he wants to free himself from the responsibility of the trust. And regarding trust, if a dispute arises between the owner and trustee—that the trustee claims to have discharged the trust and the owner denies it—then the trustee's statement is accepted. So here too, since the principal, who is the owner of the money, claims that you did not buy the slave for me but for yourself, so you have not discharged the trust, and the agent, who is the trustee, claims that I bought this slave for you, so I have discharged the trust, therefore here too the trustee's (i.e., agent's) statement is accepted. The author of al-Hidayah said: When a dispute occurs between the principal and agent—the agent says, 'I bought this slave for you,' and the principal says, 'No, you bought it for yourself'—if the slave is alive and the principal has given the price, then the agent's statement is accepted, because the agent is a trustee who wants to exit the trust. It has already passed that the trustee's statement is accepted. Hence in this case too, the agent's statement is accepted. And if the principal has not given the price, then according to the two companions (Sahibayn), even in this case the agent's statement is accepted, but according to Imam A'zam (Abu Hanifa), the principal's statement is accepted. The proof of the two companions is that in this case the agent is capable of making the purchase contract for the principal anew because the slave is alive, and a living slave is subject to purchase. Thus the agent is presently capable of buying this slave for the principal. And when the agent is capable of buying this slave for the principal, he will not be suspect in his report that he bought this slave for the principal. When the agent is not suspect in his report, his statement is definitely accepted. Objection: But if one objects: If the purchase was initially for the agent, as the principal says, then how can he buy it anew for the principal? Answer: The answer is that the agent can rescind the purchase contract with the seller and then buy it for the principal. Thus no objection remains. The proof of Imam A'zam is that the agent's reporting that he bought this slave for the principal is a place of suspicion, in that the agent originally bought the slave for himself, but when he sensed loss, he intended to foist it upon the principal. So due to this suspicion, the agent's statement is not accepted; rather, the principal's statement is accepted. Conversely, when the principal has paid the price to the agent and then a dispute occurs, the agent's statement is accepted because in that case the agent is a trustee, and in discharging the trust, the trustee's statement is accepted. Hence here too, the agent, who is a trustee, his statement regarding discharging the trust is accepted, and by inclusion and consequence, his statement that the purchase of the slave was for the principal is also accepted and admissible. And when something is established implicitly and consequentially, its description is not considered.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Wakalah (Book of Agency) is a legal analysis of a dispute between a principal (muwakkil) and an agent (wakil) concerning a purchase made by the agent. The core issue: did the agent buy the slave for the principal or for himself? The ruling depends on two variables: whether the price has been paid, and whether the slave is alive or dead. The author begins by stating the general principle: the agent's statement is not accepted where there is suspicion (tuhma) that the agent bought for himself and then imputed the loss to the principal. But if the price has already been paid, the agent is a trustee (amin), and a trustee's statement about discharging his trust is accepted.

The text then explains the mas'ala (case) in detail. Scenario 1: The agent claims he bought the slave for the principal but the slave died; the principal denies he was buying for him, and the price has not been paid. In this case, the principal's statement is accepted, and the purchase is deemed for the agent himself. This is also the view of Imams Shafi'i and Ahmad. The reason is that the agent cannot produce the slave anew (since it is dead), so his claim is akin to a claim he cannot prove; the principal, as the denier, is favored. This is supported by an analogy (qiyas) with divorce: a husband's claim of taking back his wife is accepted only if he is still capable of doing so (i.e., during the 'idda). Here, since the slave is dead, the agent cannot reperform the contract, so his statement is not accepted.

The author anticipates a textual objection by Allamah Badr al-Din al-Ayni: Why did the author of al-Hidayah say "and that is the return of the price" instead of "and that is the contract"? The answer is that the agent's ultimate goal is to get the price, not the contract itself; mentioning the cause (return of price) while meaning the actual cause (contract) is permissible in such legal analysis.

Scenario 2: The price has been paid. Here, by consensus (bil ittifaq), the agent's statement is accepted because the agent is a trustee, and a trustee's statement about fulfilling his duty is accepted. The agent wants to clear himself of liability, so his word is taken.

The text then introduces an intra-Hanafi dispute within Scenario 1 if the slave is alive and the price has not been paid. According to the two companions (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), the agent's statement is accepted because he can still buy the slave for the principal by rescinding and retracting. Imam Abu Hanifa, however, holds that the principal's statement is accepted due to suspicion: the agent might have bought for himself and then changed his mind when facing loss. The proof of the Sahibayn: since the slave is alive, the agent can still execute the contract, so he is not suspect. An objection about contradiction is resolved: the agent can rescind and then buy. Imam A'zam's proof: the situation inherently involves suspicion, so the principal (denier) is favored.

The text concludes by reiterating that when the price is paid, the agent's statement is accepted as a trustee's statement, and the issue of purchase for the principal is accepted by consequence.

Throughout, the author uses careful reasoning, analogy, and addresses a potential textual ambiguity. He presents both intra-Hanafi positions and gives the proofs, but the structure suggests that Imam Abu Hanifa's view is the relied-upon position in the first scenario where the price is unpaid and the slave is dead; for the living slave scenario, the Sahibayn's view is also considered. The later portions of the text (not fully quoted here) likely provide tarjih (preference).

Key Terms
الوكالة (al-wakālah): A contract of agency where one person (principal) appoints another (agent) to perform a legal act on his behalf.
موکل (muwakkil): The principal who appoints the agent.
وکیل (wakīl): The agent who acts on behalf of the principal.
ثمن (thaman): The price paid for the purchased item.
تہمت (tuhma): Suspicion; a legal presumption that a party may be acting deceitfully.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the dispute between the principal and agent regarding the purchase of a slave, if the slave died and the price has not been paid, whose statement is accepted according to Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) The agent's statement because he is a trustee.
B) The principal's statement because the agent cannot produce the slave anew.
C) The agent's statement because he can rescind and buy again.
D) The principal's statement because he is the owner of the money.

Key Takeaway
When the price is unpaid, the principal's statement is accepted if the agent cannot redo the contract; this principle is supported by qiyas with marital revocation after 'idda, and the living slave case involves an intra-Hanafi dispute where Abu Hanifa's view (favoring the principal) is mufta bihi.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
6 min
The Binding Effect of an Agent's Acknowledgement and the Role of Ta'ati in Sales
Ruling when agent denies, principal affirms/denies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when an agent denies agency after a sale and the principal later affirms, and explain how delivery by mutual consent (ta'ati) can create a binding sale.

Core Idea
An initial acknowledgement of agency cannot be undone by later denial; if the principal affirms, the sale binds him.

This passage addresses a common situation in commercial transactions: A person instructs another to sell an item for a third party. The seller then denies the agency, but later the alleged principal confirms the order. The Hanafi ruling clarifies that the initial statement is a binding acknowledgement, and subsequent denial is ineffective. Additionally, if the principal rejects, the sale may still be valid through ta'ati (delivery and acceptance). Understanding this ruling protects parties from disputes in agency and sale contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their statements
Person A says to B: 'Sell this slave for C.' B sells. Then A denies that C ordered him. Later C comes and either affirms or denies the order. Identify each statement's legal significance.
2
Apply the rule of iqrar (acknowledgement)
A's initial statement is an acknowledgement of agency. In Hanafi law, iqrar is binding and cannot be revoked by later denial. Therefore, if C affirms, the agency is confirmed and C takes the slave.
The text: 'li'anna qawlahu al-sabiq iqrarun minhu bil-wikalah'anhu'
3
Consider the principal's denial
If C says 'I did not order him,' the acknowledgement is reversed because the beneficiary rejects it. Then the slave does not go to C automatically.
4
Analyze the ta'ati alternative
Even if C denies, if the buyer delivers the slave to C and C accepts, a sale by ta'ati (mutual consent through delivery) arises. C becomes liable for the price, similar to buying for another without authorization.
This applies to all items, valuable or cheap.
5
Note the scope of ta'ati
Delivery in the manner of sale suffices for ta'ati even without payment of price. The key is mutual consent (taradi).

ومن قال لآخر يعنى هذا العبد لفلان فباعه ثم انكر ان يكون فلان امره ثم جاء فلان وقال انا امرته بذالك فان فلانا يأخذه لأن قوله السابق اقرار منه بالوكالة عنه فلا ينفعه الانكار اللاحق فان قال فلان لم آمره لم یکن ذالک له لان الاقرار ارتد برده قال الا ان يسلمه المشترى له فيكون بيعا عنه وعليه العهدة لانه صار مشتريا بالتعاطى كمن اشترى لغيره بغير امره حتى لزمه ثم سلمه المشترى له ودلت المسألة على ان التسليم على وجه البيع يكفى للتعاطى وان لم يوجد نقد الثمن وهو يتحقق فى النفيس والخسيس لاستتمام التراصى وهو المعتبر في الباب
And whoever said to another, 'Sell this slave for so-and-so,' and he sold it, then he denied that so-and-so ordered him, then so-and-so came and said 'I ordered him to do that,' then so-and-so takes it, because his earlier statement is an acknowledgement of agency on his behalf, so the later denial does not benefit him. If so-and-so said 'I did not order him,' then it is not for him, because the acknowledgement is reversed by its rejection. He said: unless the buyer delivers it to him (so-and-so), then it becomes a sale on his behalf and the liability is on him, because he became a buyer by mutual agreement (ta'ati), like one who buys for another without his order until it becomes binding, then he delivers it to the intended buyer. And the case indicates that delivery in the manner of sale suffices for ta'ati even if the price was not paid, and this applies to both valuable and cheap items because the mutual consent is complete, and that is what is considered in this chapter.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage deals with a scenario: Person A says to B, 'Sell this slave for C (a third party).' B sells it. Then A denies that C ordered him (or denies that he was acting for C). Later, C comes and says 'I did order A to buy it for me.' The ruling: C takes the slave (i.e., the sale is valid for C). The reason is that A's initial statement ('sell for C') is an acknowledgement (iqrar) that A is acting as C's agent. A later denial is ineffective because an acknowledgement once made cannot be undone by subsequent denial. However, if C says 'I did not order him,' then the slave does not go to C, because the acknowledgement is reversed by C's rejection. In that case, if A (the seller? Actually the person who bought it) delivers the slave to C, it becomes a sale to C by mutual agreement (ta'ati), and C becomes liable to pay the price. This is similar to someone buying goods for another without authorization; if the goods are delivered and accepted, a sale is formed. The passage also clarifies that delivery with the intention of sale is sufficient for ta'ati even without payment of price, and applies to both expensive and cheap items because mutual consent is what matters.

Key Terms
التعاطي (al-ta'ati): A sale concluded by mutual overt actions (delivery and acceptance) without formal offer and acceptance words.
اقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment, a declaration that creates legal consequences.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if A initially says 'sell for C', sells, then C denies ordering, but later accepts delivery?
A) C is not liable.
B) C is liable for the price because of ta'ati.
C) The sale is void.
D) A is liable.

Key Takeaway
An initial acknowledgement of agency is binding; subsequent denial is ineffective, but the principal's rejection reverses it; however, delivery and acceptance can create a new sale by ta'ati.

Denial of Agency and Exception via Delivery in Hanafi Fiqh
Ruling with proof and exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling when a principal denies agency but the agent delivers the object, and distinguish between the general rule (slave belongs to agent) and the exception (valid sale by mutual exchange).

Core Idea
When principal denies agency, agent's admission is void, but delivering the object creates a valid sale by mutual exchange.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a common dispute: one person (Khalid) claims he was an agent to buy a slave for another (Shahid), but Shahid denies giving such a command. The Hanafi school addresses two scenarios. First, if Shahid simply denies, Khalid's admission of agency is nullified and the slave belongs to Khalid. However, there is an exception: if Khalid delivers the slave to Shahid, then Shahid may take it by paying the price. This is not a reinstatement of agency but a new sale concluded by mutual exchange (bay' al-ta'ati). The author supports this by analogy to the case of a fuduli (unauthorized person) who buys something for another and then delivers it, which also creates a valid sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the general rule
Read the passage to understand the basic scenario: Khalid claims he was an agent to buy a slave for Shahid. Shahid denies. According to the general rule, Khalid's admission of agency is nullified by Shahid's denial, so the slave belongs to Khalid, not Shahid.
This follows the principle that an admission (iqrar) can be voided by contradictory evidence or rejection.
2
Recognize the exception from Imam Muhammad
The passage introduces an exception: 'illa an yusallimahu al-mushtari lahu' (except if the buyer delivers it to him). This means if Khalid delivers the slave to Shahid, Shahid has the right to take it. This exception is from Imam Muhammad's narration and is accepted as operative.
The grammatical analysis in the commentary clarifies two readings, but the legal effect is the same.
3
Understand the legal basis: bay' al-ta'ati
The transaction is not a revival of agency but a new sale. Khalid becomes a seller by delivering the slave, and Shahid becomes a buyer by taking it and paying. This is a sale by mutual exchange (bay' al-ta'ati), which is valid in Hanafi law without formal offer and acceptance.
Bay' al-ta'ati is based on mutual consent and customary practice.
4
Analyze the analogy to the fuduli case
The author of Hidayah provides an analogy: if a fuduli (unauthorized person) buys something for another without permission and then delivers it, the delivery creates a valid sale by mutual exchange. Similarly, in the agency denial case, the delivery creates a sale.
This is a qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) where the effective cause (illa) is the delivery with intention to transfer ownership in exchange for price.
5
Conclude the operative ruling
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that the exception applies: if the agent delivers after denial, the principal may take the item by paying its price. The transaction is valid (sahih) as a sale.
This ruling is from the Nawadir (Imam Muhammad's narrations) but is accepted in practice.

صاحب ہدایہ نے دلیل دیتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ خالد اور شاہد کے درمیان یہ لین دین ج تعاطی کے طور پر ہوگا۔ یعنی خالد بیع تعاطی کے طور پر فروخت کرنے والا ہوگا۔ اور شاہد خرید نے والا ہوگا اور بیچ تعاطی جائز ہے جیسا کہ کتاب البیوع کے آغاز میں گذر چکا ہے۔ لہذا خالد اور شاہد کا لین دین بھی جائز ہوگا۔ اور اس کی مثال ایسی ہے جیسے ایک فضولی آدمی مثلاً واصف نے اپنے غیر مثلاً عارف کیلئے بغیر عارف کے حکم کے کوئی چیز خریدی تو یہ عقد شراء مشتری یعنی واصف پر لازم ہوگا۔ مگر پھر مشتری (واصف) نے اس چیز ، عارف کے سپرد کر دیا تو یہ بیع تعاطی ہوگی۔ یعنی بیع تعاطی کے طور پر واصف بیچنے والا ہوگا۔ اور عارف خریدنے والا ہوگا۔
It will not become void. Therefore here too, Khalid's prior admission is not nullified by his subsequent denial. And when Khalid's admission of agency is not voided, then the slave he bought belongs to the principal, i.e., Shahid, not to the agent, i.e., Khalid. And if so-and-so, i.e., Shahid, said, 'I did not command Khalid to buy the mentioned slave,' then in that case Shahid has no right to take the mentioned slave. Because the buyer, i.e., Khalid, made an admission of his agency, and it became void due to the principal's (Shahid's) rejection. And when Khalid's admission of agency is voided, then the bought slave belongs to Khalid (the buyer) himself, not to Shahid. After that, even if Shahid confirms Khalid's admission, this confirmation is of no benefit to him. Because due to Shahid's rejection, when Khalid's admission became null, Shahid's confirmation is not valid. Except for the saying of Imam Muhammad: 'except if the buyer for him delivers it' is an exception to the previous phrase 'it is not for him.' That is, if so-and-so (Shahid) said, 'I did not command Khalid to buy the mentioned slave,' then in that case Shahid has no right to the mentioned slave. But there is one case in which despite this saying, Shahid has the right to take the slave. And that case is that which is explained by 'except if the buyer for him delivers it.' The author of Fath al-Qadir wrote that the word 'mushtari' is narrated in two readings: one with kasra on the 'ra', the second with fatha on the 'ra'. With kasra, the word 'al-mushtari' is the subject of 'yusallim', and 'lahu' is for the purpose, and its pronoun refers to so-and-so (Shahid). And 'yusallimuhu' has an implicit direct object, and its referent is the mentioned slave. And the second object, i.e., 'ilayhi', is omitted, and the referent of 'ilayhi' is so-and-so (Shahid). So the meaning is: if the buying person (Khalid) delivers this slave to so-and-so (Shahid) for Shahid, then Shahid has the right to take this slave and give its price to Khalid. With fatha, the pronoun in 'yusallimuhu' is the direct object, referent is the slave, and 'al-mushtari lahu' is the second object with the letter of jar, and 'al-mushtari la' refers to so-and-so (Shahid), and the subject of 'yusallimuhu' is an implied pronoun referring to the buyer (Khalid). So the meaning is: if the buyer (Khalid) delivers this slave to the buyer for him, i.e., so-and-so (Shahid), then Shahid has the right to take this slave and pay its price. Now the summary of the entire passage is: if Shahid said that he did not command Khalid to buy the mentioned slave, then Shahid is not entitled to take the mentioned slave. However, if Khalid delivers this slave to Shahid, then in that case Shahid is entitled to take this slave. But this entitlement is not because Khalid is an agent to buy for Shahid, but because Khalid's delivering the slave to Shahid is a sale from Khalid, and Shahid is obliged to take the slave by paying its price. The author of Hidayah provided evidence saying that this transaction between Khalid and Shahid is a mutual exchange (bay' al-ta'ati). That is, Khalid will be the seller by way of bay' al-ta'ati, and Shahid will be the buyer. And bay' al-ta'ati is valid, as passed at the beginning of the Book of Sales. Therefore, the transaction between Khalid and Shahid is also valid. And its example is like a fuduli person, e.g., Wasif, bought something for another, e.g., Arif, without Arif's command, then this purchase contract is binding on the buyer, i.e., Wasif. But then if the buyer (Wasif) delivers that thing to Arif, then this is a bay' al-ta'ati. That is, by way of bay' al-ta'ati, Wasif is the seller and Arif is the buyer.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school regarding a dispute over agency. The scenario: Khalid claims he was an agent to buy a slave for Shahid, but Shahid denies giving such a command. The ruling: If Shahid denies, Khalid's admission of agency is invalidated retroactively, so the slave belongs to Khalid, not Shahid. Even if Shahid later confirms, it does not help because the rejection already rendered the admission null. However, there is an exception: if Khalid delivers the slave to Shahid, then Shahid may take it, but not as an agency transaction; rather, it becomes a sale by mutual exchange (bay' al-ta'ati). The author explains the two readings of the exception phrase from Imam Muhammad's narration, specifying the grammatical analysis. The author of Hidayah then proves the validity of such a transaction by analogy to a fuduli (unauthorized agent) who buys and then delivers to the principal; that delivery becomes a valid sale by mutual exchange. Thus, the ruling is based on the Hanafi principle that bay' al-ta'ati is valid even without formal offer and acceptance, relying on mutual consent and customary practice.

Key Terms
اقرار (iqrar): Admission or declaration by Khalid that he was acting as an agent; it has legal effect unless revoked.
بیع تعاطی (bay' al-ta'ati): A sale concluded by the mutual exchange of goods without formal verbal offer and acceptance, based on customary practice.
فضولی (fuduli): An unauthorized person who acts on behalf of another without permission; the contract is suspended until ratification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is a gift from the agent to the principal.
B) It is a reinstatement of the agency contract.
C) It is a sale by mutual exchange (bay' al-ta'ati).
D) It is a loan for use (ariyah).

Key Takeaway
Delivery of the object by the agent after denial of agency transforms the transaction into a valid sale by mutual exchange, allowing the principal to take it upon payment of the price.

Bay' al-Ta'ati: Validity and the Dispute over Valuable Items
Intra-Hanafi dispute on scope of bay' al-ta'ati

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of bay' al-ta'ati according to the majority Hanafi position and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding valuable items.

Core Idea
Bay' al-ta'ati is valid for all items because mutual consent, not verbal formality, is the essence of a sale.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi concept of bay' al-ta'ati—a sale concluded by mutual delivery without verbal offer and acceptance. The author of Al-Hidayah affirms its validity for both ordinary and valuable items, citing mutual consent as the essential condition. However, Imam al-Karkhi restricts it to ordinary items only, raising an important intra-Hanafi dispute. This lesson unpacks the arguments and clarifies the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Define bay' al-ta'ati
Understand that bay' al-ta'ati is a sale concluded by the exchange of goods without verbal ijab and qabul, based on customary practice.
2
Identify the majority Hanafi position
The author of Hidayah holds that bay' al-ta'ati is valid for all items, including valuable ones (nafisah) and ordinary ones (hissiyah), as long as mutual consent is present.
3
Examine the proof
The majority cites Quran 4:29 ('an taradin') and the consistent custom (urf) of people, showing that consent is inferred from the act of taking and giving.
4
State the opposing view
Imam al-Karkhi restricts bay' al-ta'ati to ordinary items, likely arguing that valuable items require explicit consent to avoid disputes.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The majority position is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view in the Hanafi school, as endorsed by later scholars.

Source Text

منعقد ہو جاتی ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ بیع تعاطی ، اشیائے نفیسہ اور اشیاء حسیہ دونوں میں متحقق ہوتی ہے۔ یعنی بیچ تعاطی جس طرح اشیا بے نحسیہ میں جائز ہے۔ اسی طرح اشیائے نفیسہ میں بھی جائز ہے کیونکہ بیچ درست ہونے کیلئے عاقدین کی باہمی رضا مندی شرط ہے ( جیسا کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے الا ان تكون تجارة عن تراض ) اور باہمی رضامندی اشیائے نفیسہ اور اشیائے سیسہ دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کی بیچ تعاطی میں پورے طور پر موجود ہے لہذا ہر ایک کی بیع تعاطی جائز ہوگی۔
امام کرخی نے فرمایا کہ بیع تعاطی صرف اشیائے حسیہ میں جائز ہے اس کی پوری تفصیل کتاب البیوع کے اول میں گذر چکی ہے۔
The author of Hidayah said: For bay' al-ta'ati, it is sufficient that something is handed over on the basis of sale, even if the taker does not pay the price immediately. That is, just as bay' al-ta'ati is concluded by taking and giving (taking the item and paying the price), similarly it is concluded by taking without giving (taking the item without paying the price), as is people's habit. For example, you may see that people who have ongoing accounts with shops take goods without formal offer and acceptance and do not pay immediately. This transaction without offer and acceptance is called bay' al-ta'ati. So from people's custom, it is established that bay' al-ta'ati is concluded even without payment of price. The author of Hidayah said: Bay' al-ta'ati applies to both valuable items and ordinary items. That is, just as bay' al-ta'ati is valid for ordinary items, similarly it is valid for valuable items, because for a valid sale, mutual consent of the contracting parties is a condition (as Allah said: 'except it be a trade by mutual consent'), and mutual consent is fully present in bay' al-ta'ati for both valuable and ordinary items. Therefore, bay' al-ta'ati is valid for both. Imam al-Karkhi said that bay' al-ta'ati is only valid for ordinary items; its full detail has passed at the beginning of the Book of Sales.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the scope of bay' al-ta'ati (sale by mutual exchange). The author of Hidayah holds that bay' al-ta'ati is valid for all items, both valuable (nafisah) and ordinary (hissiyah), because the essential condition is mutual consent, which is present regardless of the item's value. He supports this with the Quranic verse 'illa an takuna tijaratan 'an taradin' (Quran 4:29). He also notes that customary practice (urf) shows that people often take goods without formal offer and acceptance, even valuable items, and this is accepted. In contrast, Imam al-Karkhi restricts bay' al-ta'ati to ordinary items only, presumably because valuable items require more explicit consent. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of the majority, extending bay' al-ta'ati to all items, as stated in Hidayah and other major works.

Key Terms
بیع تعاطی (bay' al-ta'ati): A sale concluded by the mutual giving and taking of goods without verbal offer and acceptance, based on customary practice.
اشیائے نفیسہ (ashya' nafisah): Valuable or expensive items (e.g., jewelry, land).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author of Hidayah, what is the basis for the validity of bay' al-ta'ati for all items?
A) Formal offer and acceptance
B) The condition of mutual consent and customary practice
C) The payment of price at the time of contract
D) The item must be inexpensive

Key Takeaway
Bay' al-ta'ati is valid for all items in the majority Hanafi view because mutual consent, established by action and custom, suffices for a valid sale.

Absolute Agency to Purchase: Buying One of Two Specified Slaves
Ruling on agent purchasing one of two specified slaves when price was not mentioned

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for an absolute agency to purchase when the agent buys one of two specified items without a specified price, and identify the exception of ghabn fahish (excessive overpayment).

Core Idea
An absolute agency to purchase allows buying singly, but excessive overpayment invalidates the purchase for the principal.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a common agency scenario: the principal authorizes the agent to purchase two specific slaves without fixing a price, and the agent buys only one. Is the principal bound? The ruling hinges on whether the agency is absolute and on the concept of ghabn fahish. The text also distinguishes this from agency to sell, where overpayment is treated differently.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the agent purchasing one of two specified slaves for the principal. The ruling is that the purchase is valid (jā'iz) for the principal.
2
Determine the nature of the agency
The agency is described as 'absolute' (tawkil mutlaq) because no price or manner of purchase was specified. This allows the agent flexibility.
Absolute agency proceeds on its absoluteness, meaning the agent may buy singly or together.
3
Analyze the exception of ghabn fahish
If the agent buys with ghabn fahish (excessive overpayment), the purchase is not valid for the principal; the agent becomes liable.
Ghabn fahish is defined as a price significantly above market value (customarily determined).
4
Note the proof (ijma)
The author states that the entire ruling is by consensus (ijma). This gives it strong authority within the Hanafi school.
Ijma is a primary source of law; here it confirms the invalidity of ghabn fahish in purchase agency.
5
Distinguish from agency to sell
Ibn al-Humam notes that for agency to sell, Imam Abu Hanifa permits ghabn fahish (selling above market) because it benefits the principal.
This distinction is crucial: purchase agency is stricter than sale agency regarding overpayment.

Source Text

ایک شخص نے دوسرے کو دو معین غلام خریدنے کا حکم کیا اور ثمن اسکے سامنے بیان نہیں کئے پھر وکیل نے دو میں سے ایک غلام مؤکل کیلئے خریدا تو جائز ہے

قال و من امر رجلا بان يشترى له عبدين باعيانهما ولم يسم له ثمنا فاشترى له احدهما جاز لان التوكيل مطلق فيجرى على اطلاقه وقد لا يتفق الجمع بينهما فى البيع الا فيما لا يتغابن الناس فيه لانه توكيل بالشراء وهذا كله بالاجماع

ترجمہ اور اگر ایک شخص نے کسی آدمی کو اس بات کا حکم دیا کہ وہ اس کے واسطے دو معین غلام خریدے اور اس آدمی کے سامنے شمن بیان نہیں کیا پھر اس آدمی نے مؤکل کیلئے ان دونوں میں سے ایک غلام خریدا تو جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ تو کیل مطلق ہے۔ لہذاوہ اپنے اطلاق پر جاری ہوگی اور کبھی بیچ میں دونوں غلاموں کا جمع کرنا ممکن نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ مگر اس صورت میں جس میں لوگ دھوکہ نہ کھاتے ہوں ۔ اسلئے کہ یہ توکیل بالشراء ہے اور یہ تمام کا تمام بالا جماع ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص مثلاً خالد نے دوسرے شخص مثلا شاہد سے کہا کہ تو میرے لئے یہ دو معین غلام خرید کر لا دے اور مؤکل (خالد) نے غلاموں میں سے ایک غلام مؤکل کیلئے خرید کیا تو یہ خریداری جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں توکیل مطلق ہے یعنی موکل نے ان دونوں غلاموں کو نہ تو علیحدہ علیحدہ خریدنے کی قید کے ساتھ مقید کیا ہے اور نہ دونوں کو ایک ساتھ خریدنے کی قید کے ساتھ مقید کیا ہے بلکہ مطلق رکھا ہے اور مطلق اپنے اطلاق پر جاری ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا وکیل ان دونوں غلاموں کو علیحدہ علیحدہ خریدے یا ایک ساتھ خرید ے دونوں صورتیں جائز ہیں۔ یعنی دونوں صورتوں میں خریداری مؤکل کیلئے ہوگی۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ کبھی دونوں غلاموں کو ایک ساتھ خرید ناممکن نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ اسلئے بھی اگر وکیل نے ایک غلام خریدا توبہ خریداری مؤکل پر ہی نافذ ہو گی ۔ ہاں اگر وکیل نے ایک غلام غبن فاحش کے ساتھ خریدا تو یہ خریداری جائز نہ ہوگی ۔ یعنی اسکا ذمہ دار وکیل ہوگا اور موکل ذمہ دار نہ ہوگا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ تو کیل بالشراء ہے یعنی موکل نے اس کو خریداری کا وکیل کیا ہے اور تو کیل بالشراء بالاجماع غبن فاحش کی متحمل نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ یعنی مؤکل کی طرف سے وکیل بالشراء کو مین فاحش کے ساتھ خریداری کرنے کی اجازت نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ پس جب وکیل بالشراء کو غبن فاحش کے ساتھ خریداری کرنے کی اجازت نہیں ہوتی تو اگر وکیل بالشراء نے غبن فاحش کے ساتھ خریداری کی تو موکل کے حکم کے خلاف ہونے کی وجہ سے یہ خریداری موکل پر نافذ نہ ہوگی۔ بلکہ وکیل پر نافذ ہوگی۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ یہ پورا مسئلہ بالا جماع ہے۔ علامہ ابن الہمام نے کہا کہ صاحب ہدایہ نے توکیل بالشراء کی قید کے ساتھ اسلئے عقد کیا ہے کہ تو کیل بالبیع کی صورت میں اگر وکیل نے غبن فاحش کے ساتھ فروخت کیا تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک یہ فروخت کرنا جائز ہے۔ یعنی اگر ایک غلام فروخت کرنے کا کسی کو وکیل کیا اور غلام کی قیمت دوسورو پی تھی مگر وکیل نے اس کو تین سورو پسیہ میں فروخت کیا تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک یہ جائز ہے اور یہ بیع مؤکل کیلئے ہے نہ کہ وکیل کیلئے ۔
A person ordered another to buy two specific slaves for him and did not specify the price. Then the agent bought one of the two for the principal. It is valid.

He said: Whoever orders a man to buy for him two slaves specified by their persons and does not name the price, then he buys one of them for him – it is valid because the agency is absolute, so it proceeds on its absoluteness. And sometimes it may not be possible to combine both in the sale except in what people do not consider excessive deception, because it is agency to purchase. And all of this is by consensus.

Translation: And if a person ordered a man to buy two specific slaves for him and did not state the price, then that man bought one of the two for the principal, it is valid. Because the agency is absolute, so it proceeds on its absoluteness. And sometimes it is not possible to combine both slaves in the sale, except in a case where people do not suffer deception. Because this is agency to purchase, and all of this is by consensus. Explanation of the issue: For example, Khalid told Shahid: 'Buy these two specific slaves for me and bring them.' Then the agent bought one of the slaves for the principal. This purchase is valid because the agency is absolute; the principal did not restrict him to buying them separately or together, but left it absolute. The absolute proceeds on its absoluteness. So whether the agent buys them separately or together, both forms are valid, and in both cases the purchase is for the principal. The author of al-Hidayah said: Sometimes purchasing both together is not impossible, so if the agent buys one, the purchase is still effective for the principal. However, if the agent buys a slave with ghabn fahish (excessive overpayment), then this purchase is not valid for the principal; the agent will be liable, not the principal. The proof is that this is agency to purchase, and agency to purchase, by consensus, does not tolerate ghabn fahish. That is, the agent for purchase is not permitted to purchase with ghabn fahish. So if the agent purchases with ghabn fahish, it violates the principal's command, so the purchase does not bind the principal but binds the agent. The author of al-Hidayah said this entire issue is by consensus. Allamah Ibn al-Humam said that the author of al-Hidayah qualified it as agency to purchase because in the case of agency to sell, if the agent sells with ghabn fahish, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, such a sale is valid, i.e., if someone is appointed agent to sell a slave, and the slave's price was two hundred rupees, but the agent sold it for three hundred rupees, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, this is valid, and the sale is for the principal, not for the agent.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from ijma (consensus). It presents the case of an absolute agency to purchase two specified slaves without a price being mentioned. The agent buys one of them. The ruling, based on the matn of al-Hidayah, is that the purchase is valid because the agency is absolute, allowing the agent to buy any of the slaves singly or together. The commentary explains that the exception is ghabn fahish (excessive overpayment), which is not permitted in agency to purchase by consensus. The agent bears liability for such overpayment. Ibn al-Humam adds that this rule is specific to agency to purchase; for agency to sell, Imam Abu Hanifa allows the agent to sell even with ghabn fahish, as selling above market price benefits the principal.

Key Terms
توکیل مطلق (tawkil mutlaq): An agency granted without specifying details, such as manner of purchase or price, allowing the agent to act according to customary practice.
غبن فاحش (ghabn fahish): Excessive deception or overpayment in a transaction, where the price paid is significantly above the market value.
توکیل بالشراء (tawkil bil-shira'): Agency to purchase something on behalf of the principal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The principal
B) The agent
C) Both equally
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
An absolute agency to purchase binds the principal only if the price is within customary bounds; excessive overpayment (ghabn fahish) is not tolerated and makes the agent liable.
