Agency to Purchase Two Slaves for a Specified Price with Equal Value
Ruling when agent buys one of two equal-value slaves for more or less than half the specified price

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on agency when an agent buys one of two equal-value slaves for more or less than half the specified price, including the istihsan exception.

Core Idea
Buying one slave for more than half the total price is not binding, but istihsan validates it if the agent later completes the pair.

This lesson examines a nuanced agency case from Al-Hidayah: a principal instructs an agent to buy two slaves of equal value for a total price. The agent buys only one. How does the law determine whether the principal is bound? Imam Abu Hanifa provides a detailed answer that balances the implied division of the price against the explicit objective of acquiring both slaves. This ruling introduces the key Hanafi principles of dalalah (implication), sarih (explicit statement), and istihsan (juridical preference).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the key variable
Determine what the agent did: he bought one of two equal-value slaves. The variable is whether he paid exactly half, less, or more than half of the total price specified by the principal.
The total price is 1000; half is 500.
2
Apply the implied division (dalalah)
Since the slaves are equal in value, the total price is implied to be divided equally. Thus, each slave is considered to have a price limit of 500 by implication.
Dalalah is a non-explicit inference; it is weaker than sarih.
3
Classify the agent's action relative to the implied limit
If the agent buys for 500 or less, he acts within the implied authority (compliance or deviation to good). If he buys for more than 500, he exceeds the implied limit (deviation to evil).
The ruling hinges on this classification.
4
Examine the istihsan exception
Even if the agent buys for more than 500, the purchase becomes valid if he later buys the second slave with the remaining amount before any dispute arises. This is by istihsan, because the principal's explicit objective (acquiring both slaves for the total price) is achieved.
Istihsan allows departure from strict implication to fulfill the principal's intent.
5
Contrast dalalah and sarih
The implied division (dalalah) is overridden by the explicit instruction (sarih) to buy both for the total price. Hence the agent's deviation can be cured by completing the pair.
This illustrates the Hanafi hierarchy: sarih prevails over dalalah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
موکل نے وکیل کو کہا دونوں کو ایک ہزار کے عوض خرید لے اور دونوں کی قیمت برابر ہے ان میں ایک کو پانچ سو یا اس سے کم یا زیادہ میں خریدا تو مؤکل کو خریداری لازم ہوگی یا نہیں

ولو امره بان يشتريهما بالالف وقيمتهما سواء فعند ابي حنيفة ان اشترى احدهما بخمس مائة او اقل جاز فان اشترى باكثر لم يلزم الأمر لانه قابل الالف بهما وقيمتهما سواء فيقسم بينهما نصفين دلالة فكان أمراً بشرى كل واحد منهما بخمسمائة ثم الشراء بها موافقة و باقل منها مخالفة الى خير وبالزيادة الى نشر قلت الزيادة او كثرت فلا يجوز الا ان يشترى الباقى ببقية الالف قبل ان يختصما استحسانالان شرى الاول قائم وقد حصل غرضه المصرح به وهو تحصيل العبدين بالالف وما ثبت الانقسام الا دلالة والصريح يفوقها

ترجمہ اور اگر متوکل نے وکیل کو حکم دیا کہ ان دونوں غلاموں کو ایک ہزار روپیہ کے عوض خرید لے اور ان دونوں کی قیمت برابر ہے۔ پس امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اگر ان دونوں میں سے ایک کو پانچ سوروپیہ یا کم کے عوض خریدا تو جائز ہے ۔ اور اگر زیادہ کے عوض خریدا تو یہ خریداری مؤکل کے ذمہ لازم نہ ہوگی۔ اسلئے کہ مؤکل نے دونوں کے مقابلہ میں ایک ہزار بیان کیا ہے اور ان دونوں کی قیمت برابر ہے۔ تو ایک ہزار روپیہ دونوں کے درمیان دلالۂ آدھا آدھا تقسیم ہوگا ۔ پس گویا موکل ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کو پانچ سوروپیہ کے عوض خرید نے کا حکم کرنے والا ہے۔ پھر پانچ سو کے عوض خرید نا تو موافقت ہے اور پانچ سو روپیہ سے کم کے عوض خریدنا بہتر ائی کی طرف من الفت ہے اور پانچ سو سے زائد کے عوض خرید نا برائی کی طرف مخالفت ہے۔ زیادتی کم ہو یا زیادہ ہو جائز نہیں ہے مگر یہ کہ باقی غلام کو ہزار میں سے باقی کے عوض خصومت پیش آنے سے پہلے خرید لے تو یہ استحسانا جائز ہوگا۔ اسلئے کہ اول غلام کا خریدنا قائم ہے اور مؤکل کی رض جس کی صراحت کی گئی تھی یعنی ایک ہزار کے عوض دونوں کو خرید نا وہ حاصل ہوگئی ہے اور بٹوارہ نہیں ثابت ہوا مگر دلالت سے اور
The principal told the agent: 'Buy both for one thousand' and their price is equal. If he bought one of them for five hundred or less, or more, does the purchase become binding on the principal or not?

And if he ordered him to buy both for one thousand and their prices are equal, then according to Abu Hanifa, if he bought one of them for five hundred or less, it is valid. If he bought for more, the order is not binding because he allocated one thousand to both, and their prices are equal, so it is divided between them by implication into halves. So it is as if he ordered him to buy each one for five hundred. Then purchasing for that amount is compliance, purchasing for less is a deviation towards good, and purchasing for more is a deviation towards evil. Whether the excess is small or large, it is not valid, unless he buys the remaining one with the remainder of the thousand before they dispute – this is valid by istihsan, because the purchase of the first is subsisting, and his express objective of acquiring both slaves for one thousand has been achieved. The division is only established by implication, and the explicit statement overrides it.

Translation: And if the principal ordered the agent to buy both these slaves for one thousand rupees and their price is equal, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, if he bought one of them for five hundred rupees or less, it is valid. If he bought for more, this purchase will not be binding on the principal. Because the principal allocated one thousand to both and their price is equal. So one thousand rupees will be divided between them by implication into two halves. So it is as if the principal ordered him to buy each of them for five hundred rupees. Then purchasing for five hundred is compliance, purchasing for less than five hundred is a deviation towards good, and purchasing for more than five hundred is a deviation towards evil. Whether the excess is small or large, it is not valid, unless he buys the remaining slave with the remainder of the thousand before a dispute arises – then it is valid by istihsan, because the purchase of the first is subsisting, and the principal's expressly stated objective of acquiring both slaves for one thousand has been achieved. The division was only established by implication, and the explicit statement overrides it.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof based on istihsan (juridical preference). The case is: the principal orders the agent to buy two slaves of equal value for a total of one thousand. The agent buys only one of them. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if he buys one for exactly five hundred (half) or less, the purchase is valid and binding on the principal. If he buys for more than five hundred, it is not binding because the total price implies each is worth five hundred. However, if before any dispute arises, the agent buys the second slave with the remaining amount (i.e., for five hundred or less), then the principal's objective of buying both for one thousand is fulfilled, and the purchase becomes valid by istihsan. The reasoning is that the division of the price is only by implication (dalaalah), and the explicit instruction (sarih) to buy both for one thousand takes precedence. Thus, the agent's act is upheld to achieve the principal's goal.

Key Terms
دلالت (dalaalah): Implication; a meaning inferred from the wording but not explicitly stated. Here, the division of the price into halves is by implication.
صراحت (sarih): Explicit statement; the clear wording of the principal's instruction.
استحسان (istihsan): Juridical preference; a method of reasoning that allows departing from strict analogy (qiyas) for a more equitable outcome based on the specific circumstances.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if an agent buys one of two equal-value slaves for 600 out of a total price of 1000, what is the ruling?
A) The purchase is valid and binding on the principal
B) The purchase is not binding unless the agent buys the second slave before a dispute
C) The purchase is void entirely
D) The agent must pay the 100 himself

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prioritizes the principal's explicit intent over implied divisions, and allows istihsan to validate an agent's act if the ultimate objective is fulfilled.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Agent Buying Two Slaves with Set Price: Istihsan vs Qiyas
Explains ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on agent buying one slave at less or more than half total price

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of istihsan to determine when an agent's purchase exceeding the implied half of a total price becomes binding on the principal.

Core Idea
The explicit command overrides the implied division; completing the total objective before dispute makes the purchase binding by istihsan.

When a principal instructs an agent to buy two items of equal value for a single total price, an implied division of the price arises. But what happens if the agent buys one item for more than half? The Hanafi school, using istihsan, holds that if the total objective is achieved before any dispute, the purchase is binding. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and contrasts it with qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principal's command and its implied division
The principal said 'buy both for 1000' and the values are equal. By indication (dalala), the price is divided equally at 500 each. Recognize that this division is implied, not explicit.
The explicit command is to acquire both for the total; the division is only by context.
2
Classify the agent's action relative to the implied division
If the agent buys one slave for 500 or less, it is compliance or beneficial deviation. If more than 500, it is harmful deviation. Note the ruling for each: beneficial deviation is valid, harmful deviation is initially not binding on the principal.
Beneficial deviation (less than implied) is allowed because it benefits the principal.
3
Determine if the total objective was achieved before dispute
If the agent later buys the second slave with the remainder of the total price before any dispute arises, the principal's express purpose (both for the total) is fulfilled. This triggers istihsan.
The first purchase remains valid; it is not rescinded.
4
Apply istihsan to override qiyas
According to qiyas, the harmful deviation would make the first purchase invalid. But istihsan prioritizes the explicit command over the implied division. Since the total objective is met, the entire transaction is binding on the principal.
The rule: 'The explicit overrides the indication' (al-sarih yafuuq al-dalala).

دلالہ ثابت ہے۔
حاصل یہ کہ مؤکل کا صریح کلام تو یہ ہے کہ دونوں غلام ایک ہزار روپیہ کے عوض حاصل ہوں اور دلالیہ اس کے کلام سے معلوم ہوتا ہے اس نے ہر غلام کا عوض پانچ سو روپیہ قرار دیا ہے اور قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کلام صریح پر عمل کرنا ممکن ہو تو صریح دلالت سے بڑھ کر ہوتا ہے یعنی جب صراحت موجود ہو اور اس پر عمل کرنا بھی ممکن ہو تو دلالت باطل ہو جاتی ہے اس کا اعتبار نہیں کیا جاتا ہے۔ پس چونکہ یہاں دونوں غلاموں کی خریداری مؤکل کی غرض کے موافق ہے اسلئے یہ خریداری جائز ہوگی۔ اور موکل پر نافذ ہوگی۔
Book of Agency. The author of Hidayah said: Sometimes it is not possible to buy both slaves together. Therefore, if the agent bought one slave, the purchase is binding on the principal. However, if the agent bought a slave with gross fraud (ghabn fahish), then this purchase is not valid; i.e., the agent will be responsible and the principal will not be responsible. The proof is that this is tawkeel bil-shira' (agency to purchase), and tawkeel bil-shira' by consensus does not bear gross fraud; i.e., the agent for purchase is not permitted to purchase with gross fraud. So when the agent for purchase is not permitted to purchase with gross fraud, if he does so, because it is against the principal's command, the purchase is not binding on the principal but on the agent. The author of Hidayah said that this entire issue is by consensus. Ibn al-Humam said that the author of Hidayah restricted it to tawkeel bil-shira' because in the case of tawkeel bil-bay' (agency to sell), if the agent sold with gross fraud, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, that sale is permissible. For example, if someone appointed an agent to sell a slave whose price was 200, but the agent sold it for 300, according to Imam Abu Hanifa this is permissible and the sale is for the principal, not for the agent. [Question]: The principal told the agent to buy both (slaves) for 1000, and their values are equal. If the agent bought one for 500 or less, is the purchase binding on the principal or not? [Arabic]: 'And if he commanded him to buy them both for one thousand, and their value is equal, then according to Abu Hanifa, if he bought one of them for five hundred or less, it is permissible. But if he bought for more, it is not binding on the commander, because he allocated the thousand to both, and their value is equal, so it is divided between them in halves by indication (dalala). So it is as if he commanded the purchase of each one for five hundred. Then purchasing for that amount is compliance, and purchasing for less is a beneficial deviation, and purchasing for more is a harmful deviation, whether the increase is small or large; it is not permissible unless he buys the remaining with the remainder of the thousand before they dispute, by istihsan, because the purchase of the first is still in place, and his expressed objective—which is acquiring both slaves for one thousand—has been achieved. The division is only established by indication, and the explicit (sarih) overrides it.' [Urdu translation:] Translation: And if the principal commanded the agent to buy these two slaves for one thousand rupees and their price is equal, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, if he bought one of them for five hundred rupees or less, it is valid. And if he bought for more, this purchase is not binding on the principal. Because the principal stated one thousand for both and their price is equal, so one thousand will be divided between them half and half by indication. So it is as if the principal commanded the purchase of each one for five hundred rupees. Then purchasing for five hundred is compliance, purchasing for less than five hundred is a deviation towards good, and purchasing for more than five hundred is a deviation towards evil, whether the increase is small or large; it is not permissible unless he buys the remaining slave with the remainder of the thousand before a dispute arises, then it is permissible by istihsan. Because the first purchase is still in effect, and the principal's expressly stated objective—which is to buy both for one thousand—has been achieved. The division is only established by indication, and the explicit overrides the indication. Explanation of the case: If a person appointed another as agent to buy two slaves of equal value for one thousand rupees, then Imam Abu Hanifa said: If the agent bought one of them for five hundred rupees or less, this purchase is valid and binding on the principal. But if he bought for more than five hundred, whether the excess is small or large, the purchase is not binding on the principal; rather, it is binding on the agent. The proof is that the principal set one thousand as the price for both slaves, and their values are equal, so by indication it is established that one thousand will be divided between them equally; as if the principal appointed the agent to buy each slave for five hundred rupees. So if the agent bought one for five hundred, it exactly matches the principal's command, so it is valid and binding. If he bought it for less, there is deviation from the command but it benefits the principal, so it is also valid and binding. But if he bought it for more, there is deviation and harm, so it is not valid for the principal; the agent is responsible. However, if the agent bought one for more, e.g., six hundred, and then before any dispute arises between agent and principal, the agent bought the second slave for the remaining four hundred, then this purchase is also valid by istihsan and binding on the principal, even though qiyas would require that it not be binding because there is still deviation. According to qiyas, Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad hold that view. The reason for istihsan is that the first purchase of the slave for six hundred is still in effect, its state has not changed by dispute. Then when the agent bought the second for four hundred, the principal's objective which he explicitly stated—that both slaves be bought for one thousand—is achieved. The equal division of one thousand over the two slaves is only established by indication from the principal's speech. The conclusion is that the principal's explicit statement is that both slaves be acquired for one thousand, and by indication it is known that he set each slave's price at five hundred. The rule is that if acting upon the explicit statement is possible, the explicit overrides the indication; i.e., when explicitness exists and acting upon it is possible, the indication becomes void and is not considered. Therefore, since here the purchase of both slaves aligns with the principal's objective, this purchase is valid and binding on the principal.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses the ruling when a principal instructs an agent to purchase two slaves of equal value for a single price of 1000. It initially addresses a general issue of ghabn fahish (gross fraud) in agency for purchase, stating by consensus that an agent for purchase cannot commit gross fraud; if he does, the purchase is on the agent, not the principal. Then it moves to a specific case: the principal commands the agent to buy both slaves for 1000, and their values are equal. Abu Hanifa's ruling is presented: if the agent buys one slave for 500 or less, the purchase is valid and binding on the principal. If he buys for more than 500, it is initially not binding. However, if the agent subsequently buys the second slave with the remainder of the 1000 before any dispute arises, then by istihsan (juristic preference), the purchase becomes binding on the principal. The proof is that the principal's explicit objective—to acquire both slaves for 1000—is achieved. The implied division of 500 per slave is only by indication (dalala), and the explicit (sarih) overrides the indication. The text contrasts this with qiyas (analogy), which would deem the purchase invalid, and notes that Imam Malik, Shafi'i, and Ahmad follow qiyas. The commentary emphasizes the Hanafi principle that explicit commands take precedence over implied meanings when both can be fulfilled. The istihsan is based on the preservation of the principal's expressed purpose and the continuity of the first purchase. This lesson is a clear example of how Hanafi fiqh uses istihsan to achieve practical justice over strict analogy.

Key Terms
توکیل بالشراء (tawkeel bil-shira'): Agency to purchase, where the principal authorizes the agent to buy a specific item for him.
غبن فاحش (ghabn fahish): Gross fraud or excessive price difference, where the purchase price significantly exceeds the market value (usually determined by custom).
دلالة (dalala): Indication or implied meaning derived from the context or circumstances, as opposed to explicit (sarih) statement.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; setting aside a strict analogy (qiyas) in favor of a more equitable ruling based on a stronger evidence or custom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if an agent is instructed to buy two slaves of equal value for 1000, and the agent buys one slave for 600, then before any dispute buys the second slave for 400, what is the ruling?
A) The purchase is not binding on the principal because the first purchase exceeded 500.
B) The purchase is binding on the principal by istihsan.
C) The purchase is binding only on the agent.
D) The purchase is void and must be returned.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when an agent's purchase exceeds the implied half of a total price, it becomes binding on the principal if the total objective is achieved before any dispute, by virtue of istihsan prioritizing the explicit command over implied meaning.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
Specification of Dirhams and Dinars in Agency: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on specification of currency in agency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether dirhams and dinars become specified (mut'ayyan) by verbal designation in an agency for purchase using a debt, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) between the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
In agency for purchase using a debt, Imam Abu Hanifa holds that currency is not specified; the Sahibayn hold it is, affecting who bears the loss.

In this passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah, we encounter a classic intra-Hanafi dispute. When a creditor instructs his debtor to use the owed debt as the price for purchasing an item, is the purchase immediately binding on the creditor upon the debtor's purchase, or only after the creditor himself takes possession? The answer hinges on whether dirhams and dinars become 'specified' (mut'ayyan) by merely naming them. We will explore the proofs of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and the later scholarly discussion on the effect of physically handing over the currency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Issue
Understand the factual scenario: a creditor (principal) instructs his debtor (agent) to use the debt owed to purchase an item (e.g., a slave). The dispute is whether the purchase binds the principal before he takes possession of the purchased item. This depends on whether the dirhams/dinars are considered 'specified' (mut'ayyan) by verbally naming them as the price.
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's Position
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that dirhams and dinars are not specified by mere verbal designation in commutative contracts. Therefore, the purchase is not binding on the principal until he actually takes possession of the purchased item. If the item is destroyed in the agent's hands before that, the loss is the agent's (the debt remains due).
3
State the Sahibayn's Position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that dirhams and dinars are never specified by designation in commutative contracts, but the agent's possession is legally equivalent to the principal's. Therefore, once the agent takes possession of the purchased item, it is binding on the principal immediately. If destroyed, the loss falls on the principal (the debt is discharged).
4
Analyze the Proofs
Examine the dalil: Imam Abu Hanifa uses qiyas on a purchase contract (dirhams are not specified until handed over to the seller) and a consensus example (showing dirhams without handing them over does not specify). The Sahibayn use the witness-Khalid example to show that dirhams are never specified, and they analogize to the case of instructing the debtor to give the debt as charity.
Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is based on qiyas jaliy (clear analogy).
5
Identify the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence is who bears the loss if the purchased item is destroyed in the agent's hands before the principal takes possession. Under Abu Hanifa, the agent loses the debt; under the Sahibayn, the principal loses the purchased item.
6
Note the Later Mashayikh Ikhtilaf
If the principal physically hands the currency to the agent, later scholars differed: some say the currency becomes specified (voiding agency if destroyed), but the majority (aammat al-masha'ikh) hold it does not become specified, aligning with Abu Hanifa's principle.
This secondary ikhtilaf expands the dispute to the effect of delivery.

كتاب الوكالة

سے دس من گندم کی بیع سلم کر لے یا ان ایک ہزار درہم کے عوض بیچ صرف کرلے تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک مسلم فیہ اور بدل صرف پر قرض خواہ (مؤکل) نے قبضہ نہ کیا ہو بلکہ قرضدار (وکیل) کے قبضہ میں ہلاک ہو گئے ہوں تو یہ وکیل (قرضدار) کا مال ہلاک ہو گا اور موکل (قرض خواہ) نے مسلم فیہ اور بدل صرف پر قبضہ کر لیا ہو تو یہ مؤکل (قرض خواہ) کا مال ہو گیا اب اگر یہ ہلاک ہوا تو موکل کا مال ہلاک ہو گا۔ اور وکیل قرضہ سے سبکدوش ہو جائے گا۔
اور صاحبین کے نزدیک مسلم فیہ اور بدل صرف پراگر وکیل (قرضدار) نے قبضہ کر لیا ہوتو وہ موکل کے ذمہ لازم ہوگا خواہ موکل کے قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے وکیل (قرضدار) کے قبضہ میں ہلاک ہو جائے۔ لیکن یہ اختلاف اس صورت میں ہے جبکہ قرض خواہ نے مسلم الیہ کو اور اس شخص کو جس کے ساتھ عقد صرف کرنے کا حکم دیا ہے متعین نہ کیا ہو۔ چنانچہ اگر قرض خواہ نے ان کو متعین کر دیا ہو تو یہ تو کیل بالا تفاق صحیح ہے اور قرضدار (وکیل) کی خریداری، متوکل (قرض خواہ) پر لازم ہوگی۔ خواہ مؤکل مسلم فیہ اور بدل صرف پر قبضہ کرے یا موکل کے قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے وکیل (قرضدار) کے قبضہ میں ہلاک ہو جائے۔
صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ دراہم و دنانیر، بیع وغیرہ عقد معاوضہ میں متعین کرنے سے متعین نہیں ہوتے، دراہم و دنانیر خواہ دین یعنی کسی کے ذمہ میں ثابت ہوں خواہ عین ہوں یعنی کسی کے ذمہ میں ثابت نہ ہوں بلکہ عقد کرنے والے کے پاس موجود ہوں۔ چنانچہ اگر شاہد نے کہا کہ میرے ایک ہزار درہم، خالد کے ذمہ قرضہ ہیں۔ پس خالد قرضدار نے قرضہ کے عوض اپنا مال عین مثلاً ایک سو دینار قرض خواہ کے ہاتھ فروخت کر دیئے۔ پھر دونوں میں اتفاق ہو گیا کہ شاہد کا خالد پر کوئی قرضہ نہیں تھا تو شاہد اور خالد کے درمیان مذکورہ عقد باطل نہیں ہوگا۔ بلکہ شاہد پر قرضہ کا مثل یعنی ایک ہزار دراہم واجب ہوں گے۔ ملاحظہ فرمائیے اگر دراہم و دنانیر متعین کرنے سے متعین ہو جاتے تو خالد کے ذمہ دین نہ ہونے پر اتفاق کرنے کی صورت میں مذکورہ عقد باطل ہو جاتا کیونکہ عقد میں جن دراہم کو بصورت دین متعین کیا تھا وہ باقی نہیں رہے حالانکہ یہاں عقد باطل نہیں ہوتا۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ دراہم و دنانیر دین ہوں یا عین ہوں، عقد معاوضہ میں متعین کرنے سے متعین نہیں ہوتے ہیں۔ اور جو چیز متعین کرنے سے متعین نہ ہوتی ہو اس میں اطلاق اور تقیید دونوں برابر ہیں۔ اطلاق کی صورت تو یہ ہے کہ قرض خواہ قرضدار سے یہ کہے کہ میرے واسطے ایک ہزار درہم کے عوض ایک غلام خرید کر لا اور اس ایک ہزار کو اس قرضہ کی طرف منسوب نہ کرے جو قرضہ قرضدار پر واجب ہے۔ اور تقیید کی صورت یہ ہے کہ اس ایک ہزار کو قرضہ کی طرف منسوب کرے مثلاً قرض خواہ یہ کہے کہ میرے لئے ایک غلام اس ایک ہزار کے عوض خرید کر لا جو ایک ہزار میرا تجھ پر واجب ہے۔ پس جب دراہم و دنانیر متعین کرنے سے متعین نہیں ہوتے اور جو چیز متعین کرنے سے متعین نہ ہوتی ہو اس میں اطلاق اور تقیید دونوں برابر ہیں تو قرض خواہ کا اپنے قرضدار کو یہ کہنا کہ تو میرے واسطے ایک غلام اس ایک ہزار درہم کے عوض خرید کر لا جو میرا تجھ پر ہے اور یہ کہنا کہ ایک ہزار درہم کے عوض خرید کر لا، دونوں برابر ہیں۔ اور قرض خواہ اگر یہ کہے کہ تو میرے لئے ایک ہزار درہم کے عوض ایک غلام خرید کر لا اور اس ایک ہزار کو قرضہ کی طرف منسوب نہ کرے تو یہ تو کیل بالا تفاق درست ہے۔ لہذا اگر ایک ہزار کو قرضہ کی طرف منسوب کر دیا تو اس صورت میں بھی توکیل درست ہوگی۔ اور جب اس صورت میں توکیل درست ہے تو وکیل یعنی قرضدار کی خریداری مؤکل یعنی قرض خواہ پر لازم ہوگی۔ پس اگر غلام، قرض خواہ (مؤکل) کے قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے وکیل (قرضدار) کے قبضہ میں مر گیا تو یہ موکل کے مال سے مرے گا۔ یعنی اس غلام کا مرنا مؤکل (قرض خواہ) کا نقصان شمار ہوگا نہ کہ وکیل کا کیونکہ وکیل کا قبضہ، مؤکل کے قبضہ کے مرتبہ میں ہوتا ہے یعنی وکیل کے قبضہ میں غلام کا مرنا ایسا ہے جیسا کہ موکل کے قبضہ میں مرا ہو اور موکل کے قبضہ میں مرنے کی صورت میں موکل ہی کا نقصان شمار ہوگا نہ کہ وکیل کا۔ اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ قرض خواہ قرضدار سے یہ کہے کہ میرا قرضہ جو تجھ پر ہے تو اسے مساکین پر صدقہ کر دے تو یہ جائز ہے اسی طرح اگر اس قرضہ کے عوض غلام خریدنے کا حکم دیا تو یہ بھی جائز ہوگا۔

حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل سے پہلے یہ ذہن نشین فرما لیجئے کہ وکالت میں دراہم و دنانیر جب تک مؤکل، وکیل کے سپرد نہیں کرتا اس وقت تک دراہم و دنانیر متعین کرنے کے باوجود بالاجماع متعین نہیں ہوتے۔ مثلاً شاہد نے حامد کو وکیل مقرر کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ تو میرے لئے ان ایک ہزار دراہم کے عوض ایک باندی خرید کر لا۔ اور مؤکل (شاہد) نے وہ ایک ہزار دراہم وکیل (خالد) کو دکھلا کر متعین بھی کر دیے لیکن وکیل کے سپرد نہیں کئے تو اب اگر یہ دراہم موکل کے قبضہ سے چوری ہو گئے اور وکیل نے ایک ہزار دراہم کے عوض سپرد نہیں کئے اور باندی خرید لی تو یہ خریداری موکل پر لازم ہوگی۔ اور مؤکل، دوسرے ایک ہزار دراہم وکیل کو ادا کرے گا۔ اس مسئلہ سے ثابت ہوا کہ وکالت میں وکیل کے حوالہ کرنے سے پہلے دراہم و دنانیر متعین کرنے کے باوجود متعین نہیں ہوتے۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں اگر دراہم و دنانیر متعین کرنے سے متعین ہو جاتے تو دراہم متعینہ چوری ہونے کے بعد وکالت باطل ہو جاتی، حالانکہ اس صورت میں وکالت باطل نہیں ہوتی۔ پس دراہم متعینہ کے چوری ہونے کے بعد دوسرے دراہم کے عوض وکالت کا باقی رہنا اور باطل نہ ہونا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ تسلیم الی الوکیل سے پہلے وکالت کے اندر دراہم و دنانیر متعین کرنے کے باوجود متعین نہیں ہوتے۔ اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وکالت چونکہ عقد شراء کا وسیلہ اور ذریعہ ہے اسلئے وکالت کو عقد شراء پر قیاس کیا جائے گا اور عقد شراء میں مشتری کی طرف سپرد کرنے سے پہلے دراہم و دنانیر متعین کرنے سے متعین نہیں ہوتے ہیں۔ لہذا وکالت جو عقد شراء کا وسیلہ ہے اس میں بھی تسلیم الی الوکیل سے پہلے دراہم و دنانیر متعین کرنے سے متعین نہ ہوں گے۔

اور اگر مؤکل نے دراہم و دنانیر وکیل کے سپرد کر دیئے تو اس صورت میں اختلاف ہے۔ چنانچہ بعض حضرات مشائخ نے فرمایا کہ اس صورت میں دراہم و دنانیر متعین ہو جاتے ہیں حتی کہ اگر وکیل نے ان دراہم و دنانیر کو ہلاک کر دیا یا وہ ہلاک ہو گئے تو وکالت باطل ہو جائے گی۔ ان حضرات کی ایک دلیل یہ ہے کہ وکالت شراء کا وسیلہ ہے اور مشتری کی طرف سپرد کرنے کے بعد عقد شراء میں دراہم و دنانیر متعین ہو جاتے ہیں۔ لہذا وکالت جو شراء کا وسیلہ ہے تسلیم الی الوکیل کے بعد دراہم و دنانیر اس میں بھی متعین ہو جائیں گے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ دراہم و دنانیر پر وکیل کا قبضہ، قبضہ امانت ہے اور امانتوں میں دراہم و دنانیر متعین ہوتے ہیں۔ لہذا تسلیم الی الوکیل کے بعد وکالت میں بھی دراہم و دنانیر متعین ہو جائیں گے۔ اور عامتہ المشائخ کا قول یہ ہے کہ وکیل کے سپرد کرنے کے بعد بھی دراہم و دنانیر متعین نہیں ہوتے۔ دوسری بات یہ ذہن نشین فرما لیں کہ حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل کی بنیاد بعض مشائخ کے قول پر ہے نہ کہ عامتہ المشائخ کے قول پر۔ لیکن اس پر یہ سوال ہوگا کہ حضرت امام صاحب کے قول کو ان بعض مشائخ کے قول سے ثابت کیا گیا ہے جو امام صاحب کے دو سو سال بعد
Book of Agency: If someone instructs his debtor to buy ten mans of wheat via salam sale or to exchange for one thousand dirhams, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, if the creditor (principal) has not taken possession of the muslam fih and the exchange currency, and they are destroyed in the hands of the debtor (agent), then it is the agent's loss. If the principal has taken possession, it becomes the principal's property, and if destroyed, it is his loss, and the agent is discharged from the debt. According to the Sahibayn, if the agent takes possession, it becomes binding on the principal even if destroyed before the principal takes possession. This difference applies only when the principal did not specify the party to receive the salam goods and the person with whom the currency exchange contract is made. If specified, there is consensus that the purchase is binding on the principal regardless of possession. The Sahibayn's proof: Dirhams and dinars are not specified by designation in commutative contracts, whether they are a debt (dayn) owed by someone or an actual property (ayn) in hand. For example, if a witness says, 'I have a debt of one thousand dirhams owed by Khalid,' then Khalid sells his own property (e.g., one hundred dinars) to the witness in exchange for that debt, and later they agree that no debt existed, the contract is not void; rather, the witness must pay the equivalent of one thousand dirhams. If dirhams and dinars were specified by designation, the contract would become void when the debt is found to be non-existent, but it does not. So they are not specified. Therefore, specifying or not specifying makes no difference. So if the principal says 'buy a slave with the thousand dirhams you owe me' or just 'with a thousand dirhams,' both are valid, and the purchase is binding. If the slave dies in the agent's hands before the principal takes possession, it is the principal's loss because the agent's possession is like the principal's possession. This is similar to instructing the debtor to give the debt to the poor.

Before presenting Imam Abu Hanifa's proof, note: In agency, until the principal hands over the dirhams/dinars to the agent, they are not specified by designation by consensus. Example: Shahid appoints Hamid as agent to buy a slave girl with these one thousand dirhams, shows them but does not hand them over; if the dirhams are stolen and the agent buys using other dirhams, the purchase is binding and the principal must pay the agent another thousand. This proves they are not specified before delivery. The reason is that agency is a means to a purchase contract, so it is analogized to a purchase contract, where dirhams/dinars are not specified until handed over to the seller. Hence, in agency they are not specified before delivery to the agent.

If the principal does hand them over, there is ikhtilaf. Some mashayikh said they become specified, so if the agent destroys them or they are destroyed, the agency becomes void. Their proof: Agency is a means to purchase, and after handing over in purchase, they become specified; also, the agent's possession is a trust (amanah), and dirhams/dinars are specified in trusts. The majority of mashayikh (aammat al-masha'ikh) say they do not become specified even after delivery. Note that Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is based on the view of some mashayikh, not the majority. But there is an objection that his proof is established by those later scholars two hundred years after him.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah deals with a specific issue in the Book of Agency (Kitab al-Wakalah): when a creditor (principal) instructs his debtor (agent) to use the debt owed as consideration to purchase something, or to conduct a currency exchange (sarf) using that debt. The passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), followed by a later disagreement among the mashayikh regarding the effect of physically handing over the currency to the agent.

First, the ruling: If the debtor/agent buys something using the debt (i.e., without transferring actual dirhams), and the purchased item or exchange currency is destroyed, Imam Abu Hanifa rules that the loss falls on the agent if the principal has not taken possession, but on the principal if he has. The Sahibayn hold that the agent's possession is equivalent to the principal's, so the purchase becomes binding on the principal immediately upon the agent taking possession, regardless of whether the principal later takes possession. This difference only applies when the principal did not specify the exact counterparty to the salam or sarf contract; if he did, all agree the purchase is binding.

The Sahibayn support their view by arguing that dirhams and dinars are never 'specified' (mut'ayyan) by mere verbal designation in commutative contracts like sale or currency exchange. They illustrate this with an example: if a witness claims a debt from Khalid, then Khalid sells his own property to the witness in exchange for that debt, and later they agree no debt existed, the contract is not void; instead, the witness must pay the equivalent value. If dirhams were specified by designation, the contract would be void because the specific debt disappeared, but it remains valid. Hence, dirhams/dinars are not specified, so there is no difference between the principal saying 'buy with the thousand you owe me' and 'buy with a thousand dirhams'—both are binding on the principal. Consequently, if the slave dies in the agent's hands before the principal takes possession, it is the principal's loss because the agent's possession is like the principal's in this context.

Following that, the passage presents Imam Abu Hanifa's proof, which is based on the idea that until the currency is physically handed over to the agent, it is not specified by consensus. An example is given: if the principal shows the agent specific dirhams but does not give them, and those dirhams are stolen, the agency remains valid and the agent can buy with other dirhams, making the purchase binding on the principal. This demonstrates that mere designation without delivery does not specify. The reasoning is based on qiyas (analogical reasoning): agency is a means to a purchase, so it follows the same rules as purchase. In a purchase, dirhams/dinars are not specified until handed over to the seller. Therefore, in agency, they are not specified until handed over to the agent.

Finally, the text discusses what happens if the principal does hand over the currency to the agent. There is an ikhtilaf among later scholars. Some mashayikh argue that after delivery, the dirhams become specified, so if they are destroyed, the agency becomes void. They analogize to purchase (where after delivery to the seller, they are specified) and to trusts (where dirhams are considered specified in the hands of a trustee). However, the majority of mashayikh (aammat al-masha'ikh) hold that even after delivery, they do not become specified; the agency remains valid and the agent can substitute other dirhams. The text notes that Imam Abu Hanifa's proof relies on the view of some mashayikh, not the majority, which raises a chronological question since those mashayikh lived two centuries later.

Key Terms
وکالت (wakalah): Agency; a contract where one person (principal) authorizes another (agent) to perform a legal act on his behalf.
مت عین (mut'ayyan): Specified or individualized; in this context, whether dirhams and dinars become specifically identified and inseparable from the contract when verbally designated.
عقد معاوضہ (aqd mu'awada): Commutative contract; a contract where each party gives and receives something of value, such as sale, currency exchange, etc.
تسلیم (taslim): Delivery or handover; the act of giving possession of something to another person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), if a creditor instructs his debtor to use the debt to buy a slave and the debtor does so, but the slave dies before the creditor takes possession, who bears the loss?
A) The debtor (agent) bears the loss because the purchase was not binding on the creditor.
B) The creditor (principal) bears the loss because the agent's possession is like the principal's and the purchase was binding.
C) The loss is shared equally between them.
D) The sale is void, so no loss arises.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the specification of currency in agency turns on whether delivery has occurred; mere verbal designation is insufficient for binding the principal before possession, and this dispute has a clear thamarah al-khilaf in liability for loss.

Specification of Currency in Agency: Delivery vs. Designation
Hanafi legal reasoning on when dirhams/dinars become specified in agency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on when dirhams/dinars become specified in wakalah and apply it to determine whether an agency remains valid after destruction of the currency.

Core Idea
In Hanafi wakalah, dirhams/dinars are not specified by mere designation; only physical delivery to the agent triggers specification.

This lesson examines a key issue in Hanafi agency law: whether designating a specific sum of money in a purchase agency makes that sum legally specified so that its loss voids the agency. The passage uses qiyas on sale, intra-madhhab disagreement, and a defense of the relied-upon view that specification occurs only after delivery. Understanding this distinction is crucial for determining the validity of agency contracts when the designated currency is lost or destroyed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is designating dirhams/dinars in a wakalah contract for purchase. The ruling is whether such designation causes legal specification (ta'yin).
Specification means the currency becomes uniquely tied to the agency; its loss voids the agency.
2
Locate the default rule before delivery
The passage states that before handing over the currency, even if explicitly designated, it does not become specified. This is proven by an example: if the designated sum is stolen, the agency remains valid and the principal must provide other funds.
The rule is established by consensus (bilā jima').
3
Trace the qiyas on sale
Agency is analogized to a contract of sale because agency is a means to a purchase. In sale, the price becomes specified only after delivery to the seller. Therefore, in agency, specification requires delivery to the agent.
The illa (effective cause) is that both involve transfer of price obligation.
4
Analyze the dispute after delivery
After the agent receives the currency, there is ikhtilāf. Some later mashāyikh (supported by a narration from Imam Muhammad) hold that specification occurs. The majority hold it does not. The passage defends the former as the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view.
The defense relies on Imam Muhammad's Ziyādāt, tracing the view to Abu Hanifa.
5
Apply the ruling to the creditor-debtor example
The passage concludes that a creditor ordering a debtor to buy a slave with the debt is invalid because the creditor cannot make the seller the owner of the debt without being able to hand over the specific currency.
This illustrates the practical consequence of specification: inability to transfer ownership of a non-specified debt.

كتاب الوكالة

کہ وکیل کا کیونکہ وکیل کا قبضہ، مؤکل کے قبضہ کے مرتبہ میں ہوتا ہے یعنی وکیل کے قبضہ میں غلام کا مرنا ایسا ہے۔ جیسا کہ موکل کے قبضہ میں مرا ہو اور موکل کے قبضہ میں مرنے کی صورت میں موکل ہی کا نقصان شمار ہوگا نہ کہ وکیل کا اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ قرض خواہ قرضدار سے یہ کہے کہ میرا قرضہ جو تجھ پر ہے تو اسے مساکین پر صدقہ کر دے تو یہ جائز ہے اسی طرح اگر اس قرضہ کے عوض غلام خریدنے کا حکم دیا تو یہ بھی جائز ہوگا۔

حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل سے پہلے یہ ذہن نشین فرما لیجئے کہ وکالت میں دراہم ودنا نیر جب تک مؤکل ، وکیل کے سپردنہیں کرتا اس وقت تک در اہم ود نا نیر متعین کرنے کے باوجود بالا جماع متعین نہیں ہوتے مثلاً شاہد نے حامد کو وکیل مقرر کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ تو میرے لئے ان ایک ہزار دراہم کے عوض ایک باندی خرید کر لا۔ اور مؤکل (شاہد ) نے وہ ایک ہزار دراہم وکیل ( خالد ) کو دکھلا کر متعین بھی کر دیے لیکن وکیل کے سپرد نہیں کئے تو اب اگر یہ در اہم موکل کے قبضہ سے چوری ہو گئے اور وکیل نے ایک ہزار دراہم کے عوض سپردنہیں کریہ اور باندی خرید لی تو یہ خریداری موکل پر لازم ہوگی۔ اور مؤکل ، دوسرے ایک ہزار دراہم وکیل کو ادا کرے گا۔ اس مسئلہ سے ثابت ہوا کہ وکالت میں وکیل کے حوالہ کرنے سے پہلے دراہم ودن نیر متعین کرنے کے باوجود متعین نہیں ہوتے۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں اگر در اہم و دنا نیر متعین کرنے سے متعین ہو جاتے تو دراہم متعینہ چوری ہونے کے بعد وکالت باطل ہو جاتی ۔ حالانکہ اس صورت میں وکالت باطل نہیں ہوتی ۔ پس درا ہم متعینہ کے چوری ہونے کے بعد دوسرے دراہم کے عوض وکالت کا باقی رہنا اور باطل نہ ہونا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ تسلیم الی الوکیل سے پہلے وکالت کے اندر در اہم و نانی متعین کرنے کے باوجود متعین نہیں ہوتے ۔ اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وکالت چونکہ عقد شراء کا وسیلہ اور ذریعہ ہے اسلئے وکالت کو عقد شراء پر قیاس کیا جائے گا اور عقد شراء میں مشتری کی طرف سپرد کرنے سے پہلے در اہم ود نا نیر متعین کرنے سے متعین نہیں ہوتے ہیں۔ لہذا وکالت جو عقد شراء کا وسیلہ ہے اس میں بھی تسلیم ودنا الی الوکیل سے پہلے درہم ودنا نیر متعین کرنے سے متعین نہ ہوں گے۔

اور اگر مؤکل نے دراہم ودنا نیر وکیل کے سپر د کر دیئے تو اس صورت میں اختلاف ہے۔ چنانچہ بعض حضرات مشائخ نے فرمایا کہ اس صورت میں دراہم ودنا نیر متعین ہو جاتے ہیں حتی کہ اگر وکیل نے ان در اہم ودنا نیر کو ہلاک کر دیا یا وہ ہلاک ہو گئے تو وکالت باطل ہو جائے گی۔ ان حضرات کی ایک دلیل یہ ہے کہ وکالت شراء کا وسیلہ ہے اور مشتری کی طرف سپرد کرنے کے بعد عقد شراء میں درا ہم و دنا نیر متعین ہو جاتے ہیں۔ لہذا وکالت جو شراء کا وسیلہ ہے تسلیم الی الوکیل کے بعد درا ہم ودنا نیر اس میں بھی متعین ہو جائیں گے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ در اہم ودنا نیر پر وکیل کا قبضہ، قبضہ امانت ہے اور امانتوں میں دراہم ودنانیر متعین ہوتے ہیں۔ لہذا تسلیم الی الوکیل کے بعد وکالت میں بھی در اہم و دنا غیر متعین ہو جائیں گے۔ اور عامتہ المشائخ کا قول یہ ہے کہ وکیل کے سپرد کرنے کے بعد بھی درا ہم ود تا نیر متعین نہیں ہوتے ۔ دوسری بات یہ ذہن نشین فرمالیں کہ حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل کی بنیاد بعض مشائخ کے قول پر ہے نہ کہ عامتہ المشائخ کے قول پر ۔ لیکن اس پر یہ سوال ہوگا کہ حضرت امام صاحب کے قول کو ان بعض مشائخ کے قول سے ثابت کیا گیا ہے جو امام صاحب کے دو سو سال بعد پیدا ہوئے ہیں۔ حالانکہ یہ قطعا ممکن نہیں ہے۔ جیسا کہ یہود کہتے تھے کہ حضرت ابراہیم یہودی تھے اور نصاریٰ کہتے تھے کہ حضرت ابراہیم نصرانی تھے ۔ مگر قرآن مجید میں کہا گیا ہے کہ حضرت ابراہیم کا زمانہ یہودیت اور نصرانیت کے وجود سے ہزاروں سال پہلے ہے۔ پس یہودیت اور نصرانیت کے وجود سے ہزاروں سال پہلے پیدا ہونے والے انسان (ابراہیم ) کو یہودی اور نصرانی قرار دینا اعلیٰ درجہ کی حماقت ہے۔ اسی طرح امام صاحب کے قول کو ان بعض مشائخ کے قول سے ثابت کرنا جو امام صاحب سے دو سو سال بعد پیدا ہوئے ہیں بہت بڑی حماقت ہے۔

اس کا جواب یہ ہے صاحب ہدایہ ان بعض مشائخ نے قول کے در پے نہیں ہیں۔ بلکہ صاحب ہدایہ نے اس پر اعتماد کیا ہے جو امام محمد سے زیادات میں منقول ہے کہ درا ہم و دنا تیر تسلیم الی الوکیل کے بعد متعین ہو جاتے ہیں ۔ اور امام محمد سے جو کچھ منقول ہے وہ سب حضرت امام صاحب ہی کا فرمودہ ہے۔ یہ اتفاقی امر ہے کہ امام محمد سے جو منقول ہے وہ بعض مشائخ کا بھی قول ہے اس جواب کے بعد یہ کہنا درست نہ ہوگا کہ امام صاحب کے قول کی دلیل کی بنیاد بعض مشائخ کا قول ہے۔

دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ وکالت میں تسلیم الی الوکیل کے بعد در اہم ودنا نیر کا متعین ہوتا یہ ان بعض مشائخ کا قول نہیں ہے۔ جو حضرت امام صاحب کے دوسوسال بعد پیدا ہوئے ہیں بلکہ ان بعض مشائخ نے امام ابو حنیفہ کی اصل سے اس کی تخریج کی ہے۔ اب مطلب یہ ہو گا کہ صاحب ہدایہ نے امام صاحب کے قبول کو امام صاحب کی اصل سے بعض مشائخ کی تخریج پر ثابت کیا ہے۔ یعنی امام صاحب کے قول کی دلیل کی بنیاد خود امام صاحب کی بیان کردہ اصل ہے لیکن اس کی تخریج بعض مشائخ نے کی ہے۔ اس جواب کے بعد بھی سابقہ اشکال واقع نہ ہوگا۔ (فتح القدير )

اب اصل مسئلہ پر امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ وکالتوں میں در اہم ودنا نیر وکیل کی طرف سپرد کرنے کے بعد متعین ہو جاتے ہیں۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر مؤکل نے دراہم ودنا نیر میں عین دراہم کے ساتھ وکالت کو مقید کر دیا۔ یعنی موکل کے ہاتھ میں دراہم لے کر وکیل کو دکھلا دیے اور اس کے سپرد کر دیئے یا وکالت کو درا ہم ودنا نیر میں سے دین کے ساتھ مقید کیا یعنی یہ کہا کہ جو درا ہم یا دنانیر میرے تجھ پر نہیں ان کے عوض غلام خرید کر دے جیسا کہ متن کا مسئلہ ہے پھر عین درا ہم کو موکل یا وکیل نے ہلاک کر دیا، یا مؤکل نے وکیل کو دین اور قرضہ سے بری کر دیا تو یہ وکالت باطل ہو جائیگی ۔ پس در اہم ودنا نیر کو ہلاک کرنے کی وجہ سے وکالت کا باطل ہونا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ وکالت میں در اہم و دنا نیر متعین ہوتے ہیں۔ کیونکہ اگر در اہم ودنا نیر متعین نہ ہوتے تو وکالت باطل نہ ہوتی مگر مؤکل کے دراہم دنانی و رنانی ہلاک کرنے کی صورت میں موکل پر دوسرے درا ہم ادا کرنا لازم ہوتا اور وکیل کے ہلاک کرنے کی صورت میں وکیل ذمہ دار ہوتا۔ بہر حال یہ ثابت ہو گیا کہ تسلیم الی الوکیل کے بعد دراہم ودنا غیر متعین ہو جاتے ہیں۔ پس جب وکالت میں دراہم ودنا نیر متعین ہو جاتے ہیں تو متن کے مسئلہ کے مطابق قرض خواہ کا قرضدار کو یہ حکم دینا کہ میرا جو تجھ پر قرضہ ہے اس کے عوض ایک غلام خرید کر دے اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ قرض خواہ نے قرضدار کے علاوہ کو یعنی غلام کے مالک کو قرضہ کی اس رقم کا مالک کر دیا ہے۔ حالانکہ قرض خواہ نے غلام کے مالک کو اس قرضہ پر قبضہ کرنے کا وکیل مقرر نہیں کیا ہے۔ اور اس طور پر کہ غلام کے مالک کو قرضہ کی رقم کا مالک بنانا نا جائز ہے اور یہ اسلئے نا جائز ہے کہ قرض خواہ جس نے غلام کے مالک کو قرضدار کے ذمہ واجب شدہ رقم کا مالک کیا ہے۔ وہ قرضہ کی اس رقم کو غلام کے مالک کی طرف سپرد کرنے پر قادر نہیں ہے اور انسان جو سپر ذکرنے پر قادر نہ ہو وہ اس چیز کو دوسرے کی ملکیت میں دینے کا مجاز بھی نہیں ہوتا
Book of Agency. Because the agent's possession is in the rank of the principal's possession, meaning the death of a slave in the agent's possession is like the death in the principal's possession. In case of death in the principal's possession, the loss is counted on the principal, not the agent. This is like a creditor saying to a debtor: 'Give my debt that is upon you as charity to the poor' – this is permissible. Similarly, if he ordered him to buy a slave with this debt, this is also permissible. Before the proof of Imam Abu Hanifa, understand that in agency, dirhams and dinars, as long as the principal does not hand them over to the agent, even if they are designated, they are not specified by consensus. For example, Shahid appointed Hamid as agent saying: 'Buy a slave-girl for me in exchange for this thousand dirhams.' And the principal (Shahid) showed the thousand dirhams to the agent (Khalid) and designated them, but did not hand them over. Then if these dirhams were stolen from the principal's possession, and the agent bought the slave-girl without having been handed the dirhams, this purchase is binding on the principal, and the principal will pay another thousand dirhams to the agent. This proves that in agency, before handing over, dirhams and dinars do not become specified despite designation. Because if they became specified by designation, then after the designated dirhams were stolen, the agency would be void. But in this case, the agency is not void. So the agency remaining valid with other dirhams after the designated ones were stolen is proof that before delivery to the agent, dirhams and dinars do not become specified despite designation. Its proof is that agency is a means and instrument of the contract of purchase, so agency is analogized to the contract of purchase. In the contract of purchase, before handing over to the buyer, dirhams and dinars do not become specified by designation. Therefore, in agency, which is a means of purchase, before delivery to the agent, dirhams and dinars also will not become specified by designation. And if the principal handed over the dirhams and dinars to the agent, then there is disagreement. Some mashayikh said that in this case dirhams and dinars become specified, so much so that if the agent destroyed them or they perished, the agency becomes void. One proof of these is that agency is a means of purchase, and after handing over to the buyer, dirhams and dinars become specified in the contract of purchase. Hence, in agency, after delivery to the agent, dirhams and dinars will also become specified. A second proof is that the agent's possession of dirhams and dinars is a trust possession, and in trusts, dirhams and dinars are specified. So after delivery to the agent, in agency, dirhams and dinars will become specified. And the statement of the majority of mashayikh is that even after handing over to the agent, dirhams and dinars do not become specified. Second, understand that the basis of Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is on the statement of some mashayikh, not on the statement of the majority. But upon this, the question arises that Imam Sahib's statement is proven by the statement of those some mashayikh who were born two hundred years after Imam Sahib, which is absolutely impossible. Just as the Jews said that Ibrahim was Jewish and the Christians said that Ibrahim was Christian, but the Quran says that Ibrahim's time was thousands of years before the existence of Judaism and Christianity. So calling Ibrahim, who was born thousands of years before Judaism and Christianity, a Jew or Christian is extreme foolishness. Similarly, proving Imam Sahib's statement from the statement of some mashayikh who were born two hundred years after Imam Sahib is great foolishness. The answer to this is that Sahib al-Hidayah is not following the statement of those mashayikh. Rather, Sahib al-Hidayah relied on what is narrated from Imam Muhammad in al-Ziyadat, that dirhams and dinars become specified after delivery to the agent. And whatever is narrated from Imam Muhammad is all from Imam Sahib. It is coincidental that what is narrated from Imam Muhammad is also the statement of some mashayikh. After this answer, it will not be correct to say that the basis of Imam Sahib's proof is the statement of some mashayikh. A second answer is that the specification of dirhams and dinars in agency after delivery is not the statement of those some mashayikh who were born two hundred years after Imam Sahib. Rather, those some mashayikh derived it from the principle of Imam Abu Hanifa. Now the meaning will be that Sahib al-Hidayah proved Imam Sahib's statement by the derivation of some mashayikh from Imam Sahib's principle. That is, the basis of Imam Sahib's proof is the principle stated by Imam Sahib himself, but its derivation was done by some mashayikh. After this answer, the previous objection will not arise. (Fath al-Qadir). Now, the summary of Imam Abu Hanifa's proof on the original issue is that in agencies, dirhams and dinars become specified after being handed over to the agent. This is why if the principal restricted the agency to specific dirhams and dinars – i.e., he took the dirhams in his hand, showed them to the agent, and handed them over, or he restricted the agency to a debt from among dirhams and dinars – i.e., he said: 'Buy a slave for me in exchange for the dirhams or dinars that are not upon you,' as in the text's issue – then if the principal or agent destroyed the specific dirhams, or the principal discharged the agent from the debt, then this agency becomes void. So the agency becoming void due to destruction of dirhams and dinars is proof that dirhams and dinars are specified in agency. Because if they were not specified, the agency would not become void. But in case the principal destroys them, it becomes obligatory upon the principal to pay other dirhams, and in case the agent destroys them, the agent is responsible. In any case, it is proven that after delivery to the agent, dirhams and dinars become specified. So when dirhams and dinars are specified in agency, then according to the issue in the text, a creditor commanding a debtor: 'Buy a slave with my debt that is upon you' means that the creditor made the owner of the slave (other than the debtor) the owner of that debt amount. But the creditor did not appoint the slave's owner as agent to take possession of that debt. And making the slave's owner the owner of the debt amount in this manner is impermissible. And it is impermissible because the creditor, who made the slave's owner the owner of the amount due from the debtor, is not able to hand over that debt amount to the slave's owner. And a person who is unable to hand over a thing is not authorized to give it into the ownership of another.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage is a detailed Hanafi legal reasoning (istidlal) on the specification (ta'yin) of dirhams and dinars in agency contracts (wakalah). The discussion revolves around whether the currency designated for a purchase becomes legally specified before or after actual delivery to the agent. The passage first establishes the default position: before handing over the dirhams/dinars to the agent, they do not become specified, even if explicitly designated. This is proven by an example: if the principal shows the agent a specific sum but does not deliver it, and that sum is stolen, the agency remains valid and the principal must provide other dirhams. This shows that the designated sum was not specified, otherwise the agency would have become void upon its loss. The reasoning is based on qiyas (analogy) with the contract of sale, where the price is not specified until actually delivered to the seller. Since agency is a means to a sale, it follows the same rule. Then the passage addresses the situation after delivery. There is ikhtilaf among Hanafi scholars. Some later mashayikh hold that after delivery, the dirhams/dinars become specified, so if the agent destroys them, the agency becomes void. They analogize to sale after delivery and to the nature of trust possession. The majority (ammat al-mashayikh) hold that even after delivery they do not become specified. The passage then defends Imam Abu Hanifa's view (which aligns with the first group) against criticism that it relies on later scholars. The response clarifies that the basis is actually a narration from Imam Muhammad in al-Ziyadat, which goes back to Imam Abu Hanifa himself. Alternatively, the later scholars derived (takhrij) the ruling from Imam Abu Hanifa's principles. Thus, Imam Abu Hanifa's view is authoritative (mufta bihi). Finally, the passage applies this to the text's example: a creditor asking a debtor to buy a slave with the debt is invalid because the creditor cannot make the slave's owner the owner of the debt without delivering it. This is because ownership transfer requires the ability to hand over the object, which is absent in the case of a debt owed by a third party. The passage concludes that the agency is void because the dirhams/dinars became specified upon delivery, but the creditor cannot transfer ownership without actual possession by the slave's owner.

Key Terms
وکالت (wakalah): A contract of agency where one party (principal) authorizes another (agent) to perform an act on their behalf, here specifically to purchase a commodity.
تعین (ta'yin): The legal specification of a particular currency (dirhams/dinars) such that its loss or destruction affects the validity of the agency or contract.
تسلیم الی الوکیل (taslim ila al-wakil): Handing over the dirhams/dinars physically to the agent, after which the agent's possession is that of a trustee (amanah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position in this passage, when do dirhams and dinars become specified in a wakalah contract?
A) Immediately upon being mentioned and shown to the agent
B) Only after the agent physically receives them
C) Never, even after receipt
D) Only after the purchase is complete

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi wakalah, dirhams/dinars become legally specified only upon physical delivery to the agent, making the agency void if they are subsequently destroyed.

Specification of Dirhams/Dinars in Agency and the Invalidity of Tamlik al-Dayn
Explaining the Hanafi ruling that dirhams and dinars become specified upon delivery to the agent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that dirhams/dinars become specified upon delivery to an agent and explain the rational proof (dalil aqli) that an agency to purchase with an unpaid debt is void.

Core Idea
Dirhams become specified upon delivery; their destruction voids the agency, proving specification.

In this passage from al-Hidayah, a key principle of Hanafi agency law is established: when coins are handed to an agent, they become identified as specific property, not just a generic debt. This has crucial consequences for the validity of an agency where a creditor instructs his debtor to buy something with the owed amount. Through a rational argument, the text demonstrates why such an agency is invalid and who bears the loss if the purchased item perishes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling and its immediate proof
The passage first states that dirhams/dinars become specified upon delivery to the agent. It then presents proof: if the principal restricts the agency to specific coins or if they are destroyed after delivery, the agency becomes void. If the coins were not specified, destruction would not void the agency; the principal would simply owe other coins.
This proof uses the consequence of destruction to establish specification.
2
Analyze the rational argument (dalil aqli) from al-Hidayah
The author argues that the agency described—a creditor commanding his debtor to buy a slave with the owed debt—necessarily entails either (a) tamlik al-dayn (making the debt owned by someone other than the debtor without authorization) or (b) commanding over something not owned. Both are impermissible, rendering the agency void.
Tamlik al-dayn without proper authorization is a key concept.
3
Determine the consequence of the invalid agency
Since the agency is void, the debtor's purchase is for himself. If the purchased item perishes before the creditor takes possession, the loss falls on the debtor (agent). However, if the creditor later physically takes the item, he may own it through a separate transaction (bay' al-ta'ati).
This illustrates the practical impact of the ruling.
4
Examine the commentary examples
Al-'Inayah and al-Kifayah provide additional scenarios illustrating tamlik al-dayn to someone other than the debtor. These confirm that such a transfer is impermissible without proper authorization for possession (wakalah bi al-qabd).
Commentaries reinforce the core principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوكالة

أصل المسألة: أن في الوكالات إذا سلمت الدراهم والدنانير إلى الوكيل تتعين. ولهذا لو قيد الموكل الوكالة بعين الدراهم مع الوكيل، أو أهلك الموكل أو الوكيل الدراهم بعد التسليم، بطلت الوكالة. فبطلان الوكالة بهلاك الدراهم دليل على تعينها. لأنها لو لم تتعين لما بطلت الوكالة، بل لزم الموكل أداء دراهم أخرى، أو ضمن الوكيل.

ثم قال صاحب الهداية: ومما يدل على ذلك أن المذكور في المسألة من التوكيل يلزم منه إما تمليك الدين من غير من عليه الدين من غير أن يوكله بقبضه، وهو لا يجوز، أو يلزم أن الموكل لم يقبض الدين بعد، بل أمر الغريم أن يدفع الثمن إلى البائع، وهذا أمر بما لا يملكه الموكل، لأن الدين لا يملك إلا بالقبض، لأن الأداء بالمثل لا بالعين.

فإذا هلكت الدراهم بعد التسليم إلى الوكيل بطلت الوكالة، فدل على أنها تتعين. ثم إذا تعلقت الوكالة بالدين، فإن الموكل لا يملك الدين إلا بالقبض، فإذا أمر الغريم أن يشتري به غلاما، فقد ملك الدين لغير من عليه الدين (أي للبائع) من غير أن يوكله بقبضه، وهو لا يجوز. وإذا لم يجز ذلك، لم تصح الوكالة. فإذا اشترى الوكيل الغلام وهلك في يده قبل قبض الموكل، كان من مال الوكيل، لأن الشراء له لا للموكل. لكن إذا قبضه الموكل ملكه ببيع التعاطي.

وذكر صاحب العناية صورة تمليك الدين من غير من عليه الدين: زيد له دين على عمرو، فقال زيد لبكر: وكلتك أن تشتري لي كتابا من رجل آخر بذلك الدين الذي لي على عمرو، فهذا لا يجوز لأن زيدا ملك الدين لبكر (الوكيل) وهو غير من عليه الدين. وذكر صاحب الكفاية صورة أخرى: زيد له دين على عمرو، فاشترى زيد من بكر كتابا بذلك الدين، فكأنه ملك الدين لبكر وهو غير من عليه الدين.
Book of Agency

The core of the issue: In agencies, when dirhams and dinars are handed over to the agent, they become specified. For this reason, if the principal restricts the agency to specific dirhams with the agent, or if the principal or agent destroys the dirhams after delivery, the agency becomes void. The invalidation of the agency by the destruction of the dirhams is proof of their specification. Because if they were not specified, the agency would not become void; rather, the principal would be obligated to pay other dirhams, or the agent would be liable.

Then the author of al-Hidayah said: Among the evidence for that is that the agency mentioned in the issue necessarily entails either making the debt owned by other than the debtor without authorizing him to take possession of it, which is impermissible, or it entails that the principal has not yet taken possession of the debt, but rather commands the debtor to pay the price to the seller, and this is a command regarding something the principal does not own, because a debt is not owned except by possession, since repayment is by like, not by specific item.

Thus, if the dirhams are destroyed after delivery to the agent, the agency becomes void, proving that they become specified. Then, if the agency is connected to a debt, the principal does not own the debt except by possession. So when he commands the debtor to buy a slave with it, he has made the debt owned by other than the debtor (i.e., the seller) without authorizing him to take possession, which is impermissible. And when that is impermissible, the agency is not valid. So if the agent buys the slave and it perishes in his hand before the principal takes possession, it is from the agent's wealth, because the purchase is for him, not the principal. But if the principal takes possession of it, he owns it by a transaction of mutual give-and-take (bay' al-ta'ati).

And the author of al-'Inayah mentioned a picture of making the debt owned by other than the debtor: Zayd has a debt on 'Amr. Zayd says to Bakr: 'I appoint you as agent to buy a book for me from another person with that debt which I have on 'Amr.' This is impermissible because Zayd has made Bakr (the agent) own the debt, and he is other than the debtor. And the author of al-Kifayah mentioned another picture: Zayd has a debt on 'Amr. Zayd buys a book from Bakr with that debt, so he has effectively made Bakr own the debt, and he is other than the debtor.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school, specifically from al-Hidayah and its commentaries. It addresses the issue of the specification (ta'yin) of dirhams and dinars in agency contracts and the consequences of that for a specific case: a creditor instructing his debtor to buy a slave using the owed debt. The passage type is an expansion of a ruling, providing rational and transmitted evidence.

The author begins by stating the core ruling: when dirhams or dinars are handed over to an agent in an agency, they become specified (mu'ayyan). That is, the particular coins are identified as the subject matter of the agency, not just a generic debt. Proof of this is that if the principal restricts the agency to specific coins, or if the coins are destroyed after delivery, the agency is invalidated. If they were not specified, destruction would not invalidate the agency; instead, the principal would have to provide replacement coins, or the agent would be liable. This shows that the coins are considered specific property.

The author then presents a rational argument (dalil aqli) from al-Hidayah: in the case where a creditor tells his debtor, 'Buy a slave with the debt you owe me,' the agency necessarily involves either (a) making the debt owned by someone other than the debtor (the seller) without authorizing him to take possession, which is impermissible, or (b) the creditor commanding the debtor to pay the price to the seller, which is a command over something the creditor does not own because the debt is only owned upon taking possession (as repayment is by like, not specific coins). Therefore, such an agency is invalid. If the agent (the debtor) buys the slave and it perishes before the creditor takes possession, the slave is considered the agent's property because the purchase was for himself (since the agency was invalid). However, if the creditor later takes physical possession of the slave, he becomes the owner through a sale by mutual give-and-take (bay' al-ta'ati), which is a valid transaction independent of the invalid agency.

The passage also references two commentaries: al-'Inayah and al-Kifayah, which give example cases to illustrate 'tamlik al-dayn min ghayr man 'alayhi al-dayn' (making the debt owned by someone other than the debtor). In both examples, the creditor attempts to transfer ownership of the debt to a third party (the seller or the agent) without proper authorization, which is impermissible. Thus, the ruling is that such agency is void, and the purchase is for the agent unless ratified by possession.

This analysis follows the Hanafi method of deriving rulings through textual evidence (naql) and rational reasoning ('aql), with explicit references to the foundational texts of the school.

Key Terms
تعيين الدراهم والدنانير (ta'yin al-darahim wa al-dananir): The legal specification of particular coins as the subject matter of the agency; once delivered to the agent, the coins are no longer a generic debt but specific property.
تمليك الدين (tamlik al-dayn): Transfer of ownership of a debt from the creditor to another person, which is valid only if the debtor or his agent takes possession, or if the transfer is with the debtor's consent and the creditor is able to deliver possession.
عزل (ta'yin): Specification; in this context, the process by which generic dirhams and dinars become identified as particular items after delivery to the agent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in this passage, if a creditor instructs his debtor to buy a slave using the debt he owes, and the debtor buys the slave but it perishes before the creditor takes possession, who bears the loss?
A) The creditor, because the agency was valid and the purchase was for him.
B) The debtor, because the purchase was for himself due to the invalid agency.
C) The seller, because the slave was not delivered.
D) Both creditor and debtor share the loss equally.

Key Takeaway
Dirhams and dinars become specified upon delivery to the agent; using an unpaid debt to purchase an item for the creditor is invalid without proper authorization, and the purchase is for the agent.

intermediate

Validity of Agency for Debtor to Buy with Debt Owed
Analyses intra-Hanafi dispute on creditor appointing debtor to buy with debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Imam Abu Hanifah's ruling on the validity of a creditor appointing a debtor as an agent to purchase with the debt, identify the two defects (tamlik al-dayn min ghayr man alayhi al-dayn and amr bi-sarf ma la yamlik), and state the condition that makes the agency valid.

Core Idea
A creditor cannot command a debtor to spend the debt on an unspecified purchase because it entails commanding disposal of what he does not own.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a creditor can appoint a debtor as an agent to buy an item using the debt amount from a third party. Imam Abu Hanifah holds that such an agency is invalid unless the seller is specifically named. The two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) analogize to the case of charity, where the creditor commands the debtor to give the debt in charity, which is valid. We will walk through the reasoning of each side and understand the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifah: such agency is invalid (fasid) when the seller is not specified.
The ruling is based on two legal defects.
2
Identify the opposing view
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the agency is valid by analogy (qiyas) to the case where the creditor commands the debtor to give the debt in charity.
They argue that the recipient (poor) is specified indirectly, so the command is not to an unspecified party.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Imam Abu Hanifah distinguishes the charity case: the poor person is a deputy of Allah, and the destination is known. In the purchase case, the seller is unknown, so the defects of tamlik al-dayn and amr bi-sarf ma la yamlik remain.
Charity is analogous to specifying the seller; without specification, the agency is invalid.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If the agency is invalid, the purchase is for the debtor's own account; if the slave dies before creditor possession, loss is on debtor. If creditor later takes possession, a new sale (bay' al-ta'ati) occurs.
If the agency is valid (seller specified), purchase is for creditor from the start.
5
Apply the exception
If the creditor specifies the seller, the agency is valid even according to Imam Abu Hanifah, because the seller can act as agent to take possession of the debt.
This avoids the two defects.

Source Text
