كتاب الوكالة
ہے۔ لہذا قرض خواہ کا غلام کے مالک کو قرضہ کی رقم کا مالک بنانا بھی جائز نہ ہوگا۔ اور جب یہ جائز نہیں ہے تو قرض خواہ کا قرضدار کو اس قرضہ کے عوض غلام خریدنے کا وکیل بنانا بھی جائز نہ ہوگا۔ اور جب یہ توکیل (وکیل بنانا ) جائز نہیں ہے تو وکیل کے غلام خریدنے کے بعد اگر وہ غلام وکیل کے قبضہ میں مرگیا اور مؤکل نے ابھی تک قبضہ نہیں کیا تو یہ غلام وکیل کے مال سے مرے گا۔ کیونکہ تو کیل کے درست نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے خریداری مؤکل کے لئے نہیں ہوئی بلکہ وکیل کیلئے ہوئی ۔ اور جب خریداری وکیل کیلئے ہوئی تو وکیل ہی نفع ، نقصان کا ذمہ دار ہوگا۔ نہ کہ مؤکل لیکن جب مؤکل اس غلام پر قبضہ کرے گا تو موکل مالک ہو جائے گا۔ مگر اسلئے نہیں کہ تو کیل درست ہے اور قرضدار کی خریداری ، قرض خواہ (مؤکل) کیلئے ہے بلکہ اسلئے کہ جب وکیل ( قرضدار) نے غلام قرض خواہ (مؤکل) کے سپر د کیا اور قرض خواہ نے اس پر قبضہ کر لیا تو یہ قرض خواہ اور قرضدار کے درمیان بیچ تعاطی ہوگئی اور بیع تعاطی کے نتیجہ میں قرض خواہ اس غلام کا مالک ہو گیا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ تملیک الدین من غير من عليه الدين من غير ان يو کله بقبضہ کر نظیر یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے ایسے قرضہ کے عوض کوئی چیز خریدی جو قرضہ مشتری کے علاوہ پر ہے۔
صاحب عنایہ نے اس کی صورت یہ بیان کی ہے کہ زید کا عمر د کے ذمہ قرض ہے۔ پھر زید نے بکر کو اپنا وکیل بالشراء مقرر کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ تو میرے اس قرضہ کے عوض جو عمر و پر ہے۔ عمرو کے علاوہ دوسرے کسی آدمی سے ایک کتاب خرید کر لا دے تو یہ نا جائز ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں وکیل نے کتاب کی خریداری ایسے قرجمہ کے عوض کی ہے جو قرضہ مشتری (وکیل) کے علاوہ عمر و پر ہے اور اس صورت میں یہ لازم آتا ہے کہ قرض خواہ یعنی زید نے قرضہ کا مالک قرضدار یعنی عمرو کے علاوہ یعنی بکر (وکیل) کو بنایا ہے اور یہ نا جائز ہے جیسا کہ گذشتہ سطروں میں اس کی دلیل مذکور ہے۔
اور صاحب کفایہ نے اس کی صورت یہ بیان کی ہے کہ زید کا عمر و پر قرضہ ہے۔ پس زید نے بکر سے اس قرضہ کے عوض جو عمر و پر ہے۔ ایک کتاب خریدی تو گویا زید قرض خواہ نے قرضہ کا مالک قرضدار کے علاوہ یعنی بکر کو بنایا ہے اور یہ سابقہ دلیل کی وجہ سے ناجائز ہے۔ صاحب کفایہ کے بیان کے مطابق علی غیر المشتری کی عبارت وضع الظاهر موضع المضمر کے قبیلہ سے ہوگی یعنی اصل عبارت یوں ہونی چاہئے تھی ۔ علی غیر نفسہ اور مطلب یہی ہوتا کہ زید نے بکر سے ایک کتاب ایسے قرضہ کے عوض خریدی جو
قرضه خود مشتری (زید) کے علاوہ یعنی عمر و پر ہے۔ علی غیر المشتری اور علی غیر نفسہ دونوں کا مطلب ایک ہی ہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل کے ذیل میں صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ متن کے مسئلہ میں مذکور تو کیل سے یا تو تملیک الدین من غير من عليه الدين من غير ان يوكله بقبضه لازم آتا ہے جو نا جائز سے اور یا یہ لازم آئے گا کہ قرض خواہ نے ابھی تک قرضہ کی رقم پر قبضہ نہیں کیا ہے ۔ مگر قرض خواہ قرضدار کو حکم دیتا ہے کہ وہ قرضہ کی رقم غلام کے بائع کو دے دے۔ حالانکہ قرض خواہ کا قرضدار کو یہ حکم دینا کہ وہ قرضہ کی رقم بائع کو دے دے ایسی چیز کا حکم کرنا ہے۔ جس کا قرض خواہ مالک نہیں ہے اسلئے کہ قرضخواہ قرضہ کی رقم کا مالک قبضہ کے بعد ہوتا ہے نہ کہ قبضہ سے پہلے اور وجہ اسکی یہ ہے کہ قرضہ کی ادائیگی با مثالہا کی جاتی ہے نہ کہ باغیانة ، یعنی قرضدار بعینہ وہ درا ہم واپس نہیں کرتا ہے جو دراہم اس نے لئے تھے ۔ بلکہ ان کے مثل دوسرے دراہم واپس کرتا ہے اور وہ دوسرے دراہم جب تک قرض خواہ ان پر قبضہ نہ کرے قرضدار کے مملوک ہوتے ہیں نہ کہ قرض خواہ کے پس قرضدار جو دراہم بائع کو نہ دے گا وہ خود اس کے مملوک ہوں گے ۔ قرض خواہ ان کا مالک نہ ہو گا۔ پس متن کے مسئلہ کے مطابق قرض خواہ کا قرضدار کو یہ حکم دینا کہ قرضہ کے دراہم کے عوض ایک غلام خرید کر لا دے بائع .

كتاب الوكالة
۲۳۴
اشرف الہدایہ جلد- و ہم
کو ایسے دراہم دینے کا حکم کرنا ہے جن کا مالک خود قر ضخواہ نہیں ہے۔ حالانکہ انسان کا ایسے دراہم : دینے کا حکم کرنا جن کا وہ خود مالک نہیں
ہے باطل ہے۔
-
جیسے قرض خواہ نے اگر قرضدار کو یہ کہا کہ میر امال جو تجھ پر ہے تو جس کو چاہے دے دے باطل ہے کیونکہ یہاں بھی ایسا مال دینے کا حکم کرنا ہے۔ جس مال کا خود امر کرنے والا یعنی قرض خواہ مالک نہیں ہے۔ بہر حال جب قرض خواہ کا قرضدار کو یہ امر کرنا باطل ہے تو توکیل مذکور باطل ہے اور جب تو کیل باطل ہے تو خریداری وکیل کیلئے ہوگی نہ کہ موکل کیلئے اور جب خریداری وکیل کیلئے ہے تو خریدا ہوا غلام اگر وکیل کے قبضہ میں مرگیا اور مؤکل نے تاہنوز قبضہ نہیں کیا تو یہ غلام وکیل کا مرے گا نہ کہ موکل کا لیکن اگر وکیل نے غلام کو موکل کے سپر د کر دیا اور متوکل نے اس پر قبضہ کر لیا تو غلام مؤکل کا ہو گا مگر مؤکل کا اسلئے نہیں ہو گا کہ یہ توکیل درست ہے۔ اور وکیل کی خریداری مؤکل کیلئے ہے بلکہ اسلئے ہوگا کہ غلام کو وکیل کا سپر د کرنا اور موکل کا اس پر قبضہ کرنا بیع تعاطی ہے۔ اور بیع تعاطی جائز ہے اور مفید ملک ہے لہذا موکل قبضہ کرنے کے بعد اس کا مالک ہو جائے گا۔
بخلاف ما اذا عين البائع ... الخ سے مصنف ہدایہ نے کہا کہ اگر مؤکل یعنی قرض خواہ نے بائع کو متعین کر دیا۔ مثلا قرض خواہ نے قرضدار سے یہ کہا کہ تو اس قرضہ کے عوض فلاں آدمی سے غلام خرید کر لا دے تو یہ توکیل امام صاحب کے نزدیک بھی صحیح ہے اور مؤکل کیلئے لازم ہے ۔ خواہ موکل اس پر قبضہ کرے یا نہ کرے کیونکہ اس صورت میں بائع قرض خواہ کی طرف سے اولاً قرضہ پر قبضہ کرنے کا وکیل ہوگا پھر بائع ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کا مالک ہو جائے گا۔ اور جب ایسا ہے تو مذکورہ دو خرابیوں ( تملیک الدین من غیر علیه الدین اور امرا بصرف مالا یملکہ ) میں سے کوئی خرابی لازم نہ آئے گی اور جب اس صورت میں مذکورہ دوخرابیوں میں سے کوئی خرابی لازم
نہیں آتی تو تو کیل بھی درست ہوگی اور جب توکیل درست ہے تو خریداری مؤکل پر نافذ ہوگی۔ خواہ موکل پر قبضہ کرے یا نہ کرے وبخلاف ما اذا امره بالتصدق سے صاحبین کے قیاس کا جواب ہے۔ صاحبین کا قیاس اگر چہ ہدایہ میں مذکور نہیں ہے لیکن خادم نے صاحبین کی دلیل کے آخر میں ذکر کیا ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ جب قرض خواہ نے قرضدار سے یہ کہا کہ میرا مال جو تجھ پر ہے تو اسے مساکین پر صدقہ کر دے تو گویا اس نے مال اللہ کیلئے مقرر کیا اور مسکین اس کا نائب ہے اور اللہ معلوم بھی ہے تو یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ قرض خواہ (مؤکل) نے بائع کو متعین کر دیا ہو اور بائع کو متعین کرنے کی صورت میں توکیل درست ہوتی ہے۔ لہذا صدقہ کرنے کیلئے تو کیل بھی درست ہوگی۔
صاحب بدايه واذا لم يصح التوكيل.. الخ سے امام صاحب کی دلیل کا تمہ ذکر فرمارہے ہیں۔ یعنی جب قرضدار کو قرضہ کے عوض عبد غیر معین خرید کر لانے کا حکم کرنے سے مذکورہ دو خرابیوں (تملیک الدین ... الخ اور امرا بـصـرف مالا يملکہ ) میں سے کوئی خرابی لازم آتی ہے تو یہ تو کیل یعنی قرض خواہ کا قرضدار کو قرضہ کے عوض عبد غیر معین خریدنے کا وکیل کرنا صحیح نہ ہوگا۔ اور جب یہ توکیل صحیح نہیں ہے تو وکیل یعنی قرضدار کی خریداری خود وکیل پر نافذ ہوگی اور غلام ہلاک ہونے کی صورت میں وکیل یعنی قرضدار کا مال ضائع ہو گا۔ نہ مؤکل یعنی قرض خواہ کا۔ ہاں اگر مؤکل یعنی قرض خواہ نے اس غلام پر وکیل یعنی قرضدار کی طرف سے قبضہ کر لیا تو یہ قرض خواہ اور قرضدار کے درمیان بیچ تعاطی منعقد ہو جائے گی اور بیع تعاطی کی وجہ سے قرض خواہ ( مؤکل ) اس غلام کا مالک ہوگا اور نفع
نقصان کا ذمہ دار ہوگا۔
Therefore, it will also be impermissible for the creditor to make the owner of the slave the owner of the debt amount. And when this is impermissible, then it will also be impermissible for the creditor to appoint the debtor as an agent to buy a slave in exchange for this debt. And when this appointment (making an agent) is impermissible, then after the agent buys the slave, if that slave dies in the agent's possession and the principal has not yet taken possession, then this slave will die from the agent's wealth. Because due to the invalidity of the agency, the purchase was not for the principal but for the agent. And when the purchase was for the agent, the agent will be responsible for profit and loss, not the principal. However, when the principal takes possession of this slave, the principal will become the owner. But not because the agency is valid and the debtor's purchase is for the creditor (principal), but rather because when the agent (debtor) handed over the slave to the creditor (principal) and the creditor took possession of it, then a sale by mutual consent (bay' al-ta'ati) occurred between the creditor and debtor, and as a result of bay' al-ta'ati, the creditor became the owner of this slave. The author of Hidayah said that making someone owner of a debt from other than the one upon whom the debt is due without authorizing him to take possession is similar to a person buying something in exchange for a debt that is upon someone other than the buyer. The author of 'Inayah explained its form: Zayd has a debt upon 'Amr. Then Zayd appointed Bakr as his agent for purchase, saying, 'Buy a book from someone other than 'Amr in exchange for this debt that is upon 'Amr.' This is impermissible because in this form the agent purchased the book in exchange for a debt that is upon 'Amr, other than the buyer (the agent). And in this form it necessarily follows that the creditor, i.e., Zayd, made someone other than the debtor, i.e., Bakr (the agent), the owner of the debt, and this is impermissible, as its proof was mentioned in the previous lines. And the author of Kifayah explained its form: Zayd has a debt upon 'Amr. Then Zayd bought a book from Bakr in exchange for this debt that is upon 'Amr. So, as if Zayd the creditor made someone other than the debtor, i.e., Bakr, the owner of the debt, and this is impermissible due to the previous proof. According to the explanation of the author of Kifayah, the phrase 'against other than the buyer' ('ala ghayr al-mushtari) is from the category of placing the apparent in the place of the implicit, i.e., the original phrase should have been 'against other than himself' ('ala ghayr nafsihi). The meaning would be that Zayd bought a book from Bakr in exchange for a debt that is upon someone other than the buyer himself (Zayd), i.e., upon 'Amr. 'Ala ghayr al-mushtari and 'ala ghayr nafsihi both have the same meaning. Under the proof of Imam Abu Hanifah, the author of Hidayah said: From the agency mentioned in the text of the issue, either it necessarily follows that there is making someone owner of a debt from other than the one upon whom the debt is due without authorizing him to take possession, which is impermissible, or it will necessarily follow that the creditor has not yet taken possession of the debt amount, but the creditor commands the debtor to give the debt amount to the seller of the slave. However, the creditor's commanding the debtor to give the debt amount to the seller is commanding something that the creditor does not own, because the creditor becomes owner of the debt amount only after taking possession, not before. The reason for this is that repayment of a debt is made by its equivalent, not by the specific items, i.e., the debtor does not return the exact same dirhams he took, but returns other dirhams similar to them. And those other dirhams, as long as the creditor has not taken possession of them, are owned by the debtor, not by the creditor. Thus, the dirhams that the debtor gives to the seller are his own property; the creditor is not their owner. Therefore, according to the issue of the text, the creditor's commanding the debtor to buy a slave and bring him in exchange for the debt dirhams is commanding the giving of dirhams whose owner the creditor himself is not. While a person's commanding the giving of dirhams whose owner he himself is not is invalid. For example, if the creditor said to the debtor, 'My property that is upon you, give it to whomever you wish,' it is invalid, because here too it is commanding the giving of property whose owner the commander, i.e., the creditor, is not. In any case, when the creditor's commanding the debtor is invalid, then the mentioned agency is invalid. And when the agency is invalid, the purchase will be for the agent, not for the principal. And when the purchase is for the agent, then the bought slave, if he dies in the agent's possession and the principal has not yet taken possession, this slave will die as the agent's, not the principal's. But if the agent handed over the slave to the principal and the principal took possession of him, then the slave becomes the principal's, but not because this agency is valid and the agent's purchase is for the principal, but rather because the agent's handing over the slave and the principal's taking possession of him is a sale by mutual consent (bay' al-ta'ati). And bay' al-ta'ati is permissible and confers ownership. Hence, after taking possession, the principal becomes its owner. 'Except when he specifies the seller...' etc. From this, the author of Hidayah said: If the principal, i.e., the creditor, specified the seller, for example, the creditor said to the debtor, 'Buy a slave from so-and-so in exchange for this debt,' then this agency is also valid according to Imam (Abu Hanifah) and is binding for the principal, whether the principal takes possession or not, because in this form, the seller will first be the agent of the creditor to take possession of the debt, then due to being the seller, he will become its owner. And when this is the case, none of the two defects (making someone owner of a debt from other than the one upon whom it is due, and commanding the disposal of what one does not own) necessarily arise. And when in this form none of the two defects necessarily arise, then the agency is also valid. And when the agency is valid, the purchase will be effective for the principal, whether the principal takes possession or not. 'And contrary to when he commands him to give charity' is a response to the analogy of the two companions (Sahibayn). Although the analogy of the two companions is not mentioned in Hidayah, but Khadim mentioned it at the end of their proof. The gist of the response is: When the creditor said to the debtor, 'My property that is upon you, give it in charity to the poor,' then he has designated the property for Allah, and the poor person is His deputy, and Allah is known. So this becomes similar to the case where the creditor (principal) specified the seller, and in the case of specifying the seller, the agency is valid. Therefore, the agency for giving charity is also valid. The author of Bada'i', 'And when the agency is not valid...' etc., is stating the conclusion of Imam's proof. That is, when commanding the debtor to buy an unspecified slave in exchange for the debt necessarily brings one of the two defects (making someone owner of a debt from other than the one upon whom it is due, and commanding the disposal of what one does not own), then this agency, i.e., the creditor making the debtor an agent to buy an unspecified slave in exchange for the debt, will not be valid. And when this agency is not valid, then the purchase by the agent, i.e., the debtor, will be effective upon the agent himself, and in case of the slave's destruction, the agent's wealth will be lost, not the principal's. Yes, if the principal, i.e., the creditor, took possession of this slave from the agent, i.e., the debtor, then a sale by mutual consent (bay' al-ta'ati) will be concluded between the creditor and debtor, and due to bay' al-ta'ati, the creditor (principal) will become the owner of this slave and responsible for profit and loss.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of a creditor appointing the debtor as an agent to buy a slave using the debt amount from a third party. The passage presents Imam Abu Hanifah's ruling that such agency is invalid because it entails either tamlik al-dayn min ghayr man alayhi al-dayn (making someone other than the debtor owner of the debt) or amr bi-sarf ma la yamlik (commanding disposal of what one does not own), both of which are impermissible. The commentary explains the reasoning: the creditor does not own the debt amount until he takes possession of it, because debt repayment is by equivalent, not the specific currency. Therefore, commanding the debtor to pay the seller with the debt amounts to commanding the disposal of property the creditor does not own. The passage then distinguishes two cases: (1) If the creditor specifies the seller (ba'i'), the agency is valid because the seller first acts as agent to take possession of the debt on behalf of the creditor, then becomes owner of the debt by selling the slave. (2) If the creditor commands the debtor to give the debt in charity, the agency is also valid because it is analogous to specifying the seller – the poor are deputies of Allah. The passage concludes that if the agency is invalid and the slave dies before the creditor takes possession, the loss is on the debtor. However, if the creditor later takes possession, it becomes a bay' al-ta'ati (sale by mutual consent) and the creditor acquires ownership.

Key Terms
تملیک الدین من غیر من علیه الدین (tamlik al-dayn min ghayr man alayhi al-dayn): Making someone other than the debtor the owner of the debt (i.e., transferring the debt to a third party without the debtor's authorization).
امر بصرف ما لا یملک (amr bi-sarf ma la yamlik): Commanding the disposal of property that one does not own.
بیع تعاطی (bay' al-ta'ati): A sale concluded by mutual exchange (hand-over) without verbal offer and acceptance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifah, what condition makes the agency of a debtor to purchase with the debt amount valid?
A) The debtor must be trustworthy.
B) The seller must be specified by the creditor.
C) The purchase must be for a slave only.
D) The creditor must take possession of the item immediately.

Key Takeaway
A creditor cannot validly appoint a debtor as an agent to buy from an unspecified seller using the debt amount, because it entails commanding disposal of property not yet owned; specifying the seller avoids this defect.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
6 min
Dispute Between Principal and Agent Over Purchase Price
Explains ruling when principal and agent disagree on purchase price

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whose word is accepted when principal and agent disagree on the purchase price, and identify the key factor (market value of the purchased item and whether the principal gave the money).

Core Idea
The agent's word is accepted when the slave-girl is worth the full price; otherwise, the principal's word prevails due to violation.

This lesson from Al-Hidayah examines a common dispute in agency (wakalah): the principal and agent disagree on the actual purchase price of a slave-girl. The Hanafi ruling turns on the market value of the purchased item and whether the principal entrusted the money. Understanding this ruling helps you see how Hanafi fiqh balances the trustee status of the agent with the need to protect the principal from violations of instructions.

Guided Path
1
Identify parties and the dispute
The principal (muwakkil) gives the agent (wakil) money to buy a slave-girl. After purchase, they disagree on the price. Identify each party's claim.
2
Check if the principal gave the money
Determine whether the principal handed over the full amount to the agent. This affects who is believed.
If money was given, the agent is a trustee (amin).
3
Assess the market value of the slave-girl
What is the actual market value of the slave-girl? Compare it to the instructed price (1000 dirhams).
Value can be 1000, 500, or other.
4
Apply the rule based on value and money
Case 1: Value = 1000 and money given → agent's word. Case 2: Value = 500 (less) and money given → principal's word (violation). Case 3: Money not given → principal's word always. Case 4: Value = 1000 but money not given → mutual oaths and rescission.
The underlying principle: agent is amīn unless he violates; then he becomes liable.
5
Understand the legal effect
When the agent's word is rejected, he is liable to pay the difference or return the slave-girl. If mutual oaths occur, the contract is rescinded and the agent keeps the slave-girl.
This reasoning is based on the analogy (qiyas) to buyer-seller disputes.

قال ومن دفع الى آخر الفا وامره ان يشترى بها جارية فاشتراها فقال الآمر اشتريتها بخمسمائة وقال المامور اشتريتها بالف فالقول قول المامور ومراده اذا كانت تساوى الفا لانه امين فيه وقد ادعى الخروج عن عهدة الامانة والأمر يدعى عليه ضمان خمسمائة وهو ينكر فان كانت تساوى خمسمائة فالقول قول الأمر لانه خالف حيث اشترى جارية تساوى خمسمائة والأمر تناول ما يساوى الفافيضمن قال وان لم يكن دفع اليه الالف فالقول قول الآمر اما اذا كانت قيمتها خمسمائة فالمخالفة وان كانت قيمتها الفا فمعناه انهما يتحالفان لأن المؤكل والوكيل فى هذا ينزلان منزلة البائع والمشترى وقد وقع الاختلاف فى الثمن وموجبه التحالف ثم يفسخ العقد الذى جرى بينهما فيلزم الجارية المامور
He said: And if one gives another a thousand [dirhams] and commands him to buy a slave-girl with it, and he buys her, then the principal says 'You bought her for five hundred' and the agent says 'I bought her for a thousand', then the word is the word of the agent. And his intention is when she is worth a thousand, because he is a trustee in it and he has claimed discharge from the trust, and the principal claims five hundred as a liability against him and he denies it. But if she is worth five hundred, then the word is the word of the principal, because he has violated [the instruction] since he bought a slave-girl worth five hundred while the command encompassed what is worth a thousand, so he becomes liable. He said: And if he did not give him the thousand, then the word is the word of the principal. As for when her value is five hundred, then [there is] violation; and if her value is a thousand, then its meaning is that they take mutual oaths, because the principal and agent in this are placed in the position of seller and buyer, and a dispute has occurred over the price, and its requirement is mutual oaths, then the contract that took place between them is rescinded, and the slave-girl becomes binding on the agent.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya discusses a dispute in agency (wakalah). The author presents a ruling from the matn of al-Jami' al-Saghir by Imam Muhammad. The scenario: a principal gives an agent 1,000 dirhams to purchase a slave-girl. After purchase, the principal claims the agent bought her for 500, while the agent claims 1,000. The ruling depends on the actual market value of the slave-girl. If she is worth 1,000, the agent's word is accepted because he is a trustee (amin) claiming discharge from trust; the principal's claim of 500 liability is a demand that the agent denies, and without evidence, the denier's word (with oath) prevails. If she is worth 500, the principal's word is accepted because the agent violated the instruction by buying a slave-girl of lesser value, and such a violation (along with gross deception, ghubn fahish) makes the purchase for the agent himself, making him liable. If the principal did not give the money, then the principal's word is accepted in both value scenarios. When the value is 500, it is a clear violation; when the value is 1,000, the dispute is over the price, so the parties are treated like seller and buyer and must take mutual oaths (tahlif), then the contract is rescinded and the slave-girl becomes the agent's responsibility. The commentary emphasizes the logical reasoning behind each case, rooted in the principles of trust, violation, and the analogy to sale.

Key Terms
وكيل (wakīl): The agent appointed to carry out a transaction on behalf of the principal.
موكل (muwakkil): The principal who appoints the agent and entrusts him with money or authority.
أمين (amīn): A trustee entrusted with property; his word is accepted regarding discharge of trust.
ضمان (ḍamān): Financial liability or guarantee; here, the agent may be liable for the difference if he violated instructions.
تحالف (taḥāluf): Mutual oaths taken by both parties when they disagree on the price, leading to rescission of the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a principal gives an agent 1000 dirhams to buy a slave-girl, the agent buys a slave-girl worth 500 dirhams, and then they dispute the price (principal says 500, agent says 1000), whose word is accepted?
A) The agent's word, because he is a trustee.
B) The principal's word, because the agent violated instructions.
C) Both take oaths and the contract is rescinded.
D) The slave-girl is valued by an expert.

Key Takeaway
In agency disputes over price, the determining factor is the market value of the purchased item and whether the principal gave the money.

When an Agent Buys at a Loss: Violation, Ghabn Fahish, and Tahaluf in Wakala
Ruling and proof for agency dispute when principal gave no money

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when an agent violates the principal's command or commits ghabn fahish, and apply the rule of tahaluf when price is disputed in wakala.

Core Idea
An agent's purchase that violates the principal's command or involves gross overpayment is for the agent, not the principal.

This lesson explores a critical scenario in Hanafi agency law: the principal instructs the agent to buy a specific slave girl for 1000 dirhams, but the agent buys her at 1000 dirhams when her market value is only 500. The text provides two proofs for why the purchase is for the agent. It then considers a further complication where the principal did not provide the money, leading to a price dispute with two subcases. Understanding these rules helps determine liability and ownership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The principal commands the agent to buy a slave girl worth 1000 dirhams for 1000 dirhams. The agent buys her for 1000 dirhams, but her market value is only 500. This creates two legal issues: violation of command (mukhalafa) and gross overpayment (ghabn fahish).
The dispute is about whether the purchase is for the principal or the agent.
2
Examine the first proof: Mukhalafa (violation)
The agent violated the principal's explicit command because the command was to buy a slave girl of equal value (1000 worth for 1000 price). By buying a slave girl worth only 500 for 1000, the agent acted contrary to the instruction and harmed the principal. In Hanafi wakala, such harmful violation makes the purchase binding on the agent.
The key is that the violation causes harm to the principal.
3
Examine the second proof: Ghabn Fahish (gross overpayment)
Even without considering the violation, the purchase involves ghabn fahish: paying 1000 for something worth 500. In Hanafi law, if an agent commits ghabn fahish, the purchase is for the agent. This is an independent proof.
Ghabn fahish is defined as a significant discrepancy; here, 500 dirhams difference.
4
Consider the second scenario: principal did not give the money
Now the principal never handed over the 1000 dirhams to the agent. After the purchase, they dispute the price. Two subcases: if the slave girl's market value is 500, the principal's statement is accepted without oath because violation and ghabn are clear. If her value is 1000 (no violation/ghabn), the parties are treated as seller and buyer (the agent hypothetically sells to the principal), and they must take mutual oaths (tahaluf) about the price.
In the second subcase, the purchase is still ultimately for the agent because the hypothetical contract is rescinded.
5
Understand Tahaluf (mutual oath-taking)
Tahaluf is the procedure when seller and buyer dispute the price: each takes an oath, then the contract is rescinded. Here, the agent (as seller) says the price was 1000, the principal (as buyer) says it was 500. They both take oaths, the hypothetical contract is void, and the slave girl remains with the agent (who must pay the seller from his own funds).
This results in the principal's statement being 'accepted' in the sense that he does not have to pay more than what he claims.

One proof for this is that the agent violated the principal's command in that the principal had ordered him to buy a slave girl whose value and price were equal to one thousand dirhams for one thousand dirhams. But the agent bought a slave girl whose value is five hundred dirhams for one thousand dirhams. So the agent violated his principal in a way that harms the principal. Whenever a purchase involves violation of the principal's command by the agent and that violation harms the principal, that purchase is for the agent himself, not for the principal. Therefore, this purchase of the slave girl is for the agent, and the agent is guarantor to the principal. The second proof is that when the agent bought a slave girl worth five hundred dirhams for one thousand dirhams, this purchase involved gross overpayment (ghabn fahish). When a purchase involves gross overpayment, the purchase is for the agent, not for the principal. And when this purchase is for the agent, then the agent is guarantor to the principal.

And if the principal did not give the one thousand dirhams, then the statement of the principal is accepted.

He said: If he did not give him the alif (one thousand), then the statement is the statement of the principal. But if its value is five hundred, then there is violation; if its value is one thousand, then its meaning is that they take mutual oaths, because the principal and the agent in this are placed in the position of seller and buyer. A dispute has occurred regarding the price, and its consequence is mutual oath. Then the contract that took place between them is rescinded, and the slave girl becomes binding on the agent (the one commanded).

Translation: And if the principal did not give the one thousand dirhams to the agent, then the principal's statement is accepted. In any case, when the slave girl's price is five hundred dirhams, then due to violation; and if its price is one thousand dirhams, then its meaning is that both the agent and the principal take oaths. Because the principal and the agent in this case are in the position of seller and buyer. A dispute has occurred regarding the price, and its ruling is mutual oath-taking. Then the contract that took place between them is rescinded, and the slave girl becomes binding on the agent.

Commentary: The second scenario of the previous issue is that the principal did not give the agent one thousand dirhams, and the agent bought the slave girl. Then a dispute occurred between them. Thus, the principal said: You bought this slave girl for five hundred dirhams. And the agent said: I bought her for one thousand dirhams. Then the principal's statement is accepted, whether the slave girl's price is five hundred dirhams or one thousand dirhams. If the slave girl's price is five hundred dirhams, then the principal's statement is accepted because the agent's violation of the principal's command is found. Because the principal had ordered to buy a slave girl whose value and price are one thousand dirhams for one thousand dirhams, and he bought a slave girl whose value is five hundred dirhams. And gross overpayment (ghabn fahish) is also realized from the agent's side, as he bought something worth five hundred dirhams for one thousand dirhams. In both these cases, the purchase is binding on the agent, not on the principal. Therefore, the principal's statement is accepted. And the purchase of the slave girl is for the agent, not for the principal. And if the slave girl's value and price are one thousand dirhams, then the meaning of the principal's statement being accepted is that both the principal and the agent take oaths. Because between the principal and the agent, hypothetically, an exchange occurs. In that the agent gives the sold item to the principal, and the principal gives the price to the agent. Therefore, the principal and the agent are in the position of seller and buyer. That is, the agent is in the position of seller, and the principal is in the position of buyer. A dispute occurs between them regarding the price: the agent (seller) says the price of the slave girl is one thousand dirhams, and the principal (buyer) says the price of the slave girl is five hundred dirhams. The ruling for a dispute between seller and buyer regarding the price is that oaths are taken from both. If both take oaths, then the contract is rescinded. Here too, if the principal and the agent both take oaths, then the hypothetical contract that was concluded between them will be rescinded. And when the hypothetical contract is rescinded, then the slave girl becomes the responsibility of the agent. That is, the agent becomes the owner, not the principal. So as a result, in this case too, the principal's statement is accepted.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling for a scenario in the law of agency (wakala) where the principal (muwakkil) instructs the agent (wakil) to purchase a specific slave girl for 1000 dirhams, but the agent buys her for 1000 while her market value is only 500. The text first provides two proofs (dalil) that the purchase is for the agent himself, not the principal: (1) the agent violated the principal's explicit command, which harms the principal, and (2) gross overpayment (ghabn fahish) makes the purchase for the agent. Then it moves to a different scenario: the principal did not hand over the 1000 dirhams to the agent, and a dispute arises about the price actually paid. Two subcases are distinguished based on the slave girl's market value. If her value is 500, the agent's purchase clearly violates the command and involves ghabn fahish, so the purchase is for the agent and the principal's statement (that it was bought for 500) is accepted. If her value is also 1000, there is no violation or ghabn fahish, but the principal and agent disagree on the price. The text treats them as if they were seller and buyer in a hypothetical exchange (the agent sells the slave girl to the principal). When seller and buyer dispute the price, the rule is that both take oaths (tahaluf), then the contract is rescinded, and the slave girl remains with the seller (the agent). Thus, in both subcases, the principal's statement is deemed accepted in the sense that the purchase is ultimately for the agent, not the principal. The commentary (tashrih) clarifies this reasoning.

Key Terms
مخالفت (mukhalafa): Violation of the principal's command by the agent.
غبن فاحش (ghabn fahish): Gross overpayment where the price exceeds the market value by a significant margin (here 500 vs 1000).
تحالف (tahaluf): Mutual oath-taking by two parties disputing the price of a contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
An agent's purchase that violates the principal's command or involves gross overpayment (ghabn fahish) is for the agent; if no violation or ghabn and the principal did not provide funds, the dispute is resolved by mutual oath (tahaluf) and the purchase remains with the agent.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Does Seller's Confirmation Prevent Tahaluf?
Ruling on dispute when principal did not name price and seller confirms agent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two Hanafi positions on whether seller's confirmation eliminates the need for mutual oath (tahaluf) between principal and agent, and identify the preferred view.

Core Idea
The seller's confirmation does not bind the principal, so tahaluf remains required between principal and agent.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents a scenario where the principal and agent dispute the price paid for a slave, and the seller confirms the agent's version. At first glance, the seller's confirmation seems to resolve the dispute. However, Hanafi scholars differ on whether this confirmation removes the need for mutual oath-taking (tahaluf) between the principal and agent. Understanding this ikhtilaf is crucial for correctly applying the rules of agency and oath in sales disputes.

Guided Path
1
State the base scenario and initial ruling
Identify the facts: principal instructs agent to buy a specific slave without naming a price; agent buys; principal says 500, agent says 1000; seller confirms agent. The initial ruling: the agent's statement with oath is accepted.
2
Identify the two Hanafi positions on tahaluf
One group (Faqih Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani) holds that no mutual oath occurs because the seller's confirmation removes the dispute. The other (Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi) holds that mutual oath is still required.
Both are Hanafi positions, not inter-madhhab.
3
Analyze the dalil for each position
Al-Hindwani: seller is present and his confirmation ends the dispute. Al-Maturidi: seller after receiving price is a stranger to both; before receiving it, stranger to principal only. No sale occurred between principal and seller, so seller's confirmation does not bind the principal.
Focus on the legal relationship: principal never dealt with seller.
4
Determine the preferred view and its practical consequence
The author declares al-Maturidi's view as 'azhar' (more apparent). Consequence: if tahaluf occurs, both take oaths, the sale is rescinded (the slave stays with agent? actually the contract between principal and agent is rescinded? Check: thamarah says the slave remains with agent). If no tahaluf, agent's statement stands and slave is for principal at agent's claimed price.
The mufta bihi is that tahaluf is still required.

مؤکل نے وکیل کو معین غلام خریدنے کا حکم دیا اور شمن بیان نہیں کئے وکیل نے غلام کو خرید لیا موکل نے کہا کہ تو نے پانچ سو کے عوض خریدا ہے اور وکیل نے کہا کہ ایک ہزار کے عوض خریدا ہے اور بائع نے وکیل کی تصدیق کی تو وکیل کا قول مع الیمین معتبر ہوگا
قال ولو امره ان يشترى له هذا العبد ولم يسم له ثمنا فاشتراه فقال الآمر اشتريته بخمسمائة وقال المامور بالف وصدق البائع المامور فالقول قول المامور مع يمينه قيل لا تحالف ههنا لانه ارتفع الخلاف بتصديق البائع اذهو حاضر وفي المسألة الأولى هو غائب فاعتبر الاختلاف وقيل يتحالفان لما ذكرنا وقد ذكر معظم يمين التحالف وهو يمين البائع والبائع بعد استيفاء الثمن اجنبى عنهما وقبله اجنبي عن المؤكل اذ لم يجر بينهما بيع فلا يصدق عليه فبقى الخلاف وهذا قول الامام أبي منصور وهو اظهر والله اعلم بالصواب
ترجمہ اور اگر موکل نے وکیل کو حکم دیا کہ اسکے واسطے یہ غلام خرید لے اور اس کا شمن بیان نہیں کیا ۔ پس وکیل نے اس غلام کو خرید لیا پھر موکل نے کہا کہ تو نے اس کو پانچ سو درہم کے عوض خریدا ہے اور وکیل نے کہا کہ ایک ہزار درہم کے عوض اور بائع نے وکیل کی تصدیق کی تو مع الیمین وکیل کا قول قبول ہو گا۔ کہا گیا ہے کہ اس جگہ باہمی قسم نہیں ہے کیونکہ بائع کی تصدیق سے اختلاف اٹھ گیا۔ اسلئے کہ بائع حاضر ہے اور پہلے مسئلہ میں بائع غائب تھا۔ اس وجہ سے اختلاف معتبر ہوا۔ اور کہا گیا ہے کہ دونوں قسم کھا ئیں گے ۔ اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے ذکر کی ہے۔ اور امام محمد نے تخالف میں سب سے بڑی قسم جو کر فرمائی وہ بائع کی قسم ہے اور بائع من حاصل کرنے کے بعد دونوں سے اجنبی ہے اور ثمن حاصل کرنے سے پہلے مؤکل سے اجنبی ہے۔ کیونکہ موکل اور اس بائع کے درمیان کوئی بیچ واقع نہیں ہوئی لہند موکل پر بائع کے قول کی تصدیق نہ ہوگی ۔ پس اختلاف باقی رہا اور یہ امام ابو منصور ماتریدی کا قول ہے اور یہی اظہر ہے ۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مؤکل نے وکیل کو ایک معین غلام خریدنے کا حکم دیا مگر اس غلام کا شمن بیان نہیں کیا۔ پس وکیل نے اس غلام کوخرید لیا۔ پھر مؤکل اور وکیل کے درمیان مقدار شمن میں اختلاف واقع ہوا۔ چنانچہ مؤکل نے اپنے وکیل سے کہا کہ تو نے یہ غلام پانچ سو روپیہ میں خریدا ہے۔ اور وکیل نے کہا کہ حضور ایسا نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ میں نے یہ غلام ایک ہزار روپیہ میں خریدا ہے اور غلام کے بائع نے بھی وکیل کے قول کی تصدیق کی تو وکیل کا قول مع الیمین معتبر ہو گا۔ مصنف ہدایہ نے کہا کہ بعض مشائخ مثلا فقیہ ابوجعفر ہندوانی کا قول یہ ہے کہ اس مسئلہ میں تخالف نہیں ہے۔ یعنی مؤکل اور وکیل کے درمیان تخالف نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ بائع کی تصدیق سے اختلاف ختم ہو گیا۔ اور بعض مشائخ مثلا امام ابو منصور ماتریدی کا قول یہ ہے کہ تخالف ہوگا۔ کیونکہ بائع بعد استیفاء ثمن دونوں سے اجنبی ہے اور قبل استیفاء ثمن صرف مؤکل سے اجنبی ہے۔ اسلئے وکیل پہلے ہی بائع سے خرید کر چکا ہے، ثمن ادا کر چکا ہے، اب بائع کی تصدیق مؤکل پر اثر نہیں کرے گی، اسلئے اختلاف باقی ہے اور تخالف ہوگا۔ اور یہی قول اظہر ہے۔
The principal ordered the agent to buy a specific slave and did not mention the price. The agent bought the slave. The principal said: You bought him for five hundred. The agent said: For one thousand. And the seller confirmed the agent. Then the agent's statement with oath is accepted.

He (the author) said: If he ordered him to buy this slave for him and did not name a price, and he bought him, and the principal said: You bought him for five hundred, and the agent said: For one thousand, and the seller confirmed the agent, then the statement is the statement of the agent with his oath. It is said: There is no mutual oath here, because the dispute is removed by the confirmation of the seller, because he is present, and in the first issue he was absent, so the dispute was considered. And it is said: They take mutual oaths, due to what we have mentioned. And Imam Muhammad has mentioned the greatest oath of mutual oath, which is the oath of the seller. And the seller after taking the price is a stranger to both of them, and before taking it he is a stranger to the principal, since no sale took place between them, so his statement is not accepted against the principal. So the dispute remains, and this is the statement of Imam Abu Mansur, and it is more apparent. And Allah knows best the correct.

Translation: And if the principal ordered the agent to buy this slave for him and did not state his price, then the agent bought this slave. Then the principal said: You bought him for five hundred dirhams, and the agent said: For one thousand dirhams, and the seller confirmed the agent, then the agent's statement with oath is accepted. It is said that there is no mutual oath here because the dispute is removed by the seller's confirmation, because the seller is present, and in the first issue the seller was absent, so the dispute was considered. And it is said that they will take mutual oaths, due to the proof we have mentioned. And Imam Muhammad did not make the greatest oath of tahaluf, which is the oath of the seller, apply. The seller after receiving the price is a stranger to both of them, and before receiving it he is a stranger to the principal, because no sale took place between the principal and the seller, so the seller's statement is not accepted against the principal. So the dispute remains, and this is the statement of Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, and it is more apparent. And Allah knows best the correct.

Commentary: The scenario is that the principal ordered the agent to buy a specific slave but did not state his price. So the agent bought this slave. Then a dispute occurred between the principal and the agent regarding the amount of the price. Thus, the principal said to his agent: You bought this slave for five hundred rupees. And the agent said: Sir, that is not the case; rather I bought this slave for one thousand rupees. And the seller of the slave also confirmed the agent's statement. Then the agent's statement with oath is accepted. The author of Hidayah said that some mashayikh, for example Faqih Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani, said that there is no mutual oath in this issue, i.e., there will be no mutual oath between the principal and the agent because the dispute is removed by the seller's confirmation. And some mashayikh, for example Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, said that there will be mutual oath. Because after receiving the price, the seller is a stranger to both, and before receiving it he is a stranger only to the principal. Therefore, since the agent has already bought from the seller and paid the price, the seller's confirmation will not affect the principal, so the dispute remains and mutual oath will occur. And this statement is more apparent.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific scenario: the principal instructs the agent to buy a particular slave (a specifically identified slave) without specifying a price. The agent buys the slave, and then a dispute arises: the principal claims the price was 500, the agent claims it was 1000, and the seller (the third-party vendor) confirms the agent's statement. The initial ruling is that the agent's statement with an oath is accepted. However, there is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf (dispute) on whether mutual oath-taking (tahaluf) between principal and agent is required. Some scholars (like Faqih Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani) say no, because the seller's confirmation removes the dispute—since the seller is present and confirms the price, there is no longer any ambiguity. Others (like Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi) say yes, tahaluf is still needed, because the seller's confirmation is not binding on the principal: the seller is a stranger to the principal (no contract between them), and once the agent has paid the price, the seller's statement is irrelevant to the principal-agent relationship. Thus the dispute remains, and tahaluf should occur. The text declares al-Maturidi's view as the more apparent (azhar) position. The commentary clarifies that this ikhtilaf is among Hanafi scholars, with the preferred view being that mutual oath is still required.

Key Terms
مأمور (ma'mur): The agent (wakil) who is commanded by the principal to perform a purchase.
آمر (amir): The principal (muwakkil) who gives the command to the agent.
تحالف (tahaluf): Mutual oath-taking between two parties disputing the price in a contract, leading to rescission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A principal instructs an agent to buy a specific slave without specifying a price. The agent buys the slave for 1000 dirhams. The principal claims the price was 500 dirhams, and the seller confirms the agent's statement. According to the preferred Hanafi view (Imam Abu Mansur), what is the ruling?
A) The agent's statement is accepted without oath, and the slave goes to the principal.
B) There is no mutual oath; the seller's confirmation ends the dispute.
C) The agent's statement with oath is accepted, and mutual oath (tahaluf) is still required.
D) The principal's statement is accepted with oath.

Key Takeaway
When a principal and agent dispute the price and the seller confirms the agent, the agent's statement with oath is accepted, but the principal still has the right to demand mutual oaths (tahaluf) because the seller's confirmation does not bind the principal.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
Seller's Confirmation and Mutual Oath: Intra-Hanafi Analysis
Intra-Hanafi dispute on seller's confirmation effect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two Hanafi positions on whether seller's confirmation precludes mutual oath and identify the tarjih (preferred view) with its thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Seller's confirmation does not bind the principal; mutual oath still required.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a procedural dispute: when an agent buys a slave, the principal and agent disagree on price, and the seller confirms the agent's word. Does this confirmation remove the need for mutual oath (tahāluf)? Two Hanafi masters differ, and the author rules for the view requiring tahāluf. Understanding why the seller's confirmation is irrelevant to the principal is key to mastering Hanafi agency law.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position from the matn
Identify the initial ruling: the agent's word with oath is accepted. This is from Imam Muhammad's statement in al-Jami' al-Saghir.
The matn does not mention tahāluf explicitly.
2
Identify the two intra-Hanafi views
Fakhr al-Islam al-Hindwani holds no tahāluf because the seller's confirmation removes the dispute. Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi holds tahāluf is required because the seller is a stranger to the principal.
Both are Hanafi scholars.
3
Examine al-Hindwani's proof
The seller is present and confirms the agent's price, effectively creating a new sale between seller and agent, which binds the principal by the agency. Thus no dispute remains.
He analogizes to a direct sale where confirmation resolves.
4
Examine al-Maturidi's proof
The seller has no contractual relation with the principal; his confirmation does not affect the principal. The analogy to buyer-seller dispute (where tahāluf applies) remains. The seller's oath is the greatest in tahāluf.
Imam Muhammad's statement that the agent's word with oath is accepted does not contradict tahāluf; tahāluf includes the agent's oath as primary.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If no tahāluf (al-Hindwani): the sale binds the principal at the agent's stated price. If tahāluf (al-Maturidi): if both swear, the constructive contract is annulled and the slave belongs to the agent.
The author declares al-Maturidi's view azhar.

اشرف الہدایہ جلد وہم

كتاب الوكالة
دیتا ہے۔ لہذا موکل اور وکیل دونوں بائع اور مشتری کے مرتبہ میں ہوں گے۔ یعنی وکیل بائع کے مرتبہ میں ہوگا اور مؤکل مشتری کے مرتبہ میں ہوگا۔ اور دونوں کے درمیان شمن میں اختلاف ہوگا کہ وکیل یعنی مشتری نے کہا کہ باندی کا من پانچ سو درہم ہیں اور وکیل یعنی بائے نے کہا کہ باندی کا شمن ایک ہزار درہم ہیں اور بائع اور مشتری کے درمیان ثمن میں اختلاف کا حکم یہ ہے کہ دونوں سے قسم لی جائے۔ اگر دونوں قسم کھا لیں تو اس عقد کو مسخ کر دیا جائے۔ پس یہاں بھی مؤکل اور وکیل اگر دونوں قسمیں کھا لیں تو وہ عقد حکمی جو موکل اور وکیل کے درمیان منعقد ہوا ہے اس کو مسخ کر دیا جائے گا۔ اور جب مؤکل اور وکیل کے درمیان عقد حکمی فسخ ہو گیا تو وہ باندی وکیل کے سر پڑے گی۔ یعنی وکیل اس کا مالک ہوگا نہ کہ مؤکل ۔ پس نتیجہ کے طور پر اس صورت میں بھی ان ہی کا قول معتبر ہوا۔ مؤکل نے وکیل کو معین غلام خریدنے کا حکم دیا اور شمن بیان نہیں کئے وکیل نے غلام کو خرید لیا موکل نے کہا کہ تو نے پانچ سو کے عوض خریدا ہے اور وکیل نے کہا کہ ایک ہزار کے عوض خریدا ہے اور بائع نے وکیل کی تصدیق کی تو وکیل کا قول مع الیمین معتبر ہوگا
قال ولو امره ان يشترى له هذا العبد ولم يسم له ثمنا فاشتراه فقال الآمر اشتريته بخمسمائة وقال المامور بالف وصدق البائع المامور فالقول قول المامور مع يمينه قيل لا تحالف ههنا لانه ارتفع الخلاف بتصديق البائع اذهو حاضر وفي المسألة الأولى هو غائب فاعتبر الاختلاف وقيل يتحالفان لما ذكرنا وقد ذكر معظم يمين التحالف وهو يمين البائع والبائع بعد استيفاء الثمن اجنبي عنهما وقبله اجنبي عن المؤكل اذ لم يجر بينهما بيع فلا يصدق عليه فبقى الخلاف وهذا قول الامام أبي منصور وهو اظهر والله اعلم بالصواب
ترجمہ اور اگر موکل نے وکیل کو حکم دیا کہ اسکے واسطے یہ غلام خرید لے اور اس کا شمن بیان نہیں کیا ۔ پس وکیل نے اس غلام کو خرید لیا پھر موکل نے کہا کہ تو نے اس کو پانچ سو درہم کے عوض خریدا ہے اور وکیل نے کہا کہ ایک ہزار درہم کے عوض اور بائع نے وکیل کی تصدیق کی تو مع الیمین وکیل کا قول قبول ہو گا۔ کہا گیا ہے کہ اس جگہ باہمی قسم نہیں ہے کیونکہ بائع کی تصدیق سے اختلاف اٹھ گیا۔ اسلئے کہ بائع حاضر ہے اور پہلے مسئلہ میں بائع غائب تھا۔ اس وجہ سے اختلاف معتبر ہوا۔ اور کہا گیا ہے کہ دونوں قسم کھا ئیں گے ۔ اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے ذکر کی ہے۔ اور امام محمد نے تخالف میں سب سے بڑی قسم جو کر فرمائی وہ بائع کی قسم ہے اور بائع من حاصل کرنے کے بعد دونوں سے اجنبی ہے اور ثمن حاصل کرنے سے پہلے مؤکل سے اجنبی ہے۔ کیونکہ موکل اور اس بائع کے درمیان کوئی بیچ واقع نہیں ہوئی لہند موکل پر بائع کے قول کی تصدیق نہ ہوگی ۔ پس اختلاف باقی رہا اور یہ امام ابو منصور ماتریدی کا قول ہے اور یہی اظہر ہے ۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مؤکل نے وکیل کو ایک معین غلام خریدنے کا حکم دیا مگر اس غلام کا شمن بیان نہیں کیا۔ پس وکیل نے اس غلام کوخرید لیا۔ پھر مؤکل اور وکیل کے درمیان مقدار شمن میں اختلاف واقع ہوا۔ چنانچہ مؤکل نے اپنے وکیل سے کہا کہ تو نے یہ غلام پانچ سو روپیہ میں خریدا ہے۔ اور وکیل نے کہا کہ حضور ایسا نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ میں نے یہ غلام ایک ہزار روپیہ میں خریدا ہے اور غلام کے بائع نے بھی وکیل کے قول کی تصدیق کی تو وکیل کا قول مع الیمین معتبر ہو گا۔ مصنف ہدایہ نے کہا کہ بعض مشائخ مثلا فقیہ ابوجعفر ہندوانی کا قول یہ ہے کہ اس مسئلہ میں تخالف نہیں ہے۔ یعنی مؤکل اور وکیل
.

كتاب الوكالة
۲۳۸
اشرف البدایہ جلد دہم
دونوں سے قسمیں لے کر ان دونوں کے درمیان واقع ہونے والے عقد حکم کو فسخ نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ جیسا کہ گذشتہ مسئلہ میں تحالف کے بعد عقد حکمی کو فسخ کر دیا گیا تھا۔
اس قول کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ غلام کے بائع نے وکیل کے قول کی تصدیق کی ہے اور مسئلہ میں بائع چونکہ موجود ہے۔ اسلئے اس کا تصدیق کرنا معتبر بھی ہوگا اور جب بائع کا تصدیق کرنا معتبر ہے تو اس کے تصدیق کرنے کی وجہ سے مؤکل اور وکیل کے درمیان واقع شده اختلاف دور ہو جائے گا پس جب اختلاف دور ہو گیا تو غلام کے بائع اور وکیل دونوں کا مقدار ثمن یعنی ایک ہزار پر اتفاق کرنا ، انشاء عقد کے مرتبہ میں ہوگا ۔ یعنی ایسا ہو گا گویا غلام کے بائع اور وکیل کے درمیان ابھی ابھی ایک ہزار روپیہ کے عوض از سر نو بیع منعقد ہوئی ہے اور اگر غلام کے درمیان ایک ہزار روپیہ کے عوض انشاء عقد ہوتا یعنی از سرنو بیع منعقد ہوتی تو یہ بیچ موکل پر لازم ہوتی ۔ پس اسی طرح یہاں بھی اختلاف کی صورت میں وکیل کا قول معتبر ہو گا۔ اور غلام کی بیع مؤکل پر لا زم اور نافذ ہوگی ۔
اور گذشتہ مسئلہ میں بائع چونکہ موجود نہیں تھا۔ اس لئے اس کے تصدیق کرنے کا سوال ہی پیدا نہیں ہوتا۔ اور جب بائع کی طرف سے موجود ہیںتھا۔ کے کا ہی کی وکیل کے قول کی تصدیق نہیں پائی گنا تو وکیل اور موکل کے درمیان مقدارشمن میں اختلاف معتبر ہوگا اور تحالف واجب ہوگا کیونکہ مقدار ثمن میں اختلاف کا حکم یہی ہے کہ دونوں سے قسمیں لے کر عقد کو فتح کر دیا جائے جیسا کہ اس کی تفصیل گزر چکی ہے۔ اور بعض مشائخ مثلاً شیخ ابو منصور ماتریدی نے فرمایا ہے کہ گذشتہ مسئلہ کی طرح اس مسئلہ میں بھی تحالف واجب ہوگا ۔ دلیل سابق میں گذر چکی ہے کہ وکیل اور موکل دونوں بائع اور مشتری کے مرتبہ میں ہیں۔ اور دونوں کے درمیان مقدار شمن میں اختلاف کا حکم تخالف ہے لہذا اس مسئلہ میں بھی وکیل اور مؤکل دونوں سے قسمیں لے کر ان دونوں کے درمیان واقع شدہ عقد حکمی کو فسخ کر دیا جائے گا اور اس فتح کا نتیجہ یہ ہوگا کہ خریدا ہوا غلام مؤکل کیلئے نہ ہوگا۔ بلکہ وکیل کے لئے ہوگا۔
و قد ذكر معظم يمين التحالف ...... الخ سے ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔
سوال یہ ہے کہ جامع صغیر کے متن ولو امره ان يشترى هذا العبد ولم يسم له ثمنا ... الخ میں امام محمد نے یہ تصریح فرمائی ہے کہ وکیل کا قول مع الیمین معتبر ہو گا اور شیخ ابو منصور نے فرمایا کہ تحالف واجب ہو گا۔ حالانکہ تحالف امام محمد کی بیان کردہ تصریح کے مخالف ہے۔ اسلئے کہ تخالف میں وکیل اور مؤکل دونوں سے قسمیں لے کر ان دونوں کے درمیان واقع شدہ عقد حکمی کو مسخ کر دیا جاتا ہے اور امام محمد نے تصریح کی ہے کہ وکیل سے قسم لے کر اس کا قول معتبر مانا جائے گا۔
جواب .. اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مذکورہ مسئلہ میں وکیل تو بائع کے مرتبہ میں ہے اور مؤکل مشتری کے مرتبہ میں ہے اور تحالف میں اگر چہ بائع اور مشتری دونوں پر قسم واجب ہوتی ہے۔ لیکن بائع کی قسم اہم اور اعظم ہے اور بائع کی قسم اسلئے اعظم ہوتی ہے کہ مقدار شمن سے اختلاف میں بائع مدعی ہوتا ہے اور مشتری منکر ہوتا ہے اور مدعی پر صرف تخالف کی صورت میں قسم واجب ہوتی ہے۔ اس کے علاوہ میں اس پر قتم واجب نہیں ہوتی اور رہا منکر تو اس پر ہر حال میں قسم واجب ہوتی ہے۔ یعنی مخالف کی صورت میں بھی اور تخالف کے علاوہ بھی ۔ بہر حال بائع یعنی وکیل کی قسم تحالف کے ساتھ خاص ہے اور جب وکیل کی قسم تحالف کے ساتھ خاص ہے تو اس کی قسم، مؤکل کی قسم کے مقابلہ میں اہم اور اعظم ہوگی ۔ پس جب وکیل جو مدعی ہے اس پر قسم واجب ہے تو مو کل جو منکر ہے اس پر بدرجہ اولی قسم واجب ہوگی ۔
And if he ordered him to buy this slave for him and did not name a price, so he bought him. Then the commander said, 'You bought him for five hundred,' and the commanded said, 'For a thousand,' and the seller confirmed the commanded. So the word of the commanded with his oath is accepted. It was said: There is no mutual oath here because the dispute is removed by the confirmation of the seller, since he is present, whereas in the first case he was absent, so the dispute was considered. And it was said: They should take mutual oath due to what we mentioned. And Imam Muhammad mentioned the greatest oath of mutual oath, which is the oath of the seller. The seller, after receiving the price, is a stranger to both, and before receiving it, he is a stranger to the principal because no sale occurred between them, so his confirmation is not accepted regarding the principal. Thus the dispute remains, and this is the statement of Imam Abu Mansur, and it is more evident. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage discusses a dispute between a principal (muwakkil) and agent (wakil) over the price of a slave bought by the agent. The principal claims the price was 500, the agent claims it was 1000, and the seller confirms the agent's statement. The initial ruling from the matn (al-Hidayah) states that the agent's statement with oath is accepted. The commentary then presents two opinions within the Hanafi school. The first, attributed to Fakhr al-Islam Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani, holds that no mutual oath (tahāluf) occurs because the seller's confirmation resolves the dispute—since the seller is present, his confirmation is credible and effectively creates a new contract between the seller and the agent at the agreed price of 1000, which then binds the principal. The second, attributed to Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi and considered the more evident (azhar) position, says mutual oath is required because the seller is a stranger to the principal (no direct sale between them), so his confirmation does not affect the principal-agent dispute. The seller's oath is deemed the greatest (a'zam) in mutual oath. Thus, both parties must swear, and if they do, the constructive contract between principal and agent is annulled, and the slave becomes the agent's property. The passage also addresses a potential objection: Imam Muhammad's statement in al-Jami' al-Saghir that the agent's word with oath is accepted seems to contradict tahāluf. The answer is that in tahāluf, the burden of oath is on the seller (agent as claimant) primarily, and the buyer (principal as defendant) must also swear. Since the agent is the claimant (mudda'i) and the principal the defendant (munkir), both swear, but the agent's oath is emphasized. This does not conflict with Imam Muhammad's statement that the agent's word is accepted with oath, because tahāluf includes that.

Key Terms
تحالف (tahāluf): Mutual oath taking between two parties in a dispute over a contract, leading to annulment of the contract.
ثمن (thaman): The price in a sale contract; amount of money paid.
مؤکل (muwakkil): The principal who appoints an agent to perform a legal act.
وکیل (wakīl): The agent appointed to perform a specific task; in this case, to buy a slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where the seller confirms the agent's stated price, which Hanafi view is considered more evident (azhar) according to Ashraf al-Hidayah?
A) There is no mutual oath because the seller's confirmation removes the dispute.
B) Mutual oath is required because the seller is a stranger to the principal.
C) The principal's statement is accepted without oath.
D) The agent must pay the difference without oath.

Key Takeaway
The seller's confirmation does not preclude mutual oath between principal and agent; the more evident Hanafi view requires tahāluf.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
advanced
12 min
Dispute Over Price Between Agent and Principal When the Seller is Present
Expansion of a Hanafi dispute on tahalf in agency sales.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam Muhammad's ruling on tahalf in the presence of the seller and explain why it differs from Shaykh Abu Mansur's view.

Core Idea
If the seller confirms the price, the agent's oath suffices; no full tahalf is needed.

In a sale by an agent, when a price dispute arises between agent and principal, the normal course is mutual oath-taking (tahalf). But what if the original seller is present and confirms the agent's claim? This lesson examines the Hanafi dispute on whether the seller's presence eliminates the need for tahalf, focusing on the reasoning of Imam Muhammad and Shaykh Abu Mansur al-Maturidi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the factual scenario
The principal sends an agent to buy a specific slave. The agent buys it for 1,000. The principal disputes the price, claiming it was lower. The seller (ba'i) is present and confirms the agent's statement about the price.
2
State Imam Muhammad's ruling
Imam Muhammad holds that no tahalf is required. The agent's statement with an oath is accepted, and the sale binds the principal.
This is the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school.
3
Examine Imam Muhammad's proof
The seller's presence and confirmation remove the uncertainty about the price. The contract is treated as if newly concluded between seller and agent, which is binding on the principal.
The seller's verification (tasdiq) is legally valid and resolves the dispute.
4
State Shaykh Abu Mansur's opposing view
Shaykh Abu Mansur al-Maturidi argues that tahalf is still required because the agent and principal are analogous to seller and buyer, and any price dispute between them necessitates tahalf.
His proof is based on the general rule for price disputes.
5
Reconcile the two views
The answer to the question from Jami' al-Saghir shows that in tahalf, the claimant (seller-agent) takes an oath only in tahalf, while the denier (principal-buyer) always takes an oath. Thus, the agent's oath is already required, and the principal's is automatically necessary, making full mutual tahalf redundant.
Imam Muhammad's position is upheld by emphasizing that the agent's oath covers both roles.

دونوں سے قسمیں لے کر ان دونوں کے درمیان واقع ہونے والے عقد حکم کو فسخ نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ جیسا کہ گذشتہ مسئلہ میں تحالف کے بعد عقد حکمی کو فسخ کر دیا گیا تھا۔
اس قول کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ غلام کے بائع نے وکیل کے قول کی تصدیق کی ہے اور مسئلہ میں بائع چونکہ موجود ہے۔ اسلئے اس کا تصدیق کرنا معتبر بھی ہوگا اور جب بائع کا تصدیق کرنا معتبر ہے تو اس کے تصدیق کرنے کی وجہ سے مؤکل اور وکیل کے درمیان واقع شده اختلاف دور ہو جائے گا پس جب اختلاف دور ہو گیا تو غلام کے بائع اور وکیل دونوں کا مقدار ثمن یعنی ایک ہزار پر اتفاق کرنا ، انشاء عقد کے مرتبہ میں ہوگا ۔ یعنی ایسا ہو گا گویا غلام کے بائع اور وکیل کے درمیان ابھی ابھی ایک ہزار روپیہ کے عوض از سر نو بیع منعقد ہوئی ہے اور اگر غلام کے درمیان ایک ہزار روپیہ کے عوض انشاء عقد ہوتا یعنی از سرنو بیع منعقد ہوتی تو یہ بیچ موکل پر لازم ہوتی ۔ پس اسی طرح یہاں بھی اختلاف کی صورت میں وکیل کا قول معتبر ہو گا۔ اور غلام کی بیع مؤکل پر لا زم اور نافذ ہوگی ۔
اور گذشتہ مسئلہ میں بائع چونکہ موجود نہیں تھا۔ اس لئے اس کے تصدیق کرنے کا سوال ہی پیدا نہیں ہوتا۔ اور جب بائع کی طرف سے موجود نہ تھا۔ اس لئے [؟] وکیل کے قول کی تصدیق نہیں پائی گئی تو وکیل اور موکل کے درمیان مقدار ثمن میں اختلاف معتبر ہوگا اور تحالف واجب ہوگا کیونکہ مقدار ثمن میں اختلاف کا حکم یہی ہے کہ دونوں سے قسمیں لے کر عقد کو فتح کر دیا جائے جیسا کہ اس کی تفصیل گزر چکی ہے۔
اور بعض مشائخ مثلاً شیخ ابو منصور ماتریدی نے فرمایا ہے کہ گذشتہ مسئلہ کی طرح اس مسئلہ میں بھی تحالف واجب ہوگا ۔ دلیل سابق میں گذر چکی ہے کہ وکیل اور موکل دونوں بائع اور مشتری کے مرتبہ میں ہیں۔ اور دونوں کے درمیان مقدار شمن میں اختلاف کا حکم تخالف ہے لہذا اس مسئلہ میں بھی وکیل اور مؤکل دونوں سے قسمیں لے کر ان دونوں کے درمیان واقع شدہ عقد حکمی کو فسخ کر دیا جائے گا اور اس فتح کا نتیجہ یہ ہوگا کہ خریدا ہوا غلام مؤکل کیلئے نہ ہوگا۔ بلکہ وکیل کے لئے ہوگا۔
و قد ذكر معظم يمين التحالف ...... الخ سے ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔
سوال یہ ہے کہ جامع صغیر کے متن ولو امره ان يشترى هذا العبد ولم يسم له ثمنا ... الخ میں امام محمد نے یہ تصریح فرمائی ہے کہ وکیل کا قول مع الیمین معتبر ہو گا اور شیخ ابو منصور نے فرمایا کہ تحالف واجب ہو گا۔ حالانکہ تحالف امام محمد کی بیان کردہ تصریح کے مخالف ہے۔ اسلئے کہ تخالف میں وکیل اور مؤکل دونوں سے قسمیں لے کر ان دونوں کے درمیان واقع شدہ عقد حکمی کو مسخ کر دیا جاتا ہے اور امام محمد نے تصریح کی ہے کہ وکیل سے قسم لے کر اس کا قول معتبر مانا جائے گا۔
جواب .. اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مذکورہ مسئلہ میں وکیل تو بائع کے مرتبہ میں ہے اور مؤکل مشتری کے مرتبہ میں ہے اور تحالف میں اگر چہ بائع اور مشتری دونوں پر قسم واجب ہوتی ہے۔ لیکن بائع کی قسم اہم اور اعظم ہے اور بائع کی قسم اسلئے اعظم ہوتی ہے کہ مقدار شمن سے اختلاف میں بائع مدعی ہوتا ہے اور مشتری منکر ہوتا ہے اور مدعی پر صرف تخالف کی صورت میں قسم واجب ہوتی ہے۔ اس کے علاوہ میں اس پر قسم واجب نہیں ہوتی اور رہا منکر تو اس پر ہر حال میں قسم واجب ہوتی ہے۔ یعنی مخالف کی صورت میں بھی اور تخالف کے علاوہ بھی ۔ بہر حال بائع یعنی وکیل کی قسم تحالف کے ساتھ خاص ہے اور جب وکیل کی قسم تحالف کے ساتھ خاص ہے تو اس کی قسم، مؤکل کی قسم کے مقابلہ میں اہم اور اعظم ہوگی ۔ پس جب وکیل جو مدعی ہے اس پر قسم واجب ہے تو مو کل جو منکر ہے اس پر بدرجہ اولی قسم واجب ہوگی ۔
They will not rescind the judicial contract that occurred between them by taking oaths from both. As in the previous issue, the judicial contract was rescinded after tahalf. The proof of this statement is that the seller of the slave has verified the statement of the agent, and in the issue the seller is present, so his verification is valid. When the seller's verification is valid, the dispute between the principal and agent is removed due to his verification. So when the dispute is removed, the agreement of the slave's seller and the agent on the amount of the price, i.e., one thousand, is in the rank of concluding the contract. That is, it is as if a new sale has just been concluded between the slave's seller and the agent for one thousand rupees, and if a contract had been concluded between them for one thousand rupees - i.e., a new sale - this sale would have been binding on the principal. Similarly here, in case of dispute, the agent's statement is accepted, and the sale of the slave will be binding and effective on the principal. In the previous issue, since the seller was not present, the question of his verification does not arise. And when the seller was not present, so [؟] the agent's statement was not verified, then the dispute between the agent and principal over the amount of the price will be considered valid, and tahalf will be obligatory, because the ruling on a dispute over the amount of the price is that oaths are taken from both and the contract is annulled, as its detail has already passed. And some mashayikh, for example Shaykh Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, have said that in this issue too, tahalf will be obligatory like the previous issue. The proof has already passed that the agent and principal are in the position of seller and buyer, and the ruling on a dispute between them over the amount of the price is tahalf, so here too, oaths will be taken from both the agent and principal, and the judicial contract between them will be rescinded, and the result of this annulment will be that the purchased slave will not be for the principal, but for the agent. And 'wa qad dhakara mu'azzam yamin al-tahalf...' etc. is an answer to a question. The question is that in the text of Jami' al-Saghir: 'wa law amrahu an yashtari hadha al-abda wa lam yusamma lahu thaman...' etc., Imam Muhammad has clearly stated that the agent's statement with an oath is accepted, and Shaykh Abu Mansur has said that tahalf is obligatory, while tahalf contradicts Imam Muhammad's explicit statement, because in tahalf, oaths are taken from both agent and principal and the judicial contract between them is annulled, and Imam Muhammad has stated that an oath is taken from the agent and his statement is accepted. The answer: In the mentioned issue, the agent is in the position of the seller and the principal in the position of the buyer. In tahalf, although oaths are obligatory on both seller and buyer, the seller's oath is more important and greater. The seller's oath is greater because in a dispute over the amount of the price, the seller is the claimant and the buyer is the denier. An oath is obligatory on the claimant only in the case of tahalf; otherwise, no oath is obligatory on him. As for the denier, an oath is obligatory on him in all circumstances, i.e., both in the case of tahalf and otherwise. In any case, the oath of the seller, i.e., the agent, is specific to tahalf, and when his oath is specific to tahalf, his oath will be more important and greater compared to the principal's oath. So when the agent, who is the claimant, is required to take an oath, then the principal, who is the denier, is even more deserving of an oath.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the requirement of mutual oath-taking (tahalf) between an agent (wakil) and his principal (muwakkil) when they dispute the price of a purchased item, and the original seller (ba'i) is present. The main ruling, attributed to Imam Muhammad, is that if the seller is present and confirms the agent's statement about the price, no tahalf is needed. Instead, the agent's statement is accepted with an oath, and the sale is binding on the principal. The reasoning is that the seller's confirmation removes the dispute, effectively making the contract as if newly concluded between the seller and the agent. In contrast, if the seller were absent, tahalf would be required. Shaykh Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, however, holds that tahalf is still required even with the seller present, because the agent and principal stand in the position of seller and buyer, and any price dispute between them triggers tahalf. The passage then presents a question reconciling Imam Muhammad's explicit statement from al-Jami' al-Saghir that the agent's statement with an oath is accepted, with Shaykh Abu Mansur's call for tahalf. The answer clarifies that the roles differ: the agent is like the seller (claimant) and the principal like the buyer (denier). In tahalf, the claimant's oath is only required in tahalf itself, while the denier must take an oath in all cases. Thus, the agent's oath is already required, and the principal's oath is a fortiori necessary. This resolution preserves Imam Muhammad's position as the relied-upon view, with the understanding that the agent's oath suffices without full mutual tahalf. The practical consequence is that in the seller's presence, the agent's statement binds the principal, and the slave purchased belongs to the principal.

Key Terms
تحالف (tahalf): Mutual oath-taking between two disputing parties, each swearing to their claim, leading to rescission of the contract.
تصدیق (tasdiq): Verification or confirmation, here by the seller of the agent's statement about the price.
مقدار ثمن (miqdar al-thaman): The specific amount of the price in a sale contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where the seller is present and confirms the agent's statement about the price, what is the Hanafi ruling according to Imam Muhammad?
A) Tahalf is required between agent and principal.
B) The agent's statement with an oath is accepted, and the sale binds the principal.
C) The contract is automatically rescinded.
D) The principal's statement is accepted without oath.

Key Takeaway
When the seller is present and confirms the price, the agent's oath suffices to bind the principal; no full tahalf is required.

Slave as Agent to Purchase Himself: Three Scenarios
Commentary on three scenarios of slave's agency to buy himself

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three outcomes when a slave agent buys himself and explain the legal reasoning for each.

Core Idea
A slave cannot own himself, so a self-purchase contract defaults to manumission if not attributed to a principal.

This lesson examines a unique case in Hanafi agency law: a slave appointed by a free person to buy himself from his master. The slave's dual nature—human and property—creates distinct rulings depending on how the contract is phrased. The commentary from Al-Hidayah provides three scenarios and the reasoning behind each.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
List the three possible ways the slave agent can frame the purchase: attributing to principal, contracting for himself, or the general objection about specific agency.
2
Analyze the outcome for each scenario
For each, determine the legal result: purchase for principal, manumission, or manumission (with objection resolved). Note the conditions that trigger each result.
3
Understand the dual nature of the slave
Grasp the Hanafi principle that a slave has two aspects: human (with legal capacity) and property (owned). This duality allows him to be an agent for another to purchase himself, but not to own himself.
4
Apply the qiyas (analogical reasoning)
See how the slave's inability to own makes his self-contract a different genus (manumission) compared to a free agent buying a specific item for himself.
5
Connect to practical implications
Consider the effect on the master's right to detain the slave after sale: if the slave is authorized to trade, his value is in his possession, so the master cannot detain him for payment.

یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر غلام نے اپنی مالیت کا اپنے مولی کے علاوہ کسی دوسرے کیلئے اقرار کیا اور یہ کہا کہ میں فلاں کا غلام ہوں تو یہ اقرار درست نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ کسی شخص کو یہ حق نہیں ہے کہ وہ دوسرے کے مال کا کسی کیلئے اقرار کرے۔ اور بیع ، غلام پر اس کے مال ہونے کی حیثیت سے وارد ہوتی ہے نہ کہ اس کے آدمی ہونے کی حیثیت سے۔ یعنی غلام کی خرید و فروخت اسلئے ہوتی ہے کہ وہ مال ہے اور اسلئے نہیں ہوتی کہ وہ آدمی ہے۔ پس جب غلام کی آدمیت اور مالیت الگ الگ دو چیزیں ہیں تو غلام کو خود اس کی ذات خریدنے کا وکیل کرنا ایسا ہے۔ جیسا کہ مولیٰ کے اموال میں سے کسی دوسر نے مال کو خریدنے کا، کیل کرنا یا غلام کے علاوہ دوسرے آدمی کو غلام خریدنے کا وکیل کرنا ۔ اور غلام کو اس کی ذات کے علاوہ مولی کے دوسرے مال کو خریدنے کا وکیل کرنا اور غلام کے علاوہ دوسرے آدمی کو غلام خریدنے کا وکیل کرنا دونوں جائز ہیں۔ تو غلام کو خود اس کی ذات خریدنے کا وکیل کرنا بھی جائز ہوگا۔ بہر حال یہ بات ثابت ہو گئی کہ غلام دوسرے آدمی کی طرف سے اپنی ذات کو خریدنے کا وکیل ہوسکتا ہے۔
الا ان مالیته فی یدہ سے صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ غلام کی آدمیت اور مالیت میں اگر تغایر ہے اور یہ الگ الگ دو چیزیں ہیں۔ مگر چونکہ غلام مازون لہ فی التجارت ہے۔ اسلئے اس کی مالیت خود اس کے قبضہ میں ہے۔ اور غلام کی مالیت خود غلام کے قبضہ میں ہونے کا اثر یہ ہو گا کہ مولیٰ اور غلام کے درمیان عقد بیع واقع ہونے کے بعد اگر مولی (بائع ) شن وصول کرنے کیلئے غلام کو روکنا چاہے تو اس کو یہ اختیار ہرگز حاصل نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ جب بائع ہیچ کو سپرد کر دیتا ہے تو پھر اس کوشن وصول کرنے کی وجہ سے مبیع روکنے کا اختیار نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ جیسا کہ مودع (جس کے پاس امانت رکھی گئی ہے) نے اگر مالک سے ودیعت کو خرید لیا اور ودیعت ، مودع کے پاس موجود ہے تو بائع مالک کوشن وصول کرنے کی خاطر ودیعت کا سامان روکنے کا حق نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ودیعت کا سامان مودع کے سپرد کر دیا گیا ہے۔ اسی
Book of Agency. ... The commentary discusses: (1) If the slave attributes the contract to his principal, the purchase is for the principal. (2) If the slave contracts for himself, he becomes free because it is manumission. (3) An objection answered: the slave is appointed to buy a specific thing (himself), but he acts for himself; however, since he is a slave, he cannot own, so it is manumission. Then the text explains the dual nature of the slave (human and property) and that the slave's value is in his possession (if authorized to trade), so the master cannot detain him after sale. Analogy with wadi'ah.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah (Ashraf al-Hidayah) addresses rulings concerning a slave appointed as an agent to purchase himself from his master for another person. The passage is an expansion probe explaining three scenarios. 

First scenario: If the slave (as agent) attributes the contract to his principal (muwakkil) by saying to his master, 'Sell me to so-and-so (my principal) for such price,' then the purchase is for the principal, not the slave. This is because the slave can be an agent for another in this matter due to his dual nature: he is both a human (with legal capacity) and property. Since the act complies with the principal's command, the contract takes effect for the principal.

Second scenario: If the slave contracts for himself (e.g., says 'Sell me to myself'), he becomes free. This is because a slave cannot own property, so he cannot buy himself. The transaction is legally interpreted as manumission (i'taq) by the master, and the slave's acceptance is acceptance of freedom. The master is considered to have consented to manumission, not a sale.

Third scenario: The passage addresses an objection: if the slave is appointed to buy a specific thing (himself), normally an agent cannot buy that specific thing for himself. However, here the slave's action (contracting for himself) is a different type of transaction (manumission), which overrides the agency. Therefore, the contract is effective for the slave (as manumission), not for the principal.

The commentary further explains the underlying legal reasoning: the slave's humanity and property status are distinct. The sale of a slave is based on property status, but agency to purchase the slave's own self is permissible because of the human aspect. Additionally, if the slave is authorized to trade (ma'dhun lahu fi al-tijarah), his value is considered in his possession, so after the sale, the master cannot detain the slave to collect the price, just as in the case of wadi'ah where the depositee who buys the deposited item cannot be detained after delivery.

Key Terms
وکالت (wakalah): Agency; the delegation of authority to another to perform a legal act.
غلام (ghulam): A male slave; in this context, a slave who is capable of entering contracts with master's permission.
اعتاق (i'taq): Manumission; freeing a slave. In this passage, the transaction is legally considered manumission when a slave attempts to buy himself.
مالیت (maliyyah): Property status; the quality of being owned as property. The slave has a dual nature: human and property.
ماذون له فی التجارة (ma'dhun lahu fi al-tijarah): A slave authorized by his master to engage in trade; such a slave has possession of his own value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if a slave agent contracts to buy himself from his master without attributing to the principal, what is the legal outcome?
A) The slave becomes the property of the principal.
B) The slave becomes free (manumission).
C) The sale is void and the slave remains enslaved.
D) The slave must pay the price and remains a slave.

Key Takeaway
A slave's self-purchase contract is manumission, not sale, because the slave cannot own; attribution to a principal changes the outcome to a valid purchase for that principal.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Agent Buying a Slave for the Slave Himself Must Clarify
Ruling on agent's duty to clarify purchase for slave's own emancipation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligation of an agent to clarify the purchase when buying a slave for the slave himself, and explain the legal consequences of failing to do so.

Core Idea
An agent buying a slave for the slave himself must clarify; silence makes the agent the buyer.

In Hanafi fiqh, when a slave appoints an agent to buy him from his master, the agent faces a crucial choice: should he simply purchase or explicitly state that he is buying for the slave? This passage from al-Hidayah clarifies the ruling, emphasizing the agent's duty to disclose the true intention to allow the master an informed decision between sale and emancipation, each with distinct legal effects.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is an agent buying a slave for the slave himself. The ruling is that it is wajib (obligatory) for the agent to explicitly state that the purchase is for the slave.
The obligation arises because the master's choice between sale and emancipation is affected.
2
Locate the illah (ratio legis)
The reason is that the master may prefer a pure sale over emancipation in exchange for property (i'taq 'ala mal). Emancipation gives the master clientage (wala') but also makes him the 'aqila, liable for the slave's future crimes.
The illah is the potential harm to the master if his preference is ignored.
3
Consequence of non-clarification
If the agent does not clarify, the purchase is deemed for the agent himself. The agent becomes liable for the price, and the master sells to the agent, not the slave.
Clarification is necessary to ensure the contract is attributed to the slave.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a difference in riwayah regarding whether the agent can be demanded for the price even when he attributes the purchase to the slave. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that the agent is not liable for the price when he clarifies.
This ikhtilaf shows the richness of Hanafi legal reasoning.
5
Understand the thamarah (practical effect)
The practical consequence: the master gets to choose the type of transaction. The agent must facilitate this choice by a clear statement. If he fails, the master is entitled to demand the price from the agent.
The ruling protects the master's rights and ensures transparency.
