غبن فاحش کی تعریف
قال والذي لا يتغابن الناس فيه ما لا يدخل تحت تقويم المقومين وقيل في العروض دہ نیم و في الحيوانات دہ یازده و في العقارات دہ دواز ده لان التصرف يكثر وجوده في الأول ويقل في الاخير ويتوسط في الأوسط وكثرة الغبن لقلة التصرف
ترجمہ اور وہ خسارہ جس کو لوگ نہیں اٹھاتے ہیں وہ ہے جو اندازہ لگانے والوں کے انداز کے تحت داخل نہ ہو۔ اور کہا گیا کہ سامان میں دس کی چیز ساڑھے دس میں ہو اور جانوروں میں دس کا جانور گیارہ کا ہو اور زمین وغیرہ غیر منقول جائداد میں دس کے بارہ ہوں ۔ کیونکہ تصرف کا وجود اول میں زیادہ ہے اور اخیر میں کم ہے اور اوسط میں درمیانی ہے اور غین کی زیادتی قلت تصرف کی وجہ سے ہوتی ہے۔
تشریح صاحب قدری نے لا يتغابن الناس فيه سے غبن فاحش کو تعبیر کیا ہے اور غبن فاحش کی تعریف کی ہے کہ غبن فاحش ایسے خسارہ کا نام ہے جو ماہرین تجارت کے اندازے میں داخل نہ ہو یعنی جو لوگ تجارت کے مالک ہیں ان میں سے کوئی شخص اس قدر مال کے عوض اندازہ نہ کرے۔ بہر حال جب لا يتغابن الناس فيه غبن فاحش ہے تو اس کا مقابل ما يتغابن الناس فيه غبن یسیر ہو گا اور جب غبن فاحش کی تعریف مالا يدخل تحت تقويم المقومين ہے تو غبن یسیر کی تعریف ما يدخل تحت تقويم المقومين ہوگی۔ یعنی ایسا خسارہ جو ماہرین تجارت کے اندازے میں نہ آئے اور وہ غبن یسیر ہے۔
مصنف قدوری کا ظاہر کلام وقيل في العروض دہ نیم الخ اس پر دال ہے کہ یہ غبن فاحش تفسیر ہے یعنی سامان میں غبن فاحش یہ ہے کہ دس درہم کی چیز ساڑھے دس درہم میں ہو جانوروں میں غبن فاحش یہ ہے کہ دس درہم کا جانور گیارہ درہم میں ہو اور غیر منقولہ جائدادزمین، مکان وغیرہ میں غبن فاحش یہ ہے کہ دس درہم کی زمین بارہ درہم میں ہو۔ مگر صاحب فتح القدیر نے کہا کہ میرے نزدیک حق یہ ہے کہ یہ غبن یسیر کی تفسیر ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ بات جمہور فقہاء اور عامتہ المشائخ کے ذکر کردہ بیان کے مطابق ہے۔ اور یہی صاحب نہایہ نے تحریر فرمایا ہے۔ پس غبن اگر مذکورہ مقدار کے مطابق ہو تو وہ غبن یسیر کہلائے گا۔ اور عقد شراء موکل پر لازم اور نافذ ہوگا اور اگر اس مقدار سے زائد ہو تو وہ غبن فاحش کہلائے گا۔ اور عقد شراء وکیل پر لازم اور نافذ ہوگا۔
دلیل اس کی دلیل کہ مذکورہ مقدار غبن یسیر اور اس سے زائد غبن فاحش ہے یہ ہے کہ غبن اس وقت زیادہ ہوتا ہے جب آدمی کو تجربہ کم ہو اور جب تجربہ زیادہ ہو غبن کم ہوتا ہے اور تجربہ کی قلت اور کثرت تصرف کی قلت اور کثرت سے ہوتی ہے۔ یعنی تصرف اور وقوع تجارت کی زیادتی سے تجربہ زیادہ ہو گا۔ اور تصرف اور وقوع تجارت کی کمی سے تجربہ کم ہوگا اور یہ بات ظاہر ہے کہ سامان میں تجارت کا وقوع زیادہ ہوتا ہے اور زمین وغیرہ غیر منقول جائداد میں تجارت کا وقوع کم ہوتا ہے۔ اور جانوروں میں تجارت کا وقوع اوسط درجہ کا ہوتا ہے۔ پھر چونکہ دس درہم ایسا نصاب ہے جس کے سرقہ سے قطع ید ہو جاتا ہے۔ اسلئے غبن یسیر کی تفسیر میں دس درہم کو اصل قرار دیا گیا ہے۔ اور ایک درہم ایسا مال ہے جس کی وجہ سے انسان کو قید خانہ میں ڈال دیا جاتا ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ تنگی اور بل کے مواقع (تجارت میں ایک درہم کے ساتھ چشم پوشی نہیں کی جاتی ہے۔ یعنی بائع ثمن ٹھہر جانے کے بعد ایک درہم چھوڑنے کا روادار نہیں ہوتا ہے اور نہ ہی مشتری ایک درہم زائد دینے کا روادار ہوتا ہے۔ بہر حال جب ایسا ہے تو سامان جس میں تجارت کا وقوع کثیر ہے اس میں ایک درہم کو غبن یسیر نہیں سمجھا جائے گا۔ ہاں نصف درہم چونکہ اس درجہ اہم نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے سامان کی تجارت میں نصف درہم غبن یسیر شمار ہوگا اور جانوروں کی تجارت چونکہ اس کی تجارت کے وقوع سے کم ہے۔ اسلئے جانوروں کی تجارت میں نصف درہم کا دو چند یعنی ایک درہم غبن یسیر شمار ہوگا ۔ اور زمین وغیرہ کی تجارت کا وقوع چونکہ جانوروں کی تجارت کے وقوع سے بھی کم ہے۔ اسلئے زمین کی تجارت میں ایک درہم کا دو چند یعنی دو درہم غبن یسیر شمار ہوں گے۔
Definition of ghaban fahish. He said: That which people do not overlook is that which does not fall within the estimation of the valuers. And it was said: in goods, ten [and] half [i.e., 10.5]; in animals, ten [and] eleven [i.e., 11]; in real estate, ten [and] twelve [i.e., 12] because transactions occur frequently in the first, rarely in the last, and moderately in the middle; and the greatness of the overpayment is due to the rarity of transactions. Translation: The loss that people do not accept is that which does not fall within the estimation of the assessors. And it was said: in goods, an item worth ten is [bought for] ten and a half; in animals, an animal worth ten is [bought for] eleven; in land and other immovable property, ten [is bought for] twelve. Because the occurrence of transactions is frequent in the first, rare in the last, and moderate in the middle; and the magnitude of the overpayment is due to the rarity of transactions. Explanation: Sahib Quduri interpreted 'la yataghāban al-nās fīhi' as ghaban fahish and defined ghaban fahish as a loss that does not fall within the estimation of trade experts, i.e., no person who owns trade would estimate a property at that value. In any case, when 'la yataghāban al-nās fīhi' is ghaban fahish, then its opposite 'ma yataghāban al-nās fīhi' is ghaban yasir. And when ghaban fahish is defined as 'mā lā yadkhulu taḥta taqwīm al-muqawwimīn', then ghaban yasir is defined as 'mā yadkhulu taḥta taqwīm al-muqawwimīn' — i.e., a loss that falls within the estimation of trade experts. The apparent statement of the author (Quduri) 'wa qīla fī al-ʿurūḍ dah nīm' etc. indicates that this is an interpretation of ghaban fahish: in goods, ghaban fahish is that an item worth ten dirhams is [bought for] ten and a half; in animals, an animal worth ten dirhams is [bought for] eleven; in immovable property like land and houses, a land worth ten dirhams is [bought for] twelve. However, Sahib Fath al-Qadir said: In my view the truth is that this is an interpretation of ghaban yasir, because this matches the statement mentioned by the majority of jurists and the generality of the mashayikh, and Sahib al-Nihaya has written this. So if the overpayment corresponds to the mentioned amount, it is called ghaban yasir, and the purchase contract is binding on the principal; if it exceeds this amount, it is called ghaban fahish, and the purchase contract is binding on the agent. Evidence: The proof that the mentioned amount is ghaban yasir and above it is ghaban fahish is that the overpayment is great when a person has little experience, and when experience is great, the overpayment is small; and the lack or abundance of experience comes from the lack or abundance of transactions. That is, with the increase of transactions and occurrence of trade, experience increases; with the decrease of transactions and occurrence of trade, experience decreases. It is obvious that trade in goods occurs frequently, trade in land and other immovable property occurs rarely, and trade in animals occurs at an intermediate level. Then, since ten dirhams is the threshold (nisab) for which amputation of the hand becomes mandatory in theft, ten dirhams is taken as the basis in the interpretation of ghaban yasir. And one dirham is such wealth for which a person can be imprisoned. For this reason, in times of scarcity and difficulty, one dirham is not overlooked in trade; i.e., a seller, after fixing the price, does not tolerate giving up one dirham, nor does a buyer tolerate paying one extra dirham. In any case, when this is the case, in goods where trade occurs frequently, one dirham is not considered ghaban yasir; rather, half a dirham is considered ghaban yasir because it is not of such importance. In the trade of animals, since its trade occurrence is less than that of goods, the excess of half a dirham is doubled, i.e., one dirham is considered ghaban yasir. And in the trade of land, since its trade occurrence is even less than that of animals, the excess of one dirham is doubled, i.e., two dirhams are considered ghaban yasir.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage is a definition-ruling with proof (talil) for the concept of ghaban fahish (major overpayment) and its opposite, ghaban yasir (minor overpayment), in Hanafi law of agency and sales. The text first presents the general definition: ghaban fahish is what people do not overlook, i.e., it does not fall within the range of valuers' estimation. Then it gives specific numerical thresholds as transmitted from earlier scholars: for trade goods (urud), a half-dirham on a ten-dirham item; for animals, one dirham on ten; for real estate, two dirhams on ten. The text then notes a difference of interpretation: the author of Fath al-Qadir and the majority of later scholars (including the author of al-Nihaya) maintain that these thresholds actually define ghaban yasir, not ghaban fahish. Thus, any overpayment up to these amounts is considered minor (ghaban yasir) and binding on the principal if done by an agent; any amount above is major (ghaban fahish) and binding on the agent. The passage then provides a rational proof (talil) for these specific amounts based on the frequency of transactions and human experience: goods are traded frequently, so a small overpayment of half a dirham is considered negligible (ghaban yasir) because people have wide experience and know the market; animals are traded less frequently, so a full dirham is considered negligible; real estate is traded least, so two dirhams are negligible. The basis of ten dirhams is derived from the theft nisab (the minimum value for amputation). The reasoning establishes that the thresholds are based on common commercial practice and human nature, not arbitrary numbers. The authority weight is from the later Hanafi commentary literature (Ashraf al-Hidayah), but the original definitions are rooted in the works of al-Quduri and the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
غبن فاحش (ghaban fahish): A major overpayment that people do not overlook; defined as what does not fall within the estimation of valuers. Quantified as exceeding half a dirham on ten dirhams goods, one dirham on ten dirhams animals, or two dirhams on ten dirhams real estate.
غبن يبیر (ghaban yasir): A minor overpayment that people do overlook; defined as what falls within the estimation of valuers. Quantified as exactly half a dirham on ten dirhams goods, one dirham on ten dirhams animals, or two dirhams on ten dirhams real estate.
تقويم المقومين (taqwīm al-muqawwimīn): The estimation or valuation made by expert assessors (valuers) in trade. What falls within their estimation is ghaban yasir; what does not is ghaban fahish.
نصاب (nisāb): The minimum value (ten dirhams) for which amputation of the hand is required for theft. Used as a basis for the ten-dirham reference in ghaban.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view (Fath al-Qadir, al-Nihaya), what is the threshold for ghaban yasir in the trade of animals?
A) Half a dirham on a ten-dirham animal
B) One dirham on a ten-dirham animal
C) Two dirhams on a ten-dirham animal
D) Three dirhams on a ten-dirham animal

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, ghaban yasir (up to half/one/two dirhams per ten) binds the principal, while ghaban fahish (above those amounts) makes the agent liable; these thresholds are based on trade frequency and the theft nisab.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Selling Half the Slave: Dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on selling half the slave by an agent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding an agent selling half a slave, and apply the qiyas awlawi and istihsan reasoning to resolve the dispute.

Core Idea
An absolute agency to sell covers half the item according to Abu Hanifa but not according to the Sahibayn unless the other half is also sold.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute on the scope of an agent's authority when the principal says 'sell my slave' without specifying whole or half. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the agent may sell half because the absolute wording includes it, and using a fortiori reasoning (qiyas awlawi) from the case of selling the whole for half price. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) disagree, arguing that custom (mutāraf) restricts the absolute to whole sale, and that selling half causes harm (ḍarar) through partnership. However, they make an exception via istihsan: if the agent sells the other half before any dispute, the first half-sale becomes a valid means to fulfill the principal's command. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to balance textual interpretation, custom, and juristic preference within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
What is the precise legal question? A principal authorizes an agent to sell his slave without specifying whole or half. The agent sells only half. Is the sale valid and binding on the principal?
The dispute is about the scope of an absolute authorization: does it include partial sale?
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa says the sale is valid. His proof: the wording is absolute (mutlaq), and according to the principle 'al-mutlaq yajri 'ala itlaqihi', it covers both whole and half. He uses qiyas awlawi: if selling the whole for half the price is valid (according to him), then selling half for half is a fortiori more beneficial and thus valid.
The qiyas awlawi is based on the idea that lesser harm (selling half) is preferable to greater harm (selling whole for half).
3
State the Sahibayn's position and proofs
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say the sale is not valid. First proof: absolute words are interpreted according to custom (mutāraf), and selling half is not customary; thus the agency does not include half, so the agent contradicts the principal. Second proof: selling half creates a harmful partnership (shirkah) in the slave, and the agent may not harm the principal.
The custom-based argument restricts the absolute, while the harm argument invokes the principle of preventing harm.
4
Analyze the exception (istihsan) of the Sahibayn
The Sahibayn allow an exception: if the agent sells the other half before any dispute (mukhasama), the first half-sale becomes valid. This is because the first sale was a means (wasīlah) to ultimately sell the whole slave, and istihsan permits departing from strict analogy to achieve the principal's objective.
The exception is based on necessity: when the agent cannot find a buyer for the whole, selling in parts may be the only way.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference? Under Abu Hanifa, the buyer immediately becomes half-owner. Under the Sahibayn, unless the other half is sold before objection, the sale is void and the buyer must return the half.
The consequence affects third-party rights and the stability of transactions.

یہ خیال رہے کہ پورے غلام کو آدھے شمن کے عوض بیچنا صرف امام صاحب کے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ اس وجہ سے یجوز عندہ کہا گیا ہے ورنہ صاحبین کے نزدیک نا جائز ہے کیونکہ پورے غلام کو نصف شمن کے عوض بیچنے میں غبن فاحش ہے اور غبن فاحش کے ساتھ بیچنا صاحبین کے نزدیک ناجائز ہے۔ جیسا کہ پہلے گزر چکا ہے۔

شرف الہدایہ جلد دہم

كتاب الوكالة
اپنا غلام بیچنے کا وکیل کیا پورے یا آدھے کو فروخت کرنے کی قید نہیں لگائی
وکیل آدھا غلام فروخت کرے تو کیا حکم ہے
قال واذا وكله ببيع عبد له فباع نصفه جاز عند ابي حنيفةً لان اللفظ مطلق من قيد الافتراق والاجتماع الاترى انه لوباع الكل بثمن النصف يجوز عنده فاذا باع النصف به اولی و قالا لا يجوز لانه غير متعارف ولما فيه من ضرر الشركة الا ان يبيع النصف الأخر قبل ان يختصمالان بيع النصف قد يقع وسيلة الى الامتثال بان لا يجد من يشتريه جملة فيحتاج الى ان يفرق فاذا باع الباقى قبل نقض البيع الأول تبين انه قع وسيلة واذا لم يبع ظهر انه لم يقع وسيلة فلا يجوز وهذا استحسان عندهما ترجمہ اور جب اپنا غلام بیچنے کا وکیل کیا۔ پس وکیل نے آدھا غلام فروخت کیا تو حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ اسلئے کہ لفظ کل یا بعض کی قید سے مطلق ہے کیا تم نہیں دیکھتے ہو کہ اگر اس نے پورے غلام کو نصف عوض فروخت کر دیا تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ پس جب نصف شمن کے عوض نصف غلام بیچا تو بدرجہ اولی جائز ہے اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ متعارف نہیں ہے اور اس وجہ سے کہ اس میں شرکت کا ضرر ہے۔ مگر یہ کہ نصف آخر کو وکیل اور موکل کے مخاصمہ سے پہلے فروخت کر دے۔ اسلئے نصف فروخت کرنا کبھی موکل کے حکم کی تھی کا ذریعہ ہو جاتا ہے۔ بایں طور کہ وکیل کو ایسا شخص بیل جائے جو پورے غلام کو یکبارگی خریدے پس وہ متفرق کر کے فروخت کرنے کا محتاج ہو گا۔ پس جب نصف اول کی بیچ ٹوٹنے سے پہلے باقی نصف کو ۔ فروخت کر دیا تو ظاہر ہو گیا کہ نصف اول فروخت کر نا تعمیل حکم کا ذریعہ واقع ہوا تھا اور جب وکیل نے باقی نصف فروخت نہیں کیا تو ظاہر ہو گیا کہ وہ تعمیل حکم کے ذریعہ واقع نہیں ہوا تھا۔ لہذا جائز نہ ہوگا اور یہ صاحبین کے نزدیک استحسان ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے دوسرے شخص کو اپنا غلام فروخت کرنے کا وکیل کیا ۔ اور پورے یا آدھے کو فروخت کرنے کی قید کے ساتھ مقید نہیں کیا۔ پس وکیل نے آدھا غلام فروخت کر دیا تو حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک یہ بیع جائز ہے اور اس کا نفاذ موکل پر ہوگا ۔۔
اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ یہ بیع جائز نہیں ہے یعنی اس بیع کا نفاذ موکل پر نہیں ہو گا۔ حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ موکل کا کلام یعنی غلام فروخت کرنے کا حکم مطلق ہے نہ اس میں پورے غلام کی قید ہے اور نہ آدھے غلام کی قید ہے اور المطلق یجری علی اطلاقہ کے تحت مطلق اپنے اطلاق پر جاری ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا اس اطلاق کے پیش نظر وکیل پورے غلام کو بیچنے کا بھی مجاز ہے۔ اور آدھے غلام کو بیچنے کا بھی مجاز ہے۔ اور جب وکیل آدھے غلام کو فروخت کرنے کا مجاز ہے تو اس کا آدھے غلام کو فروخت کرنا جائز ہوگا۔ اور اس کا نفاذ موکل پر ہوگا۔ اس دلیل کو مزید واضح کرانے کیلئے صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ اگر مذکورہ وکیل پورے غلام کو نصف شمن کے بقدر کے عوض فروخت کر دے۔ مثلاً ایک ہزار روپیہ کے غلام کو پانچ سوروپیہ کے عوض فروخت کر دے تو حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ پس جب امام صاحب کے نزدیک پورے غلام کو نصف شمن کے بقدر کے عوض بیچنا جائز ہے تو آدھے غلام کو نصف شمن کے عوض بیچنا بدرجہ اولی جائز ہوگا۔
Chapter of Agency. Ashraf al-Hidayah Volume 10. Because selling half the slave for half the price and keeping half the slave gives the principal more benefit. This is relative to selling the whole slave for half the price. Because in the first case the principal gets half the price and half the slave remains with him, while in the second case half the price is obtained but no part of the slave remains. Therefore the first case is more beneficial for the principal, and the second case is less beneficial. So when the less beneficial case (selling the whole for half) is permissible, the more beneficial case (selling half for half) is a fortiori permissible. But if you object that selling the whole for half is permissible because it does not entail the defect of partnership, while selling half for half is impermissible because it entails the defect of partnership, i.e., the principal and buyer become partners in the slave, and partnership is a defect. Since this sale involves the defect of partnership, it is a contradiction of the principal's command, and the agent is not allowed to contradict the principal's command, so this sale is not valid and does not bind the principal. And selling the whole for half does not entail the defect of partnership, so it does not involve contradiction, so it is valid and binding. Our response is that selling half for half entails the defect of partnership, but selling the whole for half does not. However, selling the whole for half causes greater loss to the principal, and bearing greater loss is permissible, so bearing lesser loss (selling half for half) is a fortiori permissible. Note that selling the whole for half is only valid according to Imam Abu Hanifa; that is why it is said 'it is valid according to him'; otherwise according to the two companions (Sahibayn) it is invalid because it involves gross deception (ghabn fahish), and selling with gross deception is invalid according to them, as previously mentioned. The proof of the two companions is that the principal's appointment of the agent to sell the slave is absolute, just as in Imam's proof. An absolute word is interpreted according to what is customary (mutāraf). Customarily, selling half is not customary. Therefore the agency does not include selling half. And when it does not include it, the agent's selling half is a contradiction of the principal's command, which is not permissible, so it is not valid. The second proof is that selling half creates partnership, which causes harm to the principal, and the agent is not authorized to cause harm. So since this transaction causes harm, the agent cannot do it.
Ashraf al-Hidayah Volume 10, page 257. Chapter of Agency. He appointed him as agent to sell his slave without restricting to whole or half. What is the ruling if the agent sells half? He said: And when he appointed him to sell his slave and he sold half of it, it is valid according to Abu Hanifa because the wording is absolute, not restricted to separation or combination. Do you not see that if he sold the whole for half the price, it is valid according to him? So if he sold half for half, it is a fortiori valid. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is not valid because it is not customary and because of the harm of partnership. Except that he sells the other half before they dispute, because selling half may occur as a means to compliance, such as when he cannot find a buyer for the whole and needs to split. So if he sells the remaining half before the first sale is rescinded, it becomes clear that the first sale was a means. If he does not sell, it becomes clear that it was not a means, so it is not valid. And this is istihsan according to them. Translation: And when he appointed him as agent to sell his slave. Then the agent sold half. According to Imam Abu Hanifa it is valid, because the wording is absolute, unrestricted to whole or half. Do you not see that if he sold the whole for half the price, it is valid according to Imam Abu Hanifa? So when he sold half for half, it is a fortiori valid. The two companions said it is not valid because it is not customary and because of the harm of partnership. But if he sells the other half before the agent and principal dispute. Because selling half sometimes becomes a means to fulfill the command, e.g., the agent finds a buyer who will only buy the whole, so he needs to sell in parts. So when he sells the remaining half before the first sale is broken, it becomes clear that the first sale was a means of compliance. And when he does not sell the remaining half, it becomes clear that it was not a means. So it is not valid, and this is istihsan according to them. Explanation: The case is that a person appointed another as agent to sell his slave, without restricting to whole or half. Then the agent sold half. According to Imam Abu Hanifa this sale is valid and binding on the principal. The two companions said this sale is not valid, i.e., it does not bind the principal. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that the principal's speech (command to sell the slave) is absolute; it is not restricted to the whole nor to half, and according to the principle 'the absolute runs on its absoluteness', the agent is authorized to sell the whole and also to sell half. And since he is authorized to sell half, his selling half is valid and binding. To clarify this proof further, the author of al-Hidayah said: If the mentioned agent sold the whole slave for half the price, e.g., a slave worth one thousand rupees for five hundred rupees, it is valid according to Imam Abu Hanifa. So when according to Imam selling the whole for half the price is valid, then selling half for half is a fortiori valid.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the scope of an agent's authority when appointed absolutely to sell a commodity (here a slave). The core issue: if the principal says 'sell my slave' without specifying whole or half, can the agent sell just half of the slave? The passage provides the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani), along with their proofs and a response to an objection. The passage begins by stating Imam Abu Hanifa's view that selling half is valid, using an a fortiori argument (qiyas awlawi): if selling the whole for half the price is valid (according to Imam Abu Hanifa, even though it involves loss), then selling half for half is even more beneficial to the principal because he retains half the slave. The objection that half-sale creates a partnership (shirkah) defect is rebutted by noting that the loss from selling the whole for half is greater, so what is less harmful is a fortiori permissible. The passage then notes that selling the whole for half is only valid according to Imam Abu Hanifa; the two companions consider it invalid due to gross deception (ghabn fahish). The two companions' proofs are then given: (1) the absolute word in agency is understood according to custom (mutāraf), and selling half is not customary; therefore the agency does not cover selling half, so the agent's act contradicts the principal's command. (2) Selling half creates a harmful partnership between principal and buyer, and the agent is not permitted to cause harm. An exception is provided based on istihsan: if the agent sells the other half before any dispute arises, it becomes clear that the first half-sale was a means (wasīlah) to ultimately fulfill the command to sell the whole slave, thus it becomes valid. The passage concludes by restating Imam Abu Hanifa's proof: an absolute authorization allows both selling the whole and selling half, and the a fortiori argument from selling the whole for half price. This passage is an expansion probe (sharh) on the matn of al-Hidayah, illustrating how different proofs (qiyas, custom, istihsan) lead to different rulings within the same school.

Key Terms
وكالة (wakālah): Agency; a contract whereby a person (principal) authorizes another (agent) to perform a legal act on his behalf.
وکیل (wakīl): The agent who is authorized to act on behalf of the principal.
موکل (muwakkil): The principal who appoints an agent.
مطلق (muṭlaq): Absolute, unrestricted. Here it refers to the wording of the agency without specifying whole or half.
متعارف (mutāraf): Customary, conventionally understood. The Sahibayn argue that the absolute word is interpreted according to custom, and selling half is not customary.
شرکت (shirkah): Partnership. Here it refers to the co-ownership of the slave between principal and buyer after selling half.
ضرر (ḍarar): Harm, detriment. The Sahibayn argue that selling half causes harm to the principal because partnership reduces his benefit.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning that departs from strict analogy (qiyas) in favor of a more appropriate ruling based on custom, necessity, or public interest.
غبن فاحش (ghabn fāḥish): Gross deception or excessive disparity in value. Used when a slave worth 1000 is sold for 500.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The agent must obtain the principal's specific permission to sell half.
B) The agent must also sell the other half before any dispute (mukhasama) arises.
C) The agent must sell both halves simultaneously.
D) The principal must ratify the sale after it occurs.

Key Takeaway
An absolute agency to sell generates an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa permits selling half based on a fortiori analogy, while the Sahibayn require the other half to be sold to avoid harm and uphold custom, using istihsan as the basis for the exception.

Selling Half a Slave by a Wakil: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Analyzes the validity of a wakil selling half a slave, with positions of Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on a wakil selling half a slave, and explain the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Absolute authority vs. harm prevention: the agent's half-sale is valid only if it completes the principal's command.

When a principal appoints an agent to sell a slave without specifying full or half, and the agent sells only half, a dispute arises between Abu Hanifa and his two leading disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. This lesson unpacks the proofs, the exception based on istihsan, and how the ruling affects the principal's recourse.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the disputed ruling
Identify the case: a wakil is appointed to sell a slave (no specification of full or half). The wakil sells half the slave. Determine the ruling according to Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.
The passage starts with 'If he appoints him to sell his slave and he sold half of it...'
2
Present Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa holds the sale valid because the command is absolute (mutlaq). He uses a fortiori analogy: if selling the whole for half the price is valid, selling half for half is even more valid.
Analogy: whole-for-half-price sale is valid → half-for-half-price a fortiori.
3
Present the Sahibayn's objection
The Sahibayn argue it is not valid because it is not customary (ghayr muta'arif) and because it creates harm of co-ownership (darar al-shirkah).
They emphasize the principal's likely intent to avoid shared ownership.
4
Explain the Sahibayn's exception
The Sahibayn make an exception: if the agent sells the other half before any dispute (khusumah) arises, then the original half sale is validated as a means (wasila) to fulfill the command. This is istihsan.
The half sale becomes a necessary step when no buyer for the whole is found.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Hanifa, the half sale is immediately binding on the principal. Under the Sahibayn, the principal can reject it unless the other half is sold before dispute.
Practical difference: principal's right to object vs. obligation to accept.

He said: And if he appoints him as an agent to sell his slave, and he sold half of it, it is valid according to Abu Hanifa because the wording is absolute, not tied to the condition of parting or joining. Do you not see that if he sold the whole for half the price, it is valid according to him; so if he sold half for half the price, it is even more valid. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is not valid because it is not customary, and because of the harm of partnership, unless he sells the other half before they dispute, because selling half may occur as a means to compliance when one cannot find a buyer for the whole, so he needs to divide it. So if he sells the remainder before the first sale is rescinded, it becomes clear that it occurred as a means; and if he does not sell, it becomes clear that it did not occur as a means, so it is not valid. And this istihsan according to them. [Urdu commentary follows with explanation of the case and arguments]
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) concerning whether a wakil (agent) who is appointed to sell a slave without specifying full or half may validly sell only half of the slave. The matn from al-Hidayah presents the positions: Abu Hanifa holds it valid (jayiz) because the command is absolute (mutlaq), and by analogy, selling the whole for half the price is valid, so selling half for half is a fortiori valid. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) disagree, stating it is not valid due to lack of custom (ghayr muta'arif) and the harm of co-ownership (darar al-shirkah) that results from partial sale. However, they make an exception: if the agent sells the remaining half before any dispute arises between agent and principal, the original half sale is validated retroactively. This exception is based on istihsan (juristic preference), as the half sale may have been a means (wasila) to fulfill the principal's command when no buyer for the whole was available. The commentary explains that Abu Hanifa's proof is the principle 'al-mutlaq yajri 'ala itlaqihi' (the absolute operates according to its absoluteness), so the agent has authority to sell the whole or any part. The Sahibayn restrict it because partial sale frustrates the principal's likely intent and creates co-ownership harm. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is not explicitly stated here, but later Hanafi practice often follows the Sahibayn's view with the exception. The author of al-Hidayah notes that the Sahibayn's ruling is istihsan; otherwise the qiyas (analogy) would always invalidate half sales.

Key Terms
مطلق (mutlaq): Unrestricted wording in the principal's authorization; no condition specifying full or half sale.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference: the Sahibayn's ruling that the half sale becomes valid if the other half is sold before dispute, based on practical need.
وسيلة (wasila): Means or intermediate step that leads to fulfillment of the principal's command (e.g., selling half as a step towards selling the whole).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), when does a wakil's sale of half a slave become valid?
A) It is always valid if the wakil acts in good faith.
B) It is valid only if the other half is sold before the principal and wakil dispute.
C) It is valid if the slave is old or disabled.
D) It is never valid regardless of circumstances.

Key Takeaway
An agent's half-sale is valid only if it ultimately leads to selling the whole, according to the Sahibayn; Abu Hanifa sees it as immediately valid.

Buying Half a Slave by a Wakil: Suspended Validity
Rules on a wakil buying half a slave, with suspended validity and condition for binding.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on a wakil purchasing half of a slave, identifying the condition for the purchase to become binding and the rationale based on necessity (wasila).

Core Idea
A wakil's purchase of half a slave is suspended; it becomes binding only if the other half is bought before the principal revokes.

Imagine you appoint an agent (wakil) to buy a slave. He only buys half of that slave. What happens? The Hanafi school holds that the purchase is valid but suspended (mawquf). It does not immediately transfer ownership. However, if the wakil later buys the remaining half before you revoke the first transaction, the entire purchase becomes binding on you. This lesson unpacks this ruling, its condition, and the underlying reasoning of the Hanafi imams, including a subtle distinction made by Abu Hanifa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and initial ruling
Consider the case: a principal appoints a wakil to buy a slave. The wakil buys only half of that slave. The text states that the purchase is 'mawquf' (suspended). What does this mean?
Mawquf indicates that the contract is valid in itself but its legal effect is contingent on a future event.
2
Understand the condition for binding effect
The text says if the wakil subsequently buys the rest of the slave (the other half), the purchase becomes binding (lazim) on the principal. Identify the condition: the remaining half must be purchased before the principal rejects the first sale.
If the principal revokes before completion, the first purchase becomes void.
3
Analyze the rationale: wasila
Why is the half purchase treated as suspended rather than void? The text explains that buying part may be a means (wasila) to fulfill the command, for example, when the slave is inherited among multiple owners and must be bought piece by piece. This is an istihsan based on necessity.
The concept of wasila allows partial transactions to be valid if they are a step toward complete compliance.
4
Note the agreement and distinction by Abu Hanifa
The ruling is unanimous (bil-ittifaq) among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. However, Abu Hanifa made a distinction: in buying, the 'means' (wasila) is realized differently than in selling. This implies that a similar suspension might not apply to a partial sale.
The distinction shows that purchase and sale are treated asymmetrically in Hanafi law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان و كل بشراء عبد فاشترى نصفه فالشراء موقوف فان اشترى باقيه لزم المؤكل لان شراء البعض قد يقع وسيلة الى الامتثال بان كان موروثا بين جماعة فيحتاج الى شرائه شقصا شقصا فاذا اشترى الباقى قبل رد الأمر البيع تبين انه وقع وسيلة فينفذ على الأمر وهذا بالاتفاق والفرق لابي حنيفة ان في الشرى يتحقق
And if he appoints him as an agent to buy a slave, and he buys half of it, then the purchase is suspended. If he buys the rest of it, it becomes binding on the principal because buying part may occur as a means to compliance, such as when the slave is inherited among a group, so he needs to buy it piece by piece. So if he buys the remainder before rejecting the first sale, it becomes clear that it occurred as a means, so it is executed in favor of the principal. This is by agreement. And the distinction for Abu Hanifa is that in buying, it is realized.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage addresses the case where a wakil is appointed to purchase a slave but only buys half. According to the text, the purchase (al-shira') is suspended (mawquf) — meaning it does not immediately take effect but is held in abeyance. If the wakil later buys the remaining half before the principal revokes the first transaction, the entire purchase becomes binding (lazim) on the principal. The rationale is that buying a part may be a means (wasila) to fulfill the purchase command, for example, when the slave is inherited by multiple owners and must be bought in shares. This ruling is agreed upon by the entire Hanafi school (bil-ittifaq), meaning Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani are in consensus. However, the passage ends by noting a distinction (al-farq) made by Abu Hanifa: in the context of buying, the concept of 'means becoming realized' (tahaqquq al-wasila) applies differently than in selling. This implies that Abu Hanifa's reasoning in the buying case aligns with the istihsan exception he accepted in the selling case, but here the agreement of the Sahibayn is present. The commentary from Ashraf al-Hidayah likely elaborated further, but the OCR only captured the Arabic matn. The key point is that partial purchase is treated more leniently than partial sale because in purchase, the principal is acquiring property, and piecemeal buying is often necessary by custom (as in inherited shares).

Key Terms
موقوف (mawquf): Suspended: the purchase of half the slave does not take immediate effect; it remains pending until the wakil buys the other half or the principal revokes.
بالاتفاق (bil-ittifaq): By agreement of the three main Hanafi imams: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens when a wakil appointed to buy a slave purchases only half of him?
A) The purchase is void because it does not fulfill the principal's command.
B) The purchase is suspended; if the wakil later buys the other half, it becomes binding on the principal.
C) The purchase is immediately binding on the principal, who must accept half ownership.
D) The wakil must return the half and cannot complete the purchase.

Key Takeaway
A wakil's purchase of half a slave is suspended and becomes binding only if the rest is bought before revocation; this ruling is based on the concept of wasila (means) and is agreed upon in the Hanafi school.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
6 min
Agent Selling or Buying Half a Slave: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sale and purchase of half a slave in wakalah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the validity of an agent selling half a slave, and explain the distinction between sale and purchase regarding suspension and suspicion.

Core Idea
Selling half a slave is impermissible unless it serves as means to the principal's end; buying half a slave is always suspended pending full purchase.

In agency law, the agent must act within the principal's command. What happens when the agent sells or buys only half of a slave? The Hanafi school has an internal dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost disciples (the Sahibayn). This passage from the Hidayah commentary unpacks the reasoning behind each view, particularly the role of istihsan and the distinction between sale and purchase based on ownership and suspicion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage covers two distinct cases: (1) agent appointed to sell a slave sells only half; (2) agent appointed to buy a slave buys only half. Note the different rulings.
2
State the intra-Hanafi positions on sale
Imam Abu Hanifa holds the sale of half a slave is valid outright. The Sahibayn hold it is invalid unless the agent later sells the other half before the first sale is rescinded. Identify which position is based on istihsan.
Sahibayn's view is istihsan; qiyas would invalidate both.
3
Analyse the ruling on purchase
All three imams agree that buying half a slave is suspended (mawquf) until the remaining half is purchased. If the agent then buys the other half, it becomes binding. Understand the rationale of suspicion (tuhmah).
Suspicion: agent may buy for himself then pass loss to principal.
4
Examine the distinction between sale and purchase
Imam Abu Hanifa provides two reasons for the difference: (1) in sale, the agent sells the principal's property (ownership encountered), reducing suspicion; in purchase, the agent buys from others, raising suspicion. (2) The command to sell is absolute because the agent has ownership; the command to purchase encounters another's ownership, so restrictions apply.
This distinction is based on the nature of the command and ownership.
5
Determine the operative ruling (mufta bihi)
The text favours the Sahibayn's view for sale (istihsan) and the consensus for purchase. Thus, for fatwa, an agent selling half a slave alone is impermissible; for purchase, the transaction is suspended until full purchase.
The relied-upon position follows the later Hanafi masters who adopt Sahibayn's view.

صاحب ہدایہ نے اس کے جواب میں دو وجہیں فرق ذکر کی ہیں۔ پہلی وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ مسئلہ شراء میں وکیل کے حق میں تہمت متحقق ہے۔ اس طور پر کہ وکیل نے نصف غلام اپنے واسطے خریدا ہو۔ مگر جب اس میں خسارہ محسوس ہوا ہو تو اس خریداری کو موکل کے ذمہ ڈالدیا ہو پس اس تہمت کی وجہ سے نصف غلام کی خریداری کو موقوف رکھا گیا اور کہا گیا کہ اگر وکیل نے باقی غلام کو بھی خرید لیا تو یہ خریداری موکل پر نافذ ہو جائے گی اور اگر نہ خریدا تو نافذ نہ ہوگی۔ لیکن مسئلہ بیع
He (the sale) will not be valid. But despite that, if the agent sells half a slave, then this sale is not permissible. Because there is harm of partnership. The second proof is when 'lima fihi' is read with waw, and without waw if 'lima fihi' is read as in some copies of Bidayah, then this phrase would not be a second proof from the Sahibayn for the original issue. Rather, in this case, the phrase is proof that the remaining half of the slave is unconventional, and it will be said that the sale of half a slave is unconventional because of the harm of partnership. And Allah knows best. In any case, the sale of half a slave is not permissible according to the Sahibayn. Yes, if the agent sells the other half before the dispute between principal and agent, then selling half a slave is permissible according to the Sahibayn as well, because selling half a slave sometimes becomes a means of complying with the principal's command. In such a way that the agent does not find a person who will buy the whole slave at once, so he needs to sell it half by half. So when before the first half sale is rescinded, the agent sells the remaining half, it becomes apparent that the first half sale was a means of complying with the principal's command. And when the first half sale was a means of complying with the principal's command, then it is permissible for the agent to sell the first half. And when the agent did not sell the remaining half, it becomes apparent that the first half sale was not a means of complying with the principal's command. So in that case, it is not permissible for the agent to sell the first half. The summary is that the principal's main objective is to sell the whole slave, and compliance with this command can happen in two ways: one is that he sells the whole slave at once; second is that he sells it half by half. So if he sells both halves, whether at once or one after the other, the principal's objective is achieved. And if he sells half a slave, then the sale is rescinded, and then he sells the remaining half, it is not permissible, or if the agent sells half a slave and cannot sell the other half, this is also not permissible because the principal's objective is not achieved. The author of Hidayah says that according to the Sahibayn, this ruling is based on istihsan. Otherwise, the requirement of qiyas is that the sale of half a slave is not permissible, whether he sells the other half or not. If he appoints him as agent to buy a slave, and he buys half a slave, then the purchase is suspended. If he buys the rest of the slave, the purchase becomes binding on the principal. Because buying a part may sometimes be a means of compliance, such as when the slave is inherited among a group, so he needs to buy it share by share. So when he buys the rest before the principal revokes the transaction, it becomes apparent that it occurred as a means, so it takes effect on the command. This is by agreement. The difference according to Abu Hanifa is that in purchase, suspicion is established, as passed. And another difference is that the command to sell encounters his (the agent's) ownership, so it is valid, so its absolute nature is considered. The command to purchase encounters the ownership of another, so it is not valid, so restricted and absolute are not considered. Translation: And if he appoints him as agent to buy a slave, and the agent buys half a slave, then this purchase remains suspended. Then if the agent buys the remaining slave, this purchase becomes binding on the principal. Because buying a part of the slave sometimes becomes a means of complying with the principal's command, such as when the slave is inherited among a group, then the agent will need to buy it share by share. So when the agent buys the remaining slave before the principal revokes the transaction, it becomes apparent that buying half a slave occurred as a means. Therefore, it will be effective on the principal, and this ruling is by consensus. And based on the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa, the difference is that in purchase, suspicion is established, as passed. And the second difference is that the command to sell encounters the principal's ownership, so it is valid, so its absolute nature is considered. The command to purchase encounters the ownership of another, so it is not valid, so restriction and absoluteness are not considered. Explanation of the issue: A person appoints someone as agent to buy a slave. The agent buys half a slave. This purchase will be suspended by consensus. That is, if the agent buys the remaining part of the slave, this purchase becomes binding and effective on the principal. If he does not buy the remaining part of the slave, this purchase is not binding on the principal. The proof is that buying a part of the slave sometimes becomes a means of complying with the principal's command. For example, a slave is inherited by several people, so those people are owners of that slave. Now if the agent wants to buy this slave, he will have to buy it share by share from all the owners. In any case, when the agent buys the remaining part of the slave before the principal revokes the transaction of the first half, it becomes apparent that buying the first half was a means of complying with the principal's command. And it has passed earlier that in the case where selling half a slave becomes a means of complying with the principal's command, the sale is effective on the principal. Therefore, in the case of purchase as well, when buying the first half becomes a means of complying with the principal's command, this purchase will be effective on the principal, because it is as if the agent bought the whole slave. The author of Hidayah said that on this point that the purchase of the first half is suspended, Imam and the Sahibayn all agree. But there is an objection on Imam's statement: Imam declared the sale of half a slave in the previous sale issue as permissible without suspension, and here in the purchase issue, he considers the purchase of half a slave as suspended. So what is the reason for the difference? The author of Hidayah mentioned two reasons for the difference. The first reason is that in purchase, suspicion is established against the agent, in that the agent might have bought half a slave for himself, but when he feels loss, he throws it onto the principal. So due to this suspicion, the purchase of half a slave is suspended, and it is said that if the agent buys the remaining slave, this purchase becomes effective on the principal, and if he does not buy, it is not effective. But in the sale issue...
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf Ul Hadaya is an expansion on the rules of agency (wakalah) concerning the sale or purchase of half a slave. The text contains an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad). For the sale case, the Sahibayn hold that selling half a slave is impermissible unless the agent subsequently sells the other half before the first sale is rescinded, thereby completing the principal's objective. They base this on istihsan (juristic preference) because qiyas would render the sale invalid in all cases. Imam Abu Hanifa, however, holds it permissible outright, considering that the agent is selling his own property (since the principal's ownership is transferred to the agent upon agency for sale). For the purchase case, all three imams agree that buying half a slave is suspended (mawquf) until the agent buys the remaining half; if he does, the purchase becomes binding on the principal. Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes between sale and purchase on two grounds: (1) in purchase, there is suspicion (tuhmah) that the agent may be acting for himself, and (2) the command to sell encounters the agent's ownership (so absoluteness is considered), whereas the command to purchase encounters another's ownership (so restriction applies). The commentary explains these distinctions in detail, emphasizing that the principal's objective—acquiring or selling the whole slave—is the key criterion for validity.

Key Terms
وکالت (wakalah): Agency; one person authorizing another to perform a legal act on his behalf.
وکیل (wakeel): The agent; the person authorized by the principal to act on his behalf.
موکل (muwakkil): The principal; the person who authorizes the agent.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; departing from qiyas due to a stronger evidence or need.
تہمت (tuhmah): Suspicion; in this context, suspicion that the agent is acting for his own benefit rather than the principal's.
موقوف (mawquf): Suspended; a transaction that is not immediately effective but becomes effective upon occurrence of a condition (e.g., buying the rest of the slave).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does Imam Abu Hanifa distinguish between selling half a slave and buying half a slave?
A) Because in sale the agent owns the item, reducing suspicion; in purchase he buys from others, raising suspicion.
B) Because the Sahibayn disagreed on purchase but not on sale.
C) Because the principal's command for sale is absolute, while for purchase it is restricted.
D) Because selling half a slave is invalid in all cases.

Key Takeaway
For selling half a slave, the relied-upon Hanafi position is that it is impermissible unless it serves as a means to complete the principal's objective; for buying half a slave, all imams agree it is suspended until the other half is purchased.

Ruling on Agent Returning Defective Slave to Principal
States the ruling on an agent selling a slave and the buyer returning it due to a non-emerging defect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a buyer returns a defective slave to an agent, and explain the role of judicial proof in validating the return to the principal.

Core Idea
A defect proven to have existed in the principal's possession permits the agent to return the slave to the principal without personal liability.

In this passage, Al-Hidayah discusses the scenario where an agent sells a slave, and the buyer later discovers a defect that must have existed before the sale. The ruling explains how the agent can return the slave to the principal through a judge's determination, and what evidence is required. Understanding this clarifies the limits of an agent's responsibility and the principal's ultimate liability for pre-existing defects.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the legal problem
Determine who is the principal (the one who ordered the sale), the agent (the seller), and the buyer. The buyer returns the slave to the agent due to a defect. The agent now needs to know whether he can pass this return to the principal.
2
Understand the type of defect
The defect is 'a defect whose like does not emerge' – meaning it could not have appeared after the sale. Therefore, it must have existed while the slave was with the principal (the original owner).
Hanafi jurisprudence distinguishes between defects that could arise after sale and those that could not; the latter are presumed pre-existing.
3
Analyze the judicial determination
The judge's ruling that the defect existed in the principal's possession is based on one of three proofs: clear evidence (bayyinah), refusal of the agent to take an oath, or the agent's confession. These are needed only when the date of sale or the nature of the defect is unclear. If the judge witnessed the sale and the defect is apparent, no proof is required.
4
Apply the ruling
Once the judge's ruling establishes the defect, the agent returns the slave to the principal. The agent does not need to file a separate lawsuit; the return is directly against the principal.
This protects the agent from bearing the loss of a defect that originated with the principal.

He said: And whoever commands a man to sell his slave, and he sells him, and takes the price or does not take it, then the buyer returns him to him (the agent) due to a defect whose like does not emerge, by the judgment of the judge through evidence (bayyinah), or by refusal of oath, or by his (the agent's) confession, then he (the agent) returns him to the one who commanded (the principal), because the judge is certain that the defect occurred in the hand of the seller. So his judgment is not based on these proofs. And the interpretation of stipulating them in the book is that the judge knows that its like does not emerge in the period of a month, for example, but the date of sale is unclear to him, so he needs these proofs to clarify the date. Or it is a defect that only women or doctors know, and their statement is a proof in directing the lawsuit, not in the return, so it is needed for the return. Even if the judge witnessed the sale and the defect is apparent, he does not need any of these. And it (the return) is upon the principal, so the agent does not need to return and litigate. Translation: And if a person commanded a man to sell his slave, and the agent sold him, and took possession of the price or did not take possession, then the buyer returned this slave to the agent due to a defect whose like cannot emerge, by the judgment of the judge through evidence, or by refusal of oath, or by the agent's confession, then the agent can return the slave to the principal, because the judge is certain that the defect occurred in the possession of the seller. Therefore, the judge's ruling is not based on these proofs. The interpretation of stipulating these proofs in the book is that the judge knows that the like of this defect cannot emerge in, for example, a month, but the judge is uncertain about the date of sale, so he needs these proofs to clarify the date. Or the defect is one that only women or doctors know, and their statement is evidence in proving the claim, not in the return, so their testimony is needed for the return. Up to the point that if the judge witnessed the sale and the defect is apparent, then there is no need for any of these. And this return is upon the principal, so the agent does not need to return and litigate.

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling when an agent sells a slave and the buyer returns it due to a defect that could not have arisen after the sale (a pre-existing defect). The key point: The agent can return the defective slave to the principal because the judge's ruling confirming the defect is based on the certainty that the defect existed in the principal's possession. The judge may require evidence (bayyinah), refusal of oath, or confession by the agent to establish the date or nature of the defect, but these are only needed when the defect is not obvious or the date is unclear. If the judge personally witnessed the sale and the defect is apparent, no proof is needed. The return is ultimately against the principal, so the agent does not need to initiate a separate lawsuit or return process; the agent simply returns the slave to the principal.

Key Terms
بقضاء القاضي (bi-qada al-qadi): By the judgment of the judge; the return of the slave is validated by a judicial ruling based on evidence.
بينة (bayyinah): Clear evidence, usually two witnesses; used here to prove the date or nature of the defect.
عيب لا يحدث مثله (ayb la yahduth mithluh): A defect whose like does not emerge (after sale); indicates a pre-existing defect for which the buyer can return the item.

Distinction Between Agency for Sale and Purchase of Half a Slave
Analyzing the legal difference between sale and purchase in agency concerning half a slave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi distinction between agency for sale and purchase regarding half a slave and apply the role of custom in limiting the agent's authority.

Core Idea
In agency for sale, the agent can bind the principal by selling half; in agency for purchase, custom restricts the agent to buying the whole slave.

This passage from Al-Hidayah examines a seemingly inconsistent ruling: an agent authorized to sell a slave may sell half and bind the principal, but an agent authorized to buy a slave cannot buy half without binding himself. The reasoning hinges on the nature of the principal's command and the role of custom. Understanding this distinction is key to grasping how Hanafi fiqh balances textual commands with practical custom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Note that the passage presents two cases: agency for sale and agency for purchase. In each, the agent acts regarding half a slave. The rulings differ.
This is the starting point of the analysis.
2
Trace the first reasoning: connection to ownership
In sale, the principal's command is to sell his own property. Since he has authority over it, his command is valid and absolute. Therefore, the agent may sell any portion.
This is a rational argument based on legal capacity.
3
Examine the second reasoning: command to purchase another's property
In purchase, the principal commands the agent to buy something not yet owned by him. Commanding to buy another's property is not inherently valid; it is permitted only out of necessity. Thus, the command is not absolute; it is interpreted according to custom.
Custom (urf) becomes the decisive factor.
4
Determine what custom dictates
Custom (urf) is that when someone says 'buy this slave,' it means the whole slave. Therefore, buying half is against custom and not binding on the principal.
Custom limits the scope of the agent's authority.
5
Derive the ruling and contrast
Thus, in sale, half-sale is valid and binding; in purchase, half-purchase is not binding on the principal but on the agent. This distinction is consistent with the principles of authority and custom.
The outcome is mufta bihi: sale binds principal, purchase binds agent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوكالة
اشرف الہدایہ جلد - دہم میں یہ تہمت متحقق نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے نصف غلام کی بیع موکل ہی کیلئے ہو سکتی ہے وکیل کیلئے نہیں ۔ پس اس فرق کی وجہ سے مسئلہ بیچ میں نصف غلام کی بیع کو بغیر توقف کے جائز قرار دیا گیا ہے۔ اور مسئلہ شراء میں نصف غلام کی شراء کو موقوف رکھا گیا ہے۔ دوسری وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ وکیل بالبیع کی صورت میں موکل کا امر بالمیچ مؤکل کی ملک سے ملاتی ہوا ہے۔ یعنی مؤکل نے اپنی مملوکہ چیز فروخت کرنے کا حکم دیا ہے۔ اور موکل کو چونکہ اپنی ملک پر ولایت حاصل ہے۔ اسلئے اس کا امر بالبیچ درست ہو گا اور جب مؤکل کا امر بالبیچ درست ہے تو اس میں اطلاق امر معتبر ہو گا۔ اور جب مؤکل کے امر بالبیع میں اطلاق معتبر ہے تو وکیل پورے غلام کو فروخت کرنے کا بھی مجاز ہو گا۔ اور آدھے غلام کو فروخت کرنے کا بھی مجاز ہوگا اور جب وکیل آدھے غلام کو فر وخت کرنے کا مجاز ہے تو اس کا آدھا غلام فروخت کرنا بھی جائز ہوگا۔ اور توکیل بالشراء کی صورت میں موکل کا امر غیر کی ملک کے ساتھ ملاقی ہوا ہے یعنی مؤکل نے جس چیز کے خریدنے کا حکم کیا ہے، وہ چیز متوکل کی ملک نہیں ہے بلکہ بائع کی ملک ہے اور غیر کی ملک خریدنے کا حکم کرنا میچ نہیں ہے محض ضرورت کے پیش نظر جائز قرار دیا ہے۔ پس جب امر بالشراء صحیح نہیں ہے تو اس میں اطلاق یا تقید معتبر نہ ہوگی یہ بلکہ عرف معتبر ہوگا۔ اور عرف یہ ہے کہ پورا غلام خریدا جائے ۔ لہذا غلام خریدنے کا حکم کرنا عرف کے پیش نظر پورا غلام خریدنے کا امر کرنا ہو گا اور جب ایسا ہے تو وکیل جس صورت میں پورا غلام خریدے گا ( خواہ ایک بارگی خواہ متفرق کر کے ) اس صورت میں یہ خریداری چونکہ موکل کے حکم کے مطابق ہے۔ اسلئے مؤکل پر لازم ہوگی اور جس صورت میں آدھا غلام خریدے گا اس صورت میں موکل کے حکم کی موافقت ن ہونے کی وجہ سے مؤکل پر لازم نہ ہوگی ۔ بلکہ وکیل پر لازم ہوگی۔
Book of Agency. In Ashraf al-Hidayah Volume 10, this accusation is not confirmed. Therefore, the sale of half a slave can be for the principal, not for the agent. For this reason, in the case of sale, the sale of half a slave is permitted without suspension, and in the case of purchase, the purchase of half a slave is suspended. The second reason for the difference is that in the case of agency for sale, the principal's command to sell is connected to the principal's ownership; that is, the principal has commanded to sell his owned property. And since the principal has authority over his own property, his command to sell is valid. When the principal's command to sell is valid, then the absolute nature of the command is considered. When the absolute nature of the principal's command to sell is considered, then the agent is authorized to sell the whole slave and also to sell half the slave. When the agent is authorized to sell half the slave, then his selling half the slave is permissible. In the case of agency for purchase, the principal's command is connected to someone else's property; that is, the thing the principal commanded to purchase is not the principal's property but the seller's property. Commanding to purchase someone else's property is not valid; it is only permitted due to necessity. Therefore, when the command to purchase is not valid, absolute or restricted interpretation is not considered; rather, custom is considered. And custom is that a whole slave is purchased. Hence, commanding to purchase a slave, according to custom, is a command to purchase the whole slave. Therefore, whenever the agent purchases the whole slave (whether at once or in parts), this purchase corresponds to the principal's command, so it is binding on the principal. When he purchases half the slave, it does not correspond to the principal's command, so it is not binding on the principal, but rather binding on the agent.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof that explains the Hanafi distinction between agency for sale and agency for purchase regarding half a slave. The author first states that in agency for sale, the agent's sale of half a slave is valid and effective for the principal immediately, but in agency for purchase, the agent's purchase of half a slave is suspended (does not bind the principal) because the agent would be binding himself. The reasoning (فرق) is twofold: First, in sale, the agent's action is linked to the principal's ownership, and the principal has full authority over his property, so his command is valid and absolute; the agent can sell all or part. Second, in purchase, the command is directed at another's property, which is not inherently valid but permitted by necessity. Therefore, the command is not absolute; custom (عرف) determines that the agent should buy the whole slave. Thus, buying half is against custom and not binding on the principal. This is a purely rational (dalil 'aqli) argument based on the nature of ownership and customary practice.

Key Terms
وکیل (wakīl): Agent appointed by the principal to perform a legal act (sale/purchase).
موکل (muwakkil): Principal who appoints the agent.
عرف (ʿurf): Customary practice; in this context, the custom that a command to buy a slave implies buying the whole slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) No, because the agent can only do what is customary.
C) Yes, but only if the principal explicitly permits selling half.
D) No, because splitting the sale is not valid.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between sale and purchase in agency based on the principal's authority over his own property and the role of custom in interpreting commands to acquire another's property.

Returning a Defective Slave to the Principal Without Litigation
Ruling on agent returning a returned defective slave to principal after judicial decision.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an agent's return of a defective slave to the principal after a judicial order and explain why no separate litigation is required.

Core Idea
A judge's order returning a defective slave to the agent suffices as return to the principal; no second lawsuit needed.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in Hanafi sales law where an agent sells a slave, and the buyer later returns it due to a pre-existing defect. The question is whether the agent must initiate a new court case to return the slave to the principal. The passage from Al-Hidayah explains that the judge's original order is sufficient, eliminating the need for additional litigation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and sequence of events
The principal hired an agent to sell a slave. The agent sold it. The buyer discovered a pre-existing defect and returned it to the agent by judicial order. Can the agent now return it to the principal?
The defect cannot arise during buyer's possession.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The agent may return the slave to the principal without a new lawsuit. The judge's order is effectively a return to the principal.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
Identify the proof (dalil)
The proof is qiyas: because the judge is certain the defect existed with the seller, the return to the agent is legally equivalent to return to the principal.
The Arabic phrase: 'لان القاضى تيقن بحدوث العيب في يد البائع'.
4
Analyze the objection and response
Objection: Why does the text require evidence/oath if the judge is certain? Answer: The judge's certainty is the real basis; the proofs are needed when the date of sale is ambiguous or the defect is only known to experts.
This is an expansion probe resolving a potential misunderstanding.
5
Understand the practical implication
The agent is saved from a second litigation. The principal bears the loss because the defect was present during his ownership.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.

Source Text

ایک شخص نے کسی کو اپنا غلام فروخت کرنے کا حکم دیا وکیل نے اسکو بیچ دیا شمن پر قبضہ کیا یا نہیں کیا پھر غلام کو ایسے عیب کی وجہ جس کے مثل پیدا نہیں ہو سکتا مشتری نے قضاء قاضی سے وکیل کی طرف واپس کیا تو وکیل مؤکل کو واپس کر سکتا ہے یا نہیں
قال ومن امر رجلا ببيع عبده قباعه و قبض الثمن اولم يقبض فرده المشترى عليه بعيب لا يحدث مثله بقضاء القاضي ببينة او باباء يمين او باقراره فانه يرده على الامر لان القاضى تيقن بحدوث العيب في يد البائع فلم يكن قضاؤه مستندا الى هذه الححج و تاويل اشتراطها فى الكتاب ان القاضى يعلم انه لا يحدث مثله في مدة شهر مثلاً لكنه اشتبه عليه تاريخ البيع فيحتاج الى هذه الحج لظهور التاريخ او كان عيباً لا يعرفه الا النساء او الاطباء وقولهن وقول الطبيب حجة فى توجه الخصومة لافي الرد فيفتقر اليها في الرد حتى لو كان القاضى عاين البيع والعيب ظاهر لا يحتاج الى شيء منها وهو رد على المؤكل فلا يحتاج الوكيل الى رد وخصومة
ترجمہ اور اگر ایک شخص نے کسی آدمی کو اپنا غلام فروخت کرنے کا حکم دیا۔ پس وکیل نے اس کو بیچ دیا اور من پر قبضہ کیا یا قبضہ نہیں کیا۔ پھر اس غلام کو ایسے عیب کی وجہ سے جس کے مثل پیدا نہیں ہو سکتا ہے۔ مشتری نے قضاء قاضی کے ساتھ وکیل کی طرف واپس کیا ( قاضی کا یہ فیصلہ ) بینہ کی وجہ سے ہو یا قسم کا انکار کرنے کی وجہ سے یا وکیل کے اقرار کی وجہ سے ہو تو وکیل اس غلام کو مؤکل کی طرف واپس کر سکتا

كتاب الوكالة
۲۶۲
اشرف الہدایہ جلد وہم
ہے۔ اسلئے کہ قاضی کو بائع کے قبضہ میں عیب پیدا ہونے کا یقین ہے۔ لہذا قاضی کا فیصلہ ان حجتوں کی طرف منسوب نہ ہوگا اور کتاب میں ان حجتوں کے شرط لگانے کی تاویل یہ ہے کہ قاضی کو علم ہے کہ اس طرح کا عیب مثلاً ایک ماہ کی مدت میں پیدا نہیں ہو سکتا ہے لیکن قاضی پر بیچ کی تاریخ مشتبہ ہو گئی تو وہ تاریخ ظاہر ہونے کے واسطے ان محبتوں کی طرف محتاج ہوگا۔ یا ایسا عیب تھا جس کو صرف عورتیں اور طبیب ہی پہنچانتے ہیں۔ اور عورتوں اور طبیب کا قول جھگڑا متوجہ ہونے میں حجت ہے اور بائع کی طرف واپس کرنے میں حجت نہیں ہے۔ حتی کہ اگر قاضی نے بیچ کا مشاہدہ کیا ہو اور عیب ظاہر ہو تو قاضی ان میں سے کسی حجت کا محتاج نہیں ہو گا ۔ اور یہی موکل پر واپسی ہے۔ پس وکیل واپس کرنے اور خصومت کرنے کا محتاج نہ ہوگا۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے دوسرے شخص کو اپنا غلام فروخت کرنے کا وکیل کیا پس وکیل نے اس غلام کو فروخت کر دیا اور مشتری کے حوالہ کر دیا، وکیل نے شمن کے قبضہ کیا ہو یا نہ کیا ہو دونوں صورتوں میں اگر مشتری نے اس غلام کو وکیل کی طرف ایسے عیب کی وجہ سے واپس کیا جس عیب کے مثل مشتری کی قبضہ میں پیدا نہیں ہو سکتا ہے۔ مثلاً غلام کے ہاتھ میں زائد انگلی کا ہونا، یا ایسے عیب کی وجہ سے واپس کیا جس کے مثل اس مدت میں پیدا نہیں ہو سکتا ہے جو مدت مشتری کے قبضہ کی ہے اور مشتری کا اس معیب غلام کو واپس کرنا قاضی کے حکم سے ہوا ہو اور قاضی کا یہ حکم مشتری کے پیش کردہ بینہ کی وجہ سے ہو یا بینہ پیش نہ کرنے کی صورت میں وکیل کے قسم کھانے سے انکار کی وجہ سے ہو۔ یا بدینہ پیش نہ کرنے کی صورت میں وکیل کے قسم کھانے سے انکار کی وجہ سے ہو یا وکیل کے عیب کا اقرار کرنے کی وجہ سے ہو تینوں صورتوں میں وکیل اس معیب غلام کو بغیر خصومت کے مؤکل کی طرف واپس کر سکتا ہے۔ یعنی وکیل اس معیب غلام کو مؤکل کی طرف واپس کرنے کیلئے خصومت اور قضائے قاضی کا محتاج نہ ہوگا کیونکہ قضائے قاضی کی وجہ سے مشتری کا غلام کو وکیل کی طرف واپس کرنا یہی مؤکل کی طرف واپس کرنا ہے ، مؤکل کی طرف واپس کرنے کیلئے علیحدہ خصومت اور جھگڑے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ دلیل ... اس کی یہ ہے کہ کلام چونکہ اس عیب کے بارے میں ہے جس کے مثل پیدا نہیں ہوسکتا ہے۔ اسلئے قاضی کو پورے طور پر یقین ہے کہ یہ عیب بائع کے قبضہ میں موجود تھا اور جب قاضی کو بائع کے قبضہ میں مذکورہ عیب کے ہونے کا یقین ہے تو قاضی اپنے علم و یقین کی روشنی میں اس معیب غلام کو بائع کی طرف واپس کرنے کا فیصلہ کر سکتا ہے اور اس فیصلہ کے تحت غلام کی واپسی جس طرح وکیل کی طرف ہو گی۔ اسی طرح مؤکل کی طرف بھی ہوگی۔
اعتراض لیکن اس پر یہ اعتراض ہو گا کہ جب عیب ایسا ہے جس کے مثل مشتری کے قبضہ میں پیدا نہیں ہوسکتا ہے تو پھر قاضی کے فیصلہ کو مذکورہ جنتوں یعنی بینہ وغیرہ پر کیوں موقوف رکھا گیا ہے۔ قاضی اپنے علم و یقین کی وجہ سے بغیر ان حجبتوں کے بھی فیصلہ صادر کر سکتا ہے۔ جواب صاحب ہدایہ نے اس کا جواب دیتے ہوئے فرمایا فلم يكن قضاؤه مستنداً الى هذه الحجج .... الخ یعنی قاضی کا معیب غلام کو واپس کرنے کا فیصلہ ان حجتوں پر موقوف نہیں ہے، یہاں عبارت میں اگر فلم یکن کی جگہ ولم یکن یعنی فار کی جگہ واو ہوتا تو عبارت زیادہ واضح ہو جاتی۔ سوال لیکن اب یہ سوال پیدا ہو گا کہ جب قاضی کو اس بات کا یقین ہے کہ یہ عیب بائع کے قبضہ میں تھا اور مشتری کے قبضہ میں آکر پیدا نہیں ہوا ہے اور قاضی کا فیصلہ مذکورہ محبتوں پر موقوف نہیں ہے تو متن (جامع صغیر میں ان حجتوں کو ذکر کرنے اور ان کی شرط لگانے سے کیا
فائدہ ہے۔
A person commanded someone to sell his slave, and the agent sold it, whether he took the price or not. Then the buyer returned the slave to the agent due to a defect that cannot arise later, by the judgment of a judge, based on evidence, or refusal to take an oath, or the agent's confession. Then he (the agent) returns it to the principal. Because the judge is certain that the defect occurred while in the possession of the seller. So his judgment is not based on these proofs. The interpretation of stipulating these in the book is that the judge knows that such a defect cannot arise in a month, for example, but the date of sale is ambiguous to him, so he needs these proofs to clarify the date. Or the defect is one that only women or doctors know, and their statements are proof for directing the litigation but not for the return. So he needs them for the return. Even if the judge witnessed the sale and the defect is apparent, he does not need any of these, and it is a return to the principal, so the agent does not need to return and litigate.
Translation: And if a person commanded someone to sell his slave, then the agent sold it and took the price or did not take it. Then this slave, due to a defect that cannot arise later, the buyer returned it to the agent by the judgment of a judge, either by evidence, or by refusing to take an oath, or by the agent's confession, then the agent can return it to the principal. Because the judge is certain that the defect occurred while in the possession of the seller. Therefore, the judge's judgment is not based on these proofs. And the interpretation of stipulating these in the book is that the judge knows that such a defect cannot arise in a period of one month, for example, but the date of sale was ambiguous to the judge, so he needs these proofs to clarify the date. Or it was a defect that only women or doctors recognize, and the statement of women and doctors is proof for directing litigation, not for the return. So he needs them for the return. Even if the judge witnessed the sale and the defect is apparent, he does not need any of these. And this is a return to the principal, so the agent does not need to return and litigate.
Explanation: The scenario is that a person appointed another as agent to sell his slave. The agent sold the slave and handed it over to the buyer, whether the agent took the price or not. In both cases, if the buyer returns the slave to the agent due to a defect that cannot arise during the buyer's possession, e.g., an extra finger on the hand, or a defect that cannot arise in the period that the buyer has possessed it, and the buyer's return is by the judge's order, and the judge's order is due to evidence presented by the buyer, or due to the agent's refusal to take an oath, or due to the agent's confession of the defect - in all three cases, the agent can return this defective slave to the principal without litigation. That is, the agent does not need litigation or a judge's order to return the defective slave to the principal, because the judge's order that the buyer return it to the agent is itself a return to the principal. There is no need for separate litigation. The reason is that since the speech is about a defect that cannot arise, the judge is fully certain that this defect existed in the seller's possession. When the judge is certain that the said defect existed in the seller's possession, then the judge, in the light of his knowledge and certainty, can decide to return the defective slave to the seller. Under this decision, the return of the slave to the agent is effectively a return to the principal. Objection: But an objection arises: when the defect is such that it cannot arise during the buyer's possession, then why is the judge's decision made dependent on the mentioned proofs like evidence etc.? The judge can give a decision based on his own knowledge and certainty without these proofs. Answer: The author of al-Hidayah replied: 'So his judgment is not based on these proofs.' meaning the judge's decision to return the defective slave is not dependent on these proofs. If in the phrase 'fa lam yakun' it were 'wa lam yakun' instead of 'fa', the phrase would be clearer. Question: But now another question arises: When the judge is certain that the defect existed in the seller's possession and did not arise after the buyer took possession, and the judge's decision is not dependent on the mentioned proofs, then what benefit is there in mentioning and stipulating these proofs in the text (al-Jami' al-Saghir)?
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from Al-Hidayah (the matn) and its commentary discussing a specific case in agency for sale. The scenario: a principal (موکل) appoints an agent (وکیل) to sell his slave. The agent sells the slave to a buyer. Later, the buyer discovers a defect that could not have arisen during his possession (e.g., a missing limb or an extra finger that existed before purchase). The buyer takes the case to a judge, who orders the agent to take back the slave. The judge's order may be based on: (1) evidence (بینہ) presented by the buyer, (2) the agent's refusal to take an oath (إباء یمین) when offered, or (3) the agent's own confession (اقرار) that the defect existed at the time of sale. In all these cases, the agent can return the defective slave directly to the principal without initiating a new lawsuit. The reason: the judge's ruling that the buyer can return the slave to the agent is effectively a ruling that the slave is returned to the seller (the principal), because the agent is merely an intermediary. The judge is certain that the defect existed with the seller because it cannot have arisen later. Therefore, no separate court case is needed between the agent and the principal. The commentary then addresses an objection: if the judge is certain based on the nature of the defect, why does the text mention needing evidence or oath? The answer (from Al-Hidayah) is that the judge's decision is ultimately based on his certainty, not on those proofs. The proofs are mentioned for cases where the judge needs to establish the date of sale or when the defect is only recognizable by experts (women, doctors). The judge may rely on his own knowledge if he witnessed the transaction. Thus, the agent's return to the principal is straightforward. This is a classic Hanafi position that simplifies the agent's role when the judge has already determined the liability of the seller.

Key Terms
عیب (ʿayb): Defect in the slave that existed before sale and cannot arise after the buyer's possession.
قضاء (qaḍāʾ): Judicial decision or judgment of a qadi.
رد (radd): Return of the defective slave to the seller (principal) by the agent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi view, if a judge orders the agent to take back a defective slave (with a defect that existed before sale), can the agent return it to the principal without a new lawsuit?
A) Yes, because the judge's order is effectively a return to the principal.
B) No, the agent must first sue the principal to prove the defect.
C) Yes, but only if the principal agrees.
D) No, the agent must get a separate judgment against the principal.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi sales law, an agent may return a defective slave to the principal directly after a judicial return order, without a new lawsuit, because the judge's certainty of the defect's pre-existence makes the return to the agent equivalent to return to the principal.
