كتاب الوكالة
واپسی فتح ہے۔ قاضی کی عموم ولایت کی وجہ سے مگر یہ کہ حجت قاصرہ یعنی اقرار پس فسخ ہونے کی وجہ سے وکیل کیلئے جائز ہے کہ وہ مؤکل سے مخاصمہ کرے اور حجت کے قاصر ہونے کی وجہ سے یہ واپسی مؤکل پر لازم نہ ہو گی مگر حجت سے اور اگر یہ عیب ایسا ہو جس کے مثل پیدا نہیں ہو سکتا ہے اور واپسی وکیل کے اقرار سے بغیر حکم قاضی کے ہو تو ایک روایت میں بغیر خصومت کے واپسی مؤکل پر لازم نہ ہو گی۔ اس لئے کہ واپسی متعین ہے۔ اور عام روایات میں ہے کہ وکیل کو موکل سے مخاصمہ کرنے کا حق نہیں ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے ذکر کی ہے اور حق تو وصف سلامت میں ہے پھر واپسی کی طرف منتقل ہوگا۔ پھر رجوع بالنقصان کی طرف منتقل ہو گا۔ پس وا پسی متعین نہیں ہوتی اور ہم نے کفایہ میں اس سے زیادہ تفصیل کے ساتھ ذکر کیا ہے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر وکیل نے غلام بیع کے عیب کا اقرار کر لیا اور اس اقرار کی وجہ سے قاضی کے فیصلہ سے مشتری نے معیب غلام ، وکیل کی طرف واپس کیا تو یہ غلام ، وکیل کے ذمہ لازم ہوگا یعنی غلام کی یہ واپسی وکیل پر شمار ہو گی موکل پر شمار نہ ہوگی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اقرار حجت قاصرہ ہے۔ لہذا اس کا اثر اقرار کرنے والے کے حق میں ظاہر ہوگا اور اس کے علاوہ کسی دوسرے کے حق میں ظاہر نہ ہوگا یعنی اقرار کرنے کی وجہ سے غلام کی واپسی مقر (وکیل) کی طرف ہوگی ۔ اور مؤکل کی طرف نہ ہوگی ۔ اور وکیل اقرار کرنے کے لئے مجبور بھی نہیں تھا۔ کیونکہ اس کے لئے خاموش رہنا بھی ممکن تھا اور یمین کا مطالبہ کرنے کی صورت میں یمین سے انکار کرنا بھی ممکن تھا پس اگر اقرار نہ کرتا بلکہ خاموش رہنا یا مطالبہ یمین کے وقت قسم کھانے سے انکار کر دیتا تو سکوت یا انکار عن الیمین کی وجہ سے فیصلہ کیا جاتا اور اقرار کی وجہ سے فیصلہ نہ کیا جاتا۔ بہر حال وکیل عیب کا اقرار کرنے میں مجبور نہیں تھا۔ بلکہ مختار تھا اور جب وکیل عیب کا اقرار کرنے میں مجبور نہیں تھا لیکن خود اسی کے حق میں اثر انداز ہو گا۔ یعنی معیب غلام کی واپسی اسی کی طرف ہوگی۔ اور اس کا اقرار مؤکل پر نہیں تھو پا جائے گا یعنی یہ واپسی موکل کے ذمہ لازم نہ ہوگی ۔ البتہ وکیل کو اپنے مؤکل کے ساتھ خصومت کرنے کا پورا پورا اختیار ہوگا ۔ یعنی وکیل، قاضی کی عدالت میں دعوئی پیش کرنے کے بعد اس بات پر بعینہ پیش کرے گا کہ غلام کا یہ عیب موکل کے پاس بھی موجود تھا۔ اگر وکیل نے بینہ پیش کر دیا تو یہ غلام موکل پر لازم ہوگا۔ یعنی وکیل اس غلام کو متوکل کی طرف واپس کر دے گا ۔ اور اگر وکیل بینہ پیش نہ کر سکا تو موکل سے قسم لی جائے گی ۔ اگر مؤکل نے قسم کھانے سے انکار کر دیا تو بھی غلام متوکل کی طرف واپس کر دیا جائے گا۔ اس نے بر خلاف اگر وکیل نے عیب کا اقرار کیا اور بغیر قضائے قاضی محض وکیل کے اقرار کی وجہ سے غلام وکیل کی طرف واپس کر دیا . گیا۔ اور عیب ایسا ہے جس کے مثل پیدا ہو سکتا ہے تو اس صورت میں وکیل کو اپنے بائع یعنی اپنے موکل سے مخاصمہ کرنے کا اختیار بھی نہ ہو گا۔ کیونکہ بغیر قضائے قاضی کے محض وکیل کے اقرار کی وجہ سے غلام کی وکیل کی طرف واپسی وکیل اور مشتری کے حق میں اگر چہ تنخ بیج ہے لیکن تیسرے کے حق میں بیج جدید ہے یعنی موکل کے حق میں ایسا ہے گویا مشتری نے یہ غلام ہے۔ لیکن یہ نسخ حجت قاصرہ یعنی اقرار کی وجہ سے ہے پس حجت کے قاصر ہونے کی وجہ سے غلام معین کو وکیل کی طرف واپس کرنا موکل کی طرف واپس کرنا نہیں ہو گا ۔ یعنی وکیل کی طرف سے واپس کرنے سے یہ غلام مؤکل کی موکل کے ساتھ خصومت کا مجاز ہوتا ہے۔ اور اگر غلام کے اندر ایسا عیب پایا گیا جس کے مثل پیدا نہیں ہو سکتا ہے اور مشتری نے غلام وکیل کی طرف محض اسکے اقرار سے بغیر قضائے قاضی کے واپس کیا تو مبسوط کے کتاب اس کی دلیل سابق میں گذر چکی ہے کہ اقرار کی وجہ سے بغیر قضاء کے غلام کی واپسی وکیل اور مشتری کے حق میں اگر چہ مسخ بیج ہے لیکن ان کے علاوہ کے حق میں بیج جدید ہے۔ اور موکل ان دونوں کا غیر ہے۔ پس ان دونوں کے درمیان منعقدہ بیج ان کے غیر یعنی موکل پر کیوں لازم ہوگی یعنی موکل پر یہ غلام لازم نہ ہوگا۔
صاحب ہدایہ نے لان الرد متعین کا جواب دیتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ آپ کا یہ کہنا کہ غلام کا ر داور واپس کیا جانا متعین ہے۔ غلط ہے۔ اسلئے کہ مشتری کا حق اولا وصف سلام میں ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ یعنی مشتری صحیح سالم بیع کا مستحق ہوتا ہے۔ لیکن جب مبیع صحیح سالم نہ ہو بلکہ امیں عیب ہو تو اسکا حق مبیع کو واپس کرنے کی طرف منتقل ہو جاتا ہے۔ یعنی مشتری کیلئے مبیع واپس کرنے کا حق ثابت ہو جاتا ہے۔لیکن اگر سابق عیب کے علاوہ مبیع کے اندر مشتری کے پاس نیا عیب بھی پیدا ہو گیا یا سابقہ عیب میں اضافہ ہو گیا تو اس صورت میں مشتری کیلئے مبیع واپس کرنے کا حق نہیں ہوتا۔ بلکہ مشتری اپنے نقصان کے بقدر ثمن واپس لے سکتا ہے۔ یعنی جو عیب بائع کے پاس پیدا ہوا تھا۔ اس کی وجہ سے غلام کی قیمت میں جو کمی واقع ہو گی۔ مشتری اس مقدار کو بائع سے لینے کا مجاز ہو گا۔ بہر حال یہ بات ثابت ہو گئی کہ عیب کی وجہ سے مبیع واپس کرنا متعین نہیں ہے اور جب واپس کرنا متعین نہیں ہے تو آپ کی بیان کردہ دلیل لان الرد متعین بھی درست نہ ہوگی ۔
صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ اس مسئلہ کو کفایہ میں اس سے زیادہ تفصیل کے ساتھ بیان کیا ہے۔
Book of Agency: The return (radd) is a sale (fath). Due to the general authority of the qadi, but because the proof is limited (hujjat qasirah) i.e. the acknowledgment (iqrar) is a rescission (faskh), it is permissible for the agent to litigate with the principal, and because the proof is limited, this return will not be binding on the principal except through proof. And if the defect is of a type that cannot originate (like it) and the return occurs by the agent's acknowledgment without the qadi's order, then in one narration the return without litigation will not be binding on the principal because the return is determined (muta'ayyan). And in the general narrations, the agent does not have the right to litigate with the principal due to the proof we mentioned. And the right (of the buyer) is first in the attribute of soundness, then it transfers to the return. Then it transfers to recourse for the reduction in price. Thus the return is not determined. And we have mentioned this with greater detail in al-Kifayah.

Explanation of the case scenario: If the agent acknowledges a defect in the slave sold, and due to that acknowledgment by the qadi's judgment the buyer returns the defective slave to the agent, then this slave becomes binding on the agent, i.e. this return of the slave is counted against the agent, not against the principal. The proof is that acknowledgment is a limited proof (hujjat qasirah). Therefore its effect appears in favor of the one who acknowledges, and does not appear in favor of anyone else. That is, due to the acknowledgment, the return of the slave is to the one who acknowledged (the agent), not to the principal. And the agent was not compelled to acknowledge, because it was possible for him to remain silent, and in case of demand for oath, it was possible for him to refuse the oath. So if he did not acknowledge but remained silent or refused to take the oath upon demand, the judgment would be based on silence or refusal to swear, not on acknowledgment. In any case, the agent was not compelled to acknowledge the defect; rather he had a choice. And when the agent was not compelled to acknowledge the defect, then it will only affect his own right, i.e. the return of the defective slave is to him, and his acknowledgment will not be binding on the principal, i.e. this return will not be binding on the principal. However, the agent has full authority to litigate with his principal, i.e. the agent, after filing a claim in the qadi's court, will present exactly that this defect in the slave was also present with the principal. If the agent presents evidence (bayyinah), then this slave becomes binding on the principal, i.e. the agent will return the slave to the principal. And if the agent cannot present evidence, then an oath will be demanded from the principal. If the principal refuses to take the oath, then also the slave will be returned to the principal. On the contrary, if the agent acknowledges the defect and without the qadi's judgment, merely by the agent's acknowledgment, the slave is returned to the agent, and the defect is of a type that can originate (like it), then in this case the agent will not have the authority to litigate with his seller i.e. his principal. Because without the qadi's judgment, merely by the agent's acknowledgment, the return of the slave to the agent, although it is a dissolution (naksh) of the sale between the agent and the buyer, but in the right of a third party it is a new sale, i.e. in the right of the principal it is as if the buyer sold this slave to the agent. So the agent has no right to litigate with his principal concerning this slave. And returning the defective slave to the agent by the qadi's judgment is a dissolution (faskh) because the qadi has general authority (wilayah 'ammah). But this is due to the limited proof i.e. the acknowledgment. So because the proof is limited, returning the specific slave to the agent is not a return to the principal, i.e. returning from the agent's side does not make this slave return to the principal, unless the agent presents evidence or the principal refuses the oath. And since this return is a dissolution (naksh) of sale, the agent has full right to litigate with his principal, because in the case of dissolution of sale, the agent is authorized to litigate with his principal. And if in the slave there is found a defect whose like cannot originate, and the buyer returns the slave to the agent merely by his acknowledgment without the qadi's judgment, then according to one narration from al-Mabsut in the Book of Sales, this return will be binding on the principal without litigation, i.e. by the buyer returning the defective slave to the agent, it becomes a return to the principal, and the agent will not need litigation etc. Because when the defect is such that its like cannot originate in the buyer's possession, then due to this defect, the return of the slave is determined (muta'ayyan), i.e. the agent and the buyer have done exactly what the qadi would do. That is, if the agent and the buyer were to litigate before the qadi about such a defect whose like cannot originate, the qadi would return the slave to the agent, and under that judgment the return would be to the principal, and the agent would not have to bear the burden of litigation. In any case, when the agent and the buyer have done the same thing that the qadi does, then just as the qadi's return of the slave to the agent results in return to the principal, similarly, without qadi's judgment, merely by the agent's acknowledgment, the slave being returned to the agent will result in return to the principal. The agent will not need litigation to return to the principal. And in the general narrations of al-Mabsut, it is that in this case the slave returns only to the agent and does not return to the principal, and the agent also does not have the right to litigate with his principal, i.e. this return is binding on the agent. The agent will return the compensation to the buyer, the agent will be the owner of this slave, and the agent will not have the right to bring a claim in the qadi's court to return the slave to his principal.

The proof for this has already passed: that because of the acknowledgment, without qadi's judgment, the return of the slave, although it is a dissolution (naksh) of the sale between the agent and the buyer, but for others it is a new sale. And the principal is other than these two. So how can a sale concluded between these two be binding on their other i.e. the principal? That is, this slave will not be binding on the principal.

The author of al-Hidayah, responding to the argument 'because the return is determined', said: Your statement that the return/redemption of the slave is determined is incorrect. Because the buyer's right is first established in the attribute of soundness (wasf salamah). That is, the buyer is entitled to a healthy, sound sale. But when the sold item is not healthy and sound but contains a defect, his right transfers to returning the sold item. That is, the buyer's right to return the sold item is established. However, if besides the prior defect, a new defect appears in the sold item in the buyer's possession, or the prior defect increased, then in this case the buyer does not have the right to return the sold item. Rather, the buyer can take back the amount of his loss from the price. That is, the decrease in value of the slave due to the defect that originated with the seller, the buyer is authorized to take that amount from the seller. In any case, it is established that returning the sold item due to a defect is not determined (muta'ayyan). And when the return is not determined, then your mentioned proof 'because the return is determined' is also incorrect.

The author of al-Hidayah says that this issue is explained in greater detail in al-Kifayah.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the effect of an agent's (wakil) acknowledgment (iqrar) of a defect in a sold slave, and whether the return (radd) of the slave binds the agent or the principal (muwakkil). It is taken from the commentary on al-Hidayah by the author of Ashraf al-Hidayah. The author first presents the general rule: when the qadi orders the return based on the agent's acknowledgment, the slave returns to the agent, not the principal, because iqrar is a limited proof (hujjat qasirah) that only affects the one who acknowledges. The agent is not compelled to acknowledge; he could remain silent or refuse the oath. Therefore his acknowledgment only binds himself. However, the agent can then litigate with the principal to prove that the defect existed before sale, and if successful (by evidence or principal's refusal of oath), the slave is returned to the principal. The author then discusses two exceptional scenarios: (1) If the defect is of a type that can originate (e.g., a new defect could appear in the buyer's possession), and the agent acknowledges without qadi's judgment, then the return only affects the agent, and he cannot litigate with the principal because the transaction is considered a new sale between agent and buyer. (2) If the defect is of a type that cannot originate (e.g., a congenital defect that could not have occurred in the buyer's possession), then according to one narration from al-Mabsut, the return by the agent's acknowledgment alone suffices to return the slave to the principal, because the defect determines the return. However, the author of al-Hidayah rejects the argument of determination, explaining that the buyer's right is first to a sound item, then to return or to claim reduction in price. If a new defect appears, the buyer cannot return but can only claim reduction. Therefore return is not determined; it depends on conditions. The author concludes that the issue is elaborated further in al-Kifayah.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment or admission of a fact, here specifically the agent's admission that the slave had a defect before sale.
حجة قاصرة (hujjat qasirah): A proof that is limited in its effect, i.e., it only binds the person who produces it and does not bind others. The agent's iqrar is hujjat qasirah, so it only binds him.
رد (radd): The return of the sold item (mabi') to the seller due to a defect.
نسخ (naksh): Dissolution of a sale, here used to describe the return without qadi's judgment as a new sale between agent and buyer concerning third parties.
فسخ (faskh): Judicial rescission or annulment of a contract, here the return ordered by the qadi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the general Hanafi ruling in the passage, what is the effect when the buyer returns a defective slave to the agent based on the agent's acknowledgment, but without any involvement of a qadi, and the defect is of a type that could have appeared after the sale?
A) The slave is returned to the principal, and the agent can litigate.
B) The slave is returned to the agent, and the agent can litigate.
C) The slave is returned to the agent, and the agent cannot litigate.
D) The slave remains with the buyer.

Key Takeaway
An agent's acknowledgment of a defect (iqrar) is a limited proof (hujjat qasirah) that binds only the agent; the principal is not liable unless the agent proves the defect through litigation or a qadi's order.

Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf: Non-Replicable Defect and the Determination Argument
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on non-replicable defect and determination

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on whether a non-replicable defect makes the return of a sold slave determined, and apply the tarjih of al-Hidayah that rejects this view.

Core Idea
Return is not determined because the buyer's right shifts from soundness to return to reduction.

This lesson focuses on a specific intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a non-replicable defect (e.g., a congenital flaw that could not have occurred in the buyer's possession). One riwaya from al-Mabsut holds that the return is determined (muta'ayyan) and therefore binds the principal directly without litigation. The author of al-Hidayah refutes this, explaining that the buyer's right is not static; it can transfer to a reduction in price if a new defect appears. Therefore, the return is not determined, and the general rule (iqrar binds only the agent) applies even in this case.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue
The dispute is about whether, when a non-replicable defect exists and the buyer returns the slave based solely on the agent's acknowledgment without a qadi's order, the return binds the principal directly or only the agent.
The ikhtilaf is within the Hanafi school: one riwaya vs. the general narrations.
2
State the conflicting positions
Position A (exceptional riwaya from Mabsut): The return is determined (muta'ayyan) because the defect could not have originated with the buyer, so the agent and buyer act as if they were the qadi. The return binds the principal without litigation. Position B (general narrations): The return only binds the agent, and the agent cannot litigate with the principal.
3
Analyze the dalil for each position
The exceptional riwaya argues that since the defect cannot arise in the buyer's possession, its existence before sale is certain, making the return determined. The general narrations rely on the principle that iqrar is hujjat qasirah, and without qadi's judgment, the return is a new sale between agent and buyer.
The general narrations' dalil is the hujjat qasirah principle.
4
Examine the Hanafi response (tarjih)
The author of al-Hidayah refutes the determination argument by explaining the buyer's right progression: first to soundness, then to return, then to reduction. If a new defect appears, the right shifts to reduction, showing return is not absolute. Therefore, the determination argument fails, and the general view is correct.
This refutation is based on the nature of the buyer's rights under the contract of sale.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under the exceptional view, the agent avoids litigation and the principal is directly liable. Under the general view, the agent bears the loss initially and must litigate to recover. The mufta bihi is the general view, so in practice, the agent must litigate.

صاحب ہدایہ نے لان الرد متعین کا جواب دیتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ آپ کا یہ کہنا کہ غلام کا ر داور واپس کیا جانا متعین ہے۔ غلط ہے۔ اسلئے کہ مشتری کا حق اولا وصف سلام میں ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ یعنی مشتری صحیح سالم بیع کا مستحق ہوتا ہے۔ لیکن جب مبیع صحیح سالم نہ ہو بلکہ امیں عیب ہو تو اسکا حق مبیع کو واپس کرنے کی طرف منتقل ہو جاتا ہے۔ یعنی مشتری کیلئے مبیع واپس کرنے کا حق ثابت ہو جاتا ہے۔لیکن اگر سابق عیب کے علاوہ مبیع کے اندر مشتری کے پاس نیا عیب بھی پیدا ہو گیا یا سابقہ عیب میں اضافہ ہو گیا تو اس صورت میں مشتری کیلئے مبیع واپس کرنے کا حق نہیں ہوتا۔ بلکہ مشتری اپنے نقصان کے بقدر ثمن واپس لے سکتا ہے۔ یعنی جو عیب بائع کے پاس پیدا ہوا تھا۔ اس کی وجہ سے غلام کی قیمت میں جو کمی واقع ہو گی۔ مشتری اس مقدار کو بائع سے لینے کا مجاز ہو گا۔ بہر حال یہ بات ثابت ہو گئی کہ عیب کی وجہ سے مبیع واپس کرنا متعین نہیں ہے اور جب واپس کرنا متعین نہیں ہے تو آپ کی بیان کردہ دلیل لان الرد متعین بھی درست نہ ہوگی ۔
صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ اس مسئلہ کو کفایہ میں اس سے زیادہ تفصیل کے ساتھ بیان کیا ہے۔
Book of Agency: The return (radd) is a sale (fath). Due to the general authority of the qadi, but because the proof is limited (hujjat qasirah) i.e. the acknowledgment (iqrar) is a rescission (faskh), it is permissible for the agent to litigate with the principal, and because the proof is limited, this return will not be binding on the principal except through proof. And if the defect is of a type that cannot originate (like it) and the return occurs by the agent's acknowledgment without the qadi's order, then in one narration the return without litigation will not be binding on the principal because the return is determined (muta'ayyan). And in the general narrations, the agent does not have the right to litigate with the principal due to the proof we mentioned. And the right (of the buyer) is first in the attribute of soundness, then it transfers to the return. Then it transfers to recourse for the reduction in price. Thus the return is not determined. And we have mentioned this with greater detail in al-Kifayah.

Explanation of the case scenario: If the agent acknowledges a defect in the slave sold, and due to that acknowledgment by the qadi's judgment the buyer returns the defective slave to the agent, then this slave becomes binding on the agent, i.e. this return of the slave is counted against the agent, not against the principal. The proof is that acknowledgment is a limited proof (hujjat qasirah). Therefore its effect appears in favor of the one who acknowledges, and does not appear in favor of anyone else. That is, due to the acknowledgment, the return of the slave is to the one who acknowledged (the agent), not to the principal. And the agent was not compelled to acknowledge, because it was possible for him to remain silent, and in case of demand for oath, it was possible for him to refuse the oath. So if he did not acknowledge but remained silent or refused to take the oath upon demand, the judgment would be based on silence or refusal to swear, not on acknowledgment. In any case, the agent was not compelled to acknowledge the defect; rather he had a choice. And when the agent was not compelled to acknowledge the defect, then it will only affect his own right, i.e. the return of the defective slave is to him, and his acknowledgment will not be binding on the principal, i.e. this return will not be binding on the principal. However, the agent has full authority to litigate with his principal, i.e. the agent, after filing a claim in the qadi's court, will present exactly that this defect in the slave was also present with the principal. If the agent presents evidence (bayyinah), then this slave becomes binding on the principal, i.e. the agent will return the slave to the principal. And if the agent cannot present evidence, then an oath will be demanded from the principal. If the principal refuses to take the oath, then also the slave will be returned to the principal. On the contrary, if the agent acknowledges the defect and without the qadi's judgment, merely by the agent's acknowledgment, the slave is returned to the agent, and the defect is of a type that can originate (like it), then in this case the agent will not have the authority to litigate with his seller i.e. his principal. Because without the qadi's judgment, merely by the agent's acknowledgment, the return of the slave to the agent, although it is a dissolution (naksh) of the sale between the agent and the buyer, but in the right of a third party it is a new sale, i.e. in the right of the principal it is as if the buyer sold this slave to the agent. So the agent has no right to litigate with his principal concerning this slave. And returning the defective slave to the agent by the qadi's judgment is a dissolution (faskh) because the qadi has general authority (wilayah 'ammah). But this is due to the limited proof i.e. the acknowledgment. So because the proof is limited, returning the specific slave to the agent is not a return to the principal, i.e. returning from the agent's side does not make this slave return to the principal, unless the agent presents evidence or the principal refuses the oath. And since this return is a dissolution (naksh) of sale, the agent has full right to litigate with his principal, because in the case of dissolution of sale, the agent is authorized to litigate with his principal. And if in the slave there is found a defect whose like cannot originate, and the buyer returns the slave to the agent merely by his acknowledgment without the qadi's judgment, then according to one narration from al-Mabsut in the Book of Sales, this return will be binding on the principal without litigation, i.e. by the buyer returning the defective slave to the agent, it becomes a return to the principal, and the agent will not need litigation etc. Because when the defect is such that its like cannot originate in the buyer's possession, then due to this defect, the return of the slave is determined (muta'ayyan), i.e. the agent and the buyer have done exactly what the qadi would do. That is, if the agent and the buyer were to litigate before the qadi about such a defect whose like cannot originate, the qadi would return the slave to the agent, and under that judgment the return would be to the principal, and the agent would not have to bear the burden of litigation. In any case, when the agent and the buyer have done the same thing that the qadi does, then just as the qadi's return of the slave to the agent results in return to the principal, similarly, without qadi's judgment, merely by the agent's acknowledgment, the slave being returned to the agent will result in return to the principal. The agent will not need litigation to return to the principal. And in the general narrations of al-Mabsut, it is that in this case the slave returns only to the agent and does not return to the principal, and the agent also does not have the right to litigate with his principal, i.e. this return is binding on the agent. The agent will return the compensation to the buyer, the agent will be the owner of this slave, and the agent will not have the right to bring a claim in the qadi's court to return the slave to his principal.

The proof for this has already passed: that because of the acknowledgment, without qadi's judgment, the return of the slave, although it is a dissolution (naksh) of the sale between the agent and the buyer, but for others it is a new sale. And the principal is other than these two. So how can a sale concluded between these two be binding on their other i.e. the principal? That is, this slave will not be binding on the principal.

The author of al-Hidayah, responding to the argument 'because the return is determined', said: Your statement that the return/redemption of the slave is determined is incorrect. Because the buyer's right is first established in the attribute of soundness (wasf salamah). That is, the buyer is entitled to a healthy, sound sale. But when the sold item is not healthy and sound but contains a defect, his right transfers to returning the sold item. That is, the buyer's right to return the sold item is established. However, if besides the prior defect, a new defect appears in the sold item in the buyer's possession, or the prior defect increased, then in this case the buyer does not have the right to return the sold item. Rather, the buyer can take back the amount of his loss from the price. That is, the decrease in value of the slave due to the defect that originated with the seller, the buyer is authorized to take that amount from the seller. In any case, it is established that returning the sold item due to a defect is not determined (muta'ayyan). And when the return is not determined, then your mentioned proof 'because the return is determined' is also incorrect.

The author of al-Hidayah says that this issue is explained in greater detail in al-Kifayah.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the effect of an agent's (wakil) acknowledgment (iqrar) of a defect in a sold slave, and whether the return (radd) of the slave binds the agent or the principal (muwakkil). It is taken from the commentary on al-Hidayah by the author of Ashraf al-Hidayah. The author first presents the general rule: when the qadi orders the return based on the agent's acknowledgment, the slave returns to the agent, not the principal, because iqrar is a limited proof (hujjat qasirah) that only affects the one who acknowledges. The agent is not compelled to acknowledge; he could remain silent or refuse the oath. Therefore his acknowledgment only binds himself. However, the agent can then litigate with the principal to prove that the defect existed before sale, and if successful (by evidence or principal's refusal of oath), the slave is returned to the principal. The author then discusses two exceptional scenarios: (1) If the defect is of a type that can originate (e.g., a new defect could appear in the buyer's possession), and the agent acknowledges without qadi's judgment, then the return only affects the agent, and he cannot litigate with the principal because the transaction is considered a new sale between agent and buyer. (2) If the defect is of a type that cannot originate (e.g., a congenital defect that could not have occurred in the buyer's possession), then according to one narration from al-Mabsut, the return by the agent's acknowledgment alone suffices to return the slave to the principal, because the defect determines the return. However, the author of al-Hidayah rejects the argument of determination, explaining that the buyer's right is first to a sound item, then to return or to claim reduction in price. If a new defect appears, the buyer cannot return but can only claim reduction. Therefore return is not determined; it depends on conditions. The author concludes that the issue is elaborated further in al-Kifayah.

Key Terms
متعين (muta'ayyan): Determined or fixed; used to describe a return that is certain and absolute, requiring no further judicial intervention.
وصف السلامة (wasf al-salamah): The attribute of soundness; the buyer's primary right is to receive a fault-free item.
رجوع بالنقصان (ruju' bil-nuqsan): Recourse for the reduction in price; the buyer's fallback right when return is not possible due to a new defect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Hidayah, why is the return of a slave with a non-replicable defect not considered determined (muta'ayyan)?
A) Because the agent's acknowledgment is always limited to himself.
B) Because the buyer's right can shift to a reduction in price if a new defect appears.
C) Because the defect could still have originated after the sale.
D) Because the qadi's involvement is always required for any return.

Key Takeaway
Even with a non-replicable defect, the return based solely on the agent's iqrar is not determined; the general rule (iqrar binds only the agent) applies, as per the tarjih of al-Hidayah.
